This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Catherine_Britt","to":"Catherine Britt"}],"pages":{"7611435":{"pageid":7611435,"ns":0,"title":"Catherine Britt","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|Australian country music artist|bot=PearBOT 5}}\n{{BLP sources|date=February 2024}}\n{{Use dmy dates|date=March 2020}}\n{{Use Australian English|date=June 2011}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Catherine Britt\n| image           = Catherine Britt.jpg\n| landscape       = <!-- Set as \"yes\" if image used is relatively wide compared to its height, otherwise leave blank -->\n| image_size      =\n| alt             =\n| caption         = Britt at radio station [[2ARM]] FM92.1, [[Armidale, New South Wales|Armidale]]. Photo by Bruce Howlett.\n| birth_name      = Catherine Elisabeth Britt\n| alias           =\n| birth_date      = {{birth date and age|df=y|1984|12|31}}\n| birth_place     = [[Newcastle, New South Wales]], Australia\n| origin          =\n| death_date      = <!-- {{death date and age|df=y|YYYY|MM|DD|YYYY|MM|DD}}, where first date = death and second = birth -->\n| death_place     =\n| genre           = [[Country music|Country]]\n| occupation      = Musician\n| instrument      = [[Singing|Vocals]], [[rhythm guitar]]\n| years_active    = 1996\u2013present\n| label           = [[ABC Commercial|ABC]], [[RCA Records Nashville|RCA Nashville]]\n| website         = {{URL|catherinebritt.com}}\n}}\n\n'''Catherine Elisabeth Britt''' (born 31 December 1984) is an Australian [[country music]] artist who has had success in both her native Australia and in the United States. She started her career in [[Newcastle, New South Wales|Newcastle]] in 1999, she moved to [[Nashville, Tennessee|Nashville]] from 2002 to 2008 and then returned to Australia. Britt has had three singles in top&nbsp;40 on the US ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Country Songs]] charts with \"The Upside of Being Down\", her highest, peaking at No.&nbsp;36 in 2004. Britt has released seven studio albums in Australia, where all seven have appeared on the [[ARIA Charts|ARIA Albums Chart]], ''[[Too Far Gone (Catherine Britt album)|Too Far Gone]]'' (16 January 2006), ''Little Wildflower'' (14 January 2008), ''Catherine Britt'' (28 May 2010) and ''[[Always Never Enough]]'' (10 August 2012). All five albums have been nominated for [[ARIA Music Awards]] in the category, [[ARIA Award for Best Country Album|Best Country Album]].\n\nAt the [[Country Music Awards of Australia]] Britt has won four [[Golden Guitar]] trophies, Female Artist of the Year for \"What I Did Last Night\" (2009), \"Charlestown Road\" (2013) and \"Boneshaker\" (2016), and Single of the Year for \"Sweet Emmylou\" (2011). Britt married her then-partner, James Beverley, in October 2013; the couple have two children. Britt was diagnosed with breast cancer in early 2015; she underwent surgery and chemotherapy.\n\n== Biography ==\nCatherine Elisabeth Britt was born on 31 December 1984 in [[Newcastle, New South Wales|Newcastle]].<ref name=\"Dicaire\"/> Her father, Steve Britt, is a school counsellor and her mother, Anne, is a teacher-librarian; they have three older sons.<ref name=\"Morris\">{{cite web | url = http://www.tamworthragepage.com/britt.htm | title = Catherine Britt | publisher = Tamworth Rage Page (Helen Morris) | last = Morris | first = Helen | access-date = 14 January 2015 | year = 2004 }}</ref> Steve has a vast collection of records, especially material by country music artists.<ref name=\"Morris\"/> From the age of ten Britt was singing in her home drawing inspiration from Dolly Parton, Loretta Lynn and Hank Williams.<ref name=\"2008 Bio\"/> Britt was a reluctant music student, \"I got singing lessons for a while and hated it ... I hate people telling me what to do with my music and stuff. They used to tell me to sing all this Natalie Imbruglia stuff so I quit them. I had guitar lessons from the same guy and he taught me the basic chords and I gave that up once I knew all the basic chords, thinking that will do me.\"<ref name=\"Morris\"/>\n\nHer first effort at song writing, \"Guardian Angel\", occurred when she was 11, she later recalled, \"it was pretty bad\".<ref name=\"Morris\"/> In the following year her parents took her to meet Australian country musician, Bill Chambers, who invited Britt on stage to duet on \"T. B. Blues\", a cover version of [[Jimmie Rodgers (country singer)|Jimmie Rodgers]]' original.<ref name=\"Dicaire\">{{cite book | chapter-url = https://books.google.com/books?id=ce2IuErOokkC&q=%22that+don%27t+bother+me%22+kasey+chambers&pg=PA235 | chapter = Part Five: Contemporary Country | last = Dicaire | first = David | title = The New Generation of Country Music Stars: Biographies of 50 Artists Born After 1940 | pages = 234\u2013237 | date = 18 August 2008 | publisher = McFarland | isbn = 978-0-78648-559-8 }}</ref><ref name=\"2008 Bio\"/> A week later Britt sang solo at a Merle Haggard tribute concert in Sydney presented by Chambers.<ref name=\"2008 Bio\"/>\n\nIn 1999 Britt independently released her debut four-track extended play, ''In the Pines'', which was produced by Chambers \u2013 she was aged 14.<ref name=\"2008 Bio\">{{cite web | archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20080719164134/http://www.theresmoretocountry.com/catherinebritt.htm | url = http://www.theresmoretocountry.com/catherinebritt.htm | title = Catherine Britt \u2013 ''There's More to Country'' | publisher = [[ABC Commercial|ABC Music]] ([[Australian Broadcasting Corporation]] (ABC)) | archive-date = 19 July 2008 | access-date = 14 January 2015 }}</ref><ref name=\"Leggett\">{{cite web | url = http://www.allmusic.com/artist/catherine-britt-mn0000102335/biography | title = Catherine Britt | last = Leggett | first = Steve | publisher = [[AllMusic]] | access-date = 14 January 2015 }}</ref> It included the track, \"That Don't Bother Me!\",<ref name=\"Dicaire\"/> co-written with Chambers' daughter, [[Kasey Chambers|Kasey]]<ref name=\"APRA That\">{{cite web | publisher = [[Australasian Performing Right Association]] (APRA) | title = 'That Don't Bother Me' at APRA search engine | url = https://www.apra.com.au/cms/worksearch/worksearch.srvlt?action=workSearch#That%20Cont%20Bother%20Me | access-date = 14 January 2015 | archive-date = 17 November 2015 | archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20151117020448/https://www.apra.com.au/cms/worksearch/worksearch.srvlt?action=workSearch#That%20Cont%20Bother%20Me | url-status = dead }} Note: User may have to click 'Search again' and provide details at 'Enter a title:' e.g That Dont Bother Me; or at 'Performer:' Catherine Britt</ref> \u2013 who also provided backing vocals.<ref name=\"Adsett\">{{cite web | url = http://www.countrymusic.com.au/cmstore/Reviews/revfrm.htm#Dusty%20Smiles | title = Latest Reviews \u2013 ''Dusty Smiles and Heartbreak Cures'' | last = Adsett | first = Ron | work = Capital News | date = October\u2013November 2001 | publisher = Country Music (Ron and Rosie Adsett) | access-date = 14 January 2014 | archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20140204041733/http://countrymusic.com.au/cmstore/Reviews/revfrm.htm#Dusty%20Smiles | archive-date = 4 February 2014 | url-status = dead }}</ref> Britt preferred to write on her own, however, she enjoyed working with Kasey \"because we were such great friends, and we knew each other and we knew we both were coming from the same place when it came to music.\"<ref name=\"Kruger\">{{cite web | url = http://www.debbiekruger.com/writer/aprap/tamworth2003.html | title = Songwriters in Tamworth \u2013 Old and New Souls in Country Music | last = Kruger | first = Debbie | author-link = Debbie Kruger | work = APRAP | date = March 2003 | publisher = Australasian Performing Right Association (APRA). Debbie Kruger | access-date = 14 January 2015 }}</ref>\n\nBritt issued her first studio album, ''Dusty Smiles and Heartbreak Cures'', on 16 May 2001, also independently and produced by Bill Chambers.<ref name=\"Dicaire\"/><ref name=\"Leggett\"/><ref name=\"Adsett\"/> It contained \"a half-dozen originals, as well as covers of [Williams] and [Haggard]\".<ref name=\"Dicaire\"/> She then signed to [[ABC Commercial|ABC Music]]/ABC Country to re-release the album on 11 March 2002.<ref name=\"AUS Country\"/> In May Elton John, who was touring Australia, heard her album; he met Britt and recommended her to industry contacts in the United States.<ref name=\"2008 Bio\"/><ref name=\"US Charts\"/> ''Dusty Smiles and Heartbreak Cures'' appeared on the [[ARIA Charts|ARIA Country Chart]] in July that year, peaking at No.&nbsp;18.<ref name=\"AUS Country\"/> At the [[ARIA Music Awards of 2002]] Britt received her first nomination for [[ARIA Award for Best Country Album|Country Album of the Year]].<ref name=\"ARIA Awards List\">ARIA Music Awards for Catherine Britt:\n* Search Results 'Catherine Britt': {{cite web\n |url=http://www.ariaawards.com.au/history/search/?view=list&text=Catherine%20Britt \n |title=Search Results for 'Catherine Britt' \n |publisher=Australian Recording Industry Association (ARIA) \n |access-date=14 January 2015 \n}}\n* 2002 winners and nominees: {{cite web\n |url=http://www.ariaawards.com.au/history/year/2002?view=list \n |title=Winners By Year 2002 \n |publisher=Australian Recording Industry Association (ARIA) \n |access-date=14 January 2015 \n}}\n* 2006 winners and nominees: {{cite web\n |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20071212125336/http://www.ariaawards.com.au/history-by-year.php?year=2006 \n |url=http://www.ariaawards.com.au/history/year/2006?view=list \n |title=Winners By Year 2006 \n |publisher=Australian Recording Industry Association (ARIA) \n |archive-date=12 December 2007 \n |access-date=14 January 2015 \n |url-status=dead \n}}\n* 2008 winners and nominees: {{cite web\n |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090813152819/http://www.ariaawards.com.au/history-by-year.php?year=2008 \n |url=http://www.ariaawards.com.au/history/year/2008?view=list \n |title=Winners By Year 2008 \n |publisher=Australian Recording Industry Association (ARIA) \n |archive-date=13 August 2009 \n |access-date=14 January 2015 \n |url-status=dead \n}}\n* 2010 winners and nominees: {{cite web\n |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120421080110/http://www.ariaawards.com.au/history/year/2010 \n |url=http://www.ariaawards.com.au/history/year/2010?view=list \n |title=Winners by Year 2010 \n |publisher=Australian Recording Industry Association (ARIA) \n |archive-date=21 April 2012 \n |access-date=14 January 2015 \n |url-status=dead \n}}\n* 2012 winners and nominees: {{cite web\n |url=http://www.ariaawards.com.au/history/year/2012?view=list \n |title=Winners By Year 2012 \n |publisher=Australian Recording Industry Association (ARIA) \n |access-date=14 January 2015 \n}}\n</ref> Late in 2002 Britt, for three weeks, supported the Australian leg of a tour by [[Chris Isaak]].<ref name=\"Lobley\">{{cite news | url = http://www.smh.com.au/articles/2002/12/19/1040174347827.html | title = True Britt | last = Lobley | first = Katrina | work = [[Sydney Morning Herald]] | publisher = [[Fairfax Media]] | access-date = 14 January 2015 }}</ref><ref name=\"Isaak\">{{cite web | url = http://catalogue.nla.gov.au/Record/5811712 | title = Chris Isaak &#91;picture&#93;: with special guest Catherine Britt: Burswood Theatre, Monday 25th November | publisher = National Library of Australia | access-date = 14 January 2015 }}</ref> Her backing band included Kurt Bailey on drums and Ben Conicella on bass guitar.<ref name=\"Lobley\"/>\n\nBritt attended the [[Country Music Awards of Australia]], held in Tamworth, in January 2003 and told [[Debbie Kruger]] of [[Australasian Performing Right Association]] (APRA) of her writing process for the album, \"The way I write songs is a bit strange ... I just sit down and it'll be five minutes, and the song will just come out on paper, and then I'll have to look back on it and go, 'Right, does this make sense?' I hardly ever change my words, ever, I always just write them down and that's it. That real five-minute rush, I guess.\"<ref name=\"Kruger\"/> For some lyrics she would check with her parents \"I really didn't even know what it meant. And that happens a lot of the time for me, I have to go to Mum and Dad and say, 'Does this make sense?' And every time it does.\"<ref name=\"Kruger\"/> Brendan Hutchens of TV series, ''[[George Negus Tonight]]'', interviewed Britt for \"Episode 5\", broadcast on 5 March 2003.<ref name=\"Hutchens\">{{cite web | url = http://www.abc.net.au/dimensions/dimensions_people/Transcripts/s800459.htm | title = Episode 5: Catherine Britt \u2013 Country Singer: Transcript | publisher = Australian Broadcasting Corporation (ABC) | last = Hutchens | first = Brendan | work = [[George Negus Tonight]] | date = 5 March 2003| access-date = 14 January 2015 }}</ref> She described touring with Isaak \"It's been great, he's been kind to me and his whole band's really good to me, so it's better than I thought\".<ref name=\"Hutchens\"/>\n\nIn 2004, she moved to [[Nashville, Tennessee]], and was soon signed to [[RCA Records Nashville|RCA Nashville]] for international releases. Her US debut single, \"The Upside of Being Down\", peaked at No.&nbsp;36 on the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Country Songs]] in August that year.<ref name=\"US Charts\">''Billboard'' Charting:\n* Catherine Britt:&nbsp;{{cite magazine | url = http://www.billboard.com/artist/298808/catherine-britt/chart?f=357 | title = Catherine Britt \u2013 Chart History | magazine = [[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] | publisher = [[Prometheus Global Media]] | access-date = 14 January 2015 | archive-date = 24 August 2015 | archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20150824113209/http://www.billboard.com/artist/298808/catherine-britt/chart?f=357 | url-status = dead }}\n* Elton John and Catherine Britt:&nbsp;{{cite magazine | url = http://www.billboard.com/articles/news/61953/chart-beat | title = Chart Beat | first = Fred | last = Bronson | magazine = Billboard | publisher = Prometheus Global Media | date = 28 July 2005 | access-date = 14 January 2015 }}</ref> In July 2005 Britt and John released a country music duet, \"Where We Both Say Goodbye\", which was co-written by Britt with [[Jerry Salley]].<ref name=\"US Charts\"/><ref name=\"APRA Where\">{{cite web | publisher = [[Australasian Performing Right Association]] (APRA) | title = 'Where We Both Say Goodbye' at APRA search engine | url = https://www.apra.com.au/cms/worksearch/worksearch.srvlt?action=workSearch#Where%20We%20Both%20Say%20Goodbye | access-date = 14 January 2015 | archive-date = 17 November 2015 | archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20151117020448/https://www.apra.com.au/cms/worksearch/worksearch.srvlt?action=workSearch#Where%20We%20Both%20Say%20Goodbye | url-status = dead }} Note: User may have to click 'Search again' and provide details at 'Enter a title:' e.g Where We Both Say Goodbye; or at 'Performer:' Catherine Britt</ref> The single entered at No.&nbsp;49 on the Hot Country Songs \u2013 John's first appearance on that chart.<ref name=\"US Charts\"/>\n\nBritt's second album, ''[[Too Far Gone (Catherine Britt album)|Too Far Gone]]'', was released in Australia on 16 January 2006.<ref name=\"AMG Too\">{{cite web | url = http://www.allmusic.com/album/too-far-gone-mw0000452011/credits | title = ''Too Far Gone'' \u2013 Catherine Britt &#124; Credits | publisher = AllMusic | access-date = 15 January 2015 }}</ref><ref name=\"TooFar\">{{cite web | date = 16 January 2006 | title = The ARIA Report | publisher = Australian Recording Industry Association (ARIA) | issue = 828 | archive-url = https://webarchive.nla.gov.au/awa/20060119130000/http://pandora.nla.gov.au/pan/23790/20060120-0000/issue828.pdf | url = http://issue828.pdf | page = 30 | archive-date = 19 January 2006 | access-date = 15 January 2015 }}{{cbignore|bot=medic}}</ref> It had been recorded in Nashville with Chambers co-producing with [[Keith Stegall]] ([[Alan Jackson]], [[George Jones]], [[Jamie O'Neal]]).<ref name=\"2008 Bio\"/><ref name=\"AMG Too\"/><ref name=\"AMG Stegall\">{{cite web | url = http://www.allmusic.com/artist/keith-stegall-mn0000081608/credits | title = Keith Stegall &#124; Credits | publisher = AllMusic | access-date = 15 January 2015 }}</ref> Session musicians include [[Kenny Chesney]] on backing vocals, [[Stuart Duncan]] on fiddle and mandolin, Mark Fain on upright bass, [[Paul Franklin (musician)|Paul Franklin]] on steel guitar, [[Rob Ickes]] on dobro, [[Brent Mason]] on guitars (acoustic, electric), [[Dave Pomeroy]] on bass guitar, [[Hargus \"Pig\" Robbins]] on piano, [[John Wesley Ryles]] on backing vocals, Bruce Watkins on acoustic guitar and [[Glenn Worf]] on bass guitar.<ref name=\"AMG Too\"/> In Australia the album reached No.&nbsp;47 on the ARIA Albums Chart and No.&nbsp;3 on the related Country Chart.<ref name=\"AUS Country\"/><ref name=\"AUS Charts\"/> Tim Noel of comcast.net opined \"may not be strong enough to share with your friends as far as an introduction to [Britt]. There is some strong material here such as 'Swingin' Door' and 'Poor Man's Pride', but it's filled with mediocre stuff that sounds like late 90s material... I know Britt has a more rocking side that should hopefully come out in her upcoming [album].\"<ref name=\"Noel\">{{cite web | url = http://home.comcast.net/~cntryniche/britt2.htm | title = Catherine Britt review | publisher = [[Comcast Interactive Media]] ([[Comcast]]) | last = Noel | first = Tim | website = comcast.net | date = 14 June 2007 | access-date = 15 January 2015 }}</ref>\n\nAt the [[ARIA Music Awards of 2006]] Britt, with ''Too Far Gone'', received her second nomination for Country Album of the Year.<ref name=\"ARIA Awards List\"/> From May to October 2007 Britt was an opening act for a co-headlining tour of the US by Alan Jackson with [[Brooks & Dunn]].<ref name=\"Fabian\">{{cite web | url = http://countrymusic.about.com/od/tourschedules/a/AJ_BnD_07Tour.htm | title = Alan Jackson and Brooks & Dunn Tour Dates \u2013 Featuring Jake Owen and Catherine Britt | publisher = [[IAC/InterActiveCorp]] | last = Fabian | first = Shelly | website = [[About.com]] | date = May 2007 | access-date = 15 January 2015 | archive-date = 6 April 2012 | archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20120406174738/http://countrymusic.about.com/od/tourschedules/a/AJ_BnD_07Tour.htm | url-status = dead }}</ref> Britt recorded her third studio album, ''Little Wildflower'', with [[Brett Beavers]] producing ([[Dierks Bentley]]) in Nashville. It was released on 14 January 2008 in Australia, which reached No.&nbsp;6 on the ARIA Country Albums chart;<ref name=\"AUS Country\"/> it provided Britt with her third ARIA Award nomination in Best Country Album in [[ARIA Music Awards of 2008|2008]].<ref name=\"ARIA Awards List\"/>\n\nIts lead single, \"What I Did Last Night\", appeared in May 2007 and peaked at No.&nbsp;39 on the US Hot Country Songs chart.<ref name=\"US Charts\"/><ref name=\"Dawson 2\">{{cite web | url = http://www.nucountry.com.au/articles/diary/may2007/190507_urbanflood.htm | title = Dave's Diary \u2013 19/5/07 \u2013 Keith Urban, Greencards and Catherine Britt | publisher = David Dawson | last = Dawson | first = Dave | work = Nu Country | date = 19 May 2007 | access-date = 15 January 2015 }}</ref> When Brooks & Dunn toured Australia, during March 2008, they were supported by Britt.<ref name=\"Dawson 1\">{{cite web | url = http://www.nucountry.com.au/articles/diary/february2008/200208_catherinebritt.htm | title = Dave's Diary \u2013 20/2/08 \u2013 Catherine Britt | publisher = David Dawson | last = Dawson | first = Dave | work = Nu Country | date = 20 February 2008 | access-date = 15 January 2015 }}</ref> By April 2008 Britt was dropped from RCA's roster without releasing any albums in the US market.<ref name=\"MorrisE\">{{cite news | url = http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1585038/country-labels-keep-rosters-full-despite-album-sales-dip.jhtml | archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20080411032354/http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1585038/country-labels-keep-rosters-full-despite-album-sales-dip.jhtml | url-status = dead | archive-date = 11 April 2008 | title = Country Labels Keep Rosters Full Despite Album Sales Dip | last = Morris | first = Edward | work = CMT News | publisher = [[Viacom International]] | date = 8 April 2008 | access-date = 14 January 2015 }}</ref> Britt returned to live in Newcastle by 2009.<ref name=\"Morris\"/><ref name=\"JetStar Interview\">{{cite journal | url = http://www.jetstarmag.com/story/my-favourite-place-catherine-britt/2106/1/ | title = My Favourite Place: Catherine Britt | journal = [[Jetstar Magazine]] | publisher = [[Ink (company)|Ink]] | date = January 2014 | access-date = 14 January 2015 | archive-url = https://archive.today/20150118183846/http://www.jetstarmag.com/story/my-favourite-place-catherine-britt/2106/1/ | archive-date = 18 January 2015 | url-status = dead }}</ref>\n\nBritt contacted Chambers to produce her next album, ''Catherine Britt'', and he co-opted his then-son-in-law, [[Shane Nicholson (singer)|Shane Nicholson]], as co-producer.<ref name=\"Dawson 3\"/> It was recorded at Sing Sing Studios in Melbourne.<ref name=\"Dawson 3\"/> The track, \"Call You Back Town\", which Britt co-wrote with [[Ashley Monroe]], relates to her experiences in Nashville; Britt recalled \"[it] can be a very harsh place at times, wonderful place too ... I saw both sides of it. This song was a result of seeing that side at certain stages and how I felt about that. No, they never call you back \u2013 you call and leave a message and they never get back to you.\"<ref name=\"Dawson 3\">{{cite web | url = http://www.nucountry.com.au/articles/diary/may2010/020510_catherine_britt.htm | title = Dave's Diary \u2013 2/5/10 \u2013 Catherine Britt Interview | publisher = David Dawson | last = Dawson | first = Dave | work = Nu Country | date = 2 May 2010 | access-date = 15 January 2015 }}</ref> The album, which reached No.&nbsp;5 on the ARIA Country Albums chart,<ref name=\"AUS Country\"/> was also nominated for Best Country Album in [[ARIA Music Awards of 2010|2010]] at the ARIA Awards ceremony.<ref name=\"ARIA Awards List\"/>\n\nBritt's fifth studio album, ''[[Always Never Enough]]'', was released on 10 August 2012, which peaked at No.&nbsp;44 on the ARIA Albums Chart and No.&nbsp;3 on its Country Albums Chart.<ref name=\"AUS Country\"/><ref name=\"AUS Charts\"/> The album was recorded in [[Austin, Texas]] at Cedar Creek Studios with Britt and Chambers co-producing.<ref name=\"Ngarralinyi\">{{cite web | url = http://www.2tlp.com.au/featured17.html | title = CD Review \u2013 Featured Album of the Month | publisher = Community Indigenous Radio \u2013 Ngarralinyi \u2013 2TLP Radio \u2013 103.3 FM (Ralph Saunders) | access-date = 16 January 2015 | archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20150116164416/http://www.2tlp.com.au/featured17.html | archive-date = 16 January 2015 | url-status = dead }}</ref> Sophie Hamley of Jolene: The Country Music Blog felt it was \"her masterpiece\" with \"[n]ot a single song that I want to skip over or not pay close attention to.\"<ref name=\"Hamley\">{{cite web | url = http://jolenethecountrymusicblog.blogspot.com.au/2012/08/album-review-always-never-enough-by.html | title = Album review: ''Always Never Enough'' by Catherine Britt | publisher = Awesome Inc (Sophie Hamley) | last = Hamley | first = Sophie | work = Jolene: The Country Music Blog | date = 8 August 2010 | access-date = 16 January 2015 }}</ref> Also in [[ARIA Music Awards of 2012|2012]] Britt received her fifth nomination for Best Country Album at the ARIA Awards ceremony.<ref name=\"ARIA Awards List\"/>\n\nIn November 2012 Britt, Chambers and [[Tim Rogers (musician)|Tim Rogers]] (of [[You Am I]]) formed a group, The Hillbilly Killers, as a side project to perform \"[s]ad songs, high and lonesome songs, songs with an ache and a hurt undeniable, timeless even. But [Chambers] wanted those songs to have an edge too. Something a little unhinged. Something dark and unruly.\"<ref name=\"Swift\">{{cite news | url = https://rhythms.com.au/interviews/the-hillbilly-killers-set-to-release-debut-record/ | title = The Hillbilly Killers Set to Release Debut Record | publisher = Martin and Verity Jones | last = Swift | first = Emma | work = Rhythms | date = August 2013 | access-date = 16 January 2015 | archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20150116120435/https://rhythms.com.au/interviews/the-hillbilly-killers-set-to-release-debut-record/ | archive-date = 16 January 2015 | url-status = dead }}</ref> Other members were James Gillard, Michael Muchow on guitar and [[Shane O'Mara (musician)|Shane O'Mara]] on guitar.<ref name=\"Condon\">{{cite web | url = http://themusic.com.au/news/all/2012/11/07/country-supergroup-the-hillbilly-killers-announce-first-gig/ | title = Country Supergroup The Hillbilly Killers Announce First Gig | publisher = Street Press Australia | last = Condon | first = Dan | work = TheMusic.com.au | date = 7 November 2012 | access-date = 16 January 2015 }}</ref> Their official debut gig was at the [[Tamworth Country Music Festival]] in January 2013.<ref name=\"Condon\"/>\n\nThe group toured Australia's east coast and issued their debut single, \"They Call Us the Hillbilly Killers\", by March that year.<ref name=\"Swift\"/> Natalie Salvo of ''The AU Review'' caught their performance at The Basement in Sydney on 24 April 2013, Britt Chambers and Rogers each had a brief solo set before the trio were joined by two more musicians,<ref name=\"Salvo\"/> Gillard on double bass and backing vocals, and Paul Novosel on drums. Salvo felt \"the now-quintet used everything from guitars to banjo, double bass, slide guitar and stomp box to create just the right mix of homespun charm, venomous love notes, down-to-earth storytelling and country hoedowns.\"<ref name=\"Salvo\">{{cite web | url = http://www.theaureview.com/sydney/the-hillbilly-killers-feat-tim-rogers-bill-chambers-catherine-britt-the-basement-sydney-24-04-2013 | title = Live Review: The Hillbilly Killers (feat. Tim Rogers, Bill Chambers & Catherine Britt) \u2013 The Basement Sydney (24.04.13) | publisher = Heath Media & the AU review | last = Salvo | first = Natalie | work = The AU Review | date = 26 April 2014 | access-date = 16 January 2015 }}</ref> Britt provides rhythm guitar and backing vocals with occasional lead vocals.<ref name=\"Tarala\">{{cite news | url = https://www.newcastleherald.com.au/story/1423026/britt-on-life-with-the-hillbilly-killers/ | title = Britt on life with The Hillbilly Killers | publisher = Fairfax Media | last = Tarala | first = Kate | work = [[The Newcastle Herald]] | date = 10 April 2013 | access-date = 16 January 2015 }}</ref>\n\nOn 18 November 2013 Britt issued her first compilation album, ''The Hillbilly Pickin' Ramblin' Girl So Far...'', on ABC Music and [[Universal Music Australia]].<ref name=\"ARIA Hillbilly\">{{cite web | date = 23 December 2013 | title = The ARIA Report | publisher = Australian Recording Industry Association (ARIA) | issue = 1238 | archive-url = https://webarchive.nla.gov.au/awa/20131123130000/http://pandora.nla.gov.au/pan/23790/20131124-0000/Issue%201238.pdf | url = http://issue%201238.pdf | page = 29 | archive-date = 23 November 2013 | access-date = 16 January 2015 }}{{cbignore|bot=medic}}</ref> The album reached No.&nbsp;20 on the ARIA Country Albums Chart.<ref name=\"AUS Country\"/> A new track, \"Who Cares\", was issued as a single. In mid-2014 Britt was featured vocalist on a single by Graham Rodger, \"Reach Out\", which appeared on his album, ''Dust and Leather''. The charity single was provided for the Trans Help Foundation, which highlights the well-being of truck drivers.<ref name=\"Carroll\">{{cite web | url = http://www.floreena.com/Artists-News.php | title = Artists News: Graham Rodger & Catherine Britt present their latest single 'Reach Out' | publisher = Trans Help Foundation | last = Carroll | first = Di | access-date = 16 January 2015 | archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20150116135953/http://www.floreena.com/Artists-News.php | archive-date = 16 January 2015 | url-status = dead }}</ref>\n\nIn 2021, Britt collaborated with [[Lachlan Bryan]] and formed The Pleasures. The Pleasures released their debut single \"The Beginning of the End\" in January 2022<ref>{{cite web|url= https://www.thesoundcafe.com/post/australia-s-catherine-britt-lachlan-bryan-launch-the-pleasures |title= Australia's Catherine Britt & Lachlan Bryan launch The Pleasures |website=The Sound Cafe|date= January 2022|access-date= 17 August 2023}}</ref> and album of the same name on 4 August 2023.<ref>{{cite web|url= https://www.abc.net.au/listen/programs/saturdaynightcountry/saturday-night-country/102667128 |title= A pleasurable time with The Pleasures|website=[[Australian Broadcasting Corporation]]|date= 12 August 2023| access-date= 17 August 2023}}</ref> The album debuted at number 20 on the Australian ARIA Country Albums chart.<ref>{{cite web|url= https://www.aria.com.au/charts/country-albums-chart/2023-08-14 |title= ARIA Top 40 Country Albums for week of 14 August 2023|website=[[ARIA Charts]]|date=14 August 2023|access-date= 17 August 2023}}</ref>\n\n=== Personal life ===\nBritt married long-term partner, James Beverley, in October 2013.<ref name=\"Examiner March 2016\"/> The couple had eloped to Las Vegas and kept the ceremony and details private.<ref name=\"Examiner March 2016\">{{cite web | url = https://www.examiner.com.au/story/3825038/weekender-spill/ | title = Weekender Spill | work = [[The Examiner (Tasmania)|The Examiner]] | date = 31 March 2016 | access-date = 7 September 2020 }}</ref> In May 2015 Britt was diagnosed with breast cancer.<ref name=\"Kellar\">{{cite news | url = http://www.smh.com.au/nsw/singer-catherine-britt-to-undergo-breast-cancer-surgery-20150609-ghkaik.html | title = Singer Catherine Britt to undergo breast cancer surgery | last = Kellar | first = Jim | work = [[The Sydney Morning Herald]] | date = 10 June 2015 | access-date = 24 January 2016 }}</ref> Amidst surgery and chemotherapy, her wedding re-enactment went ahead in October the same year, celebrating the couple's second anniversary.<ref name=\"Examiner March 2016\"/><ref name=\"Moran\">{{cite news | url = http://www.dailytelegraph.com.au/entertainment/sydney-confidential/family-affair-as-brave-catherine-britt-weds-love-of-her-life-james-beverley/news-story/a75347be1f1ead050aa4665eb29ffd11 | title = Family affair as brave Catherine Britt weds love of her life James Beverley | last = Moran | first = Jonathon | work = [[The Daily Telegraph (Sydney)|The Daily Telegraph]] | date = 18 October 2015 | access-date = 24 January 2016 }}</ref> Both Britt's mother, Anne Britt, and her mother-in-law, Lee Beverley, were subsequently diagnosed and treated for breast cancer.<ref name=\"Sams\">{{cite web | url = https://www.smh.com.au/entertainment/celebrity/a-trifecta-of-bad-luck-singer-catherine-britts-family-cancer-battle-20170407-gvg8h9.html | title = A trifecta of bad luck: Singer Catherine Britt's family cancer battle | last = Sams | first = Christine | work = [[The Sydney Morning Herald]] | date = 9 April 2017 | access-date = 7 September 2020 }}</ref> By September 2019 Britt and Beverley had two children.<ref name=\"Rockman\">{{cite web | url = https://www.newcastleherald.com.au/story/6397056/baby-joy-for-catherine-britt-and-husband-james/ | title = Country music star Catherine Britt has baby number two and couldn't be happier | last = Rockman | first = Lisa | work = Newcastle Herald | date = 20 September 2019 | access-date = 7 September 2020 }}</ref>\n\nIn January 2016 she won her fourth Golden Guitar at the [[Country Music Awards of Australia]], for Female Artist of the Year (\"Boneshaker\").<ref name=\"Domjen\">{{cite news | url = http://www.dailytelegraph.com.au/entertainment/sydney-confidential/golden-guitar-awards-country-singer-catherine-britt-wins-female-artist-of-the-year/news-story/fda72e77d6038a6181980316b5de204b | title = Golden Guitar Awards: Country singer Catherine Britt wins female artist of the year | last = Domjen | first = Briana | work = [[The Daily Telegraph (Sydney)|The Daily Telegraph]] | date = 23 January 2016 | access-date = 24 January 2016 }}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n===Studio albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|+ List of studio albums with Australian Independent Record Awards (commonly known informally as [[AIR Awards]]) is an annual awards night to recognise, promote and celebrate the success of Australia's Independent Music sector.\n{{awards table}}\n|-\n| [[AIR Awards of 2013|2013]]<ref name=\"13nom\">{{cite (Britt)\n|{{nom}}\n|-\n|}\n\n===ARIA Music Awards===\nThe [[ARIA Music Awards]] are a set of annual ceremonies presented by [[Australian Recording Industry Association]] (ARIA), which recognise excellence, innovation, and achievement across all genres of the [[music of Australia]]. They commenced in 1987.Catherine Britt has been nominated for [[ARIA Award for Best Country Album]] for all first six studio albums.<ref name=\"ARIA Awards List\"/><ref name=\"CountryAlbum\">ARIA Award previous winners. {{cite web|url=http://www.ariaawards.com.au/history/award/Best-Country-Album|title=ARIA Awards Best Country Album|publisher=Australian Recording Industry Association (ARIA)|access-date=9 April 2022}}</ref>\n\n{{awards table}}\n|-\n| [[ARIA Music Awards of 2002|2002]]\n| ''Dusty Smiles and Heartbreak Cures''\n| Best Country Album\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| [[ARIA Music [[Country Music Association of Australia]] (CMAA) since 1992).<ref name=\"CMAA\">{{cite web | publisher = [[Country Music Association of Australia]] (CMAA) | title = About CMAA | url = February 2005 | access-date = 15 January 2015}}</ref> Catherine Britt has won four [[Golden Guitar]] trophies, Female Artist of the Year in 2009, 2013 and 2016, and Single of the Year in 2011.<ref It commenced in 2009.<ref name=\"about\">{{cite web|url=https://www.apraamcos.com.au/about/supporting-the-industry/competitions/vanda-young-global-songwriting-competition#_89667|title=About the Vanda Young Global Song Writing Competition|website= [[APRA AMCOS]]|access-date=12 March 2021}}</ref>\n\n{{awards table}}\n|-\n| 2011<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.apraamcos.com.au/about/supporting-the-industry/competitions/vanda-young-global-songwriting-competition/past-winners|title=Past Winners|website= [[APRA AMCOS]]|access-date=13 March 2021}}</ref>\n| \"Sweet Emmylou\"\n| Vanda & Young Global Songwriting Competition\n| style=\"background:silver;\"| 2nd\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n==References==\n{{Reflist}}\n\n==External links==\n* [http://www.catherinebritt.com/ Catherine Britt official website]\n* [http://realcountry.podomatic.com/entry/2013-12-22T23_02_51-08_00 Interview with Catherine Britt] on [[Ben Sorensen's REAL Country]]\n{{Authority control}}\n\n{{DEFAULTSORT:Britt, Catherine}}\n[[Category:1984 births]]\n[[Category:Living people]]\n[[Category:Musicians from Newcastle, New South Wales]]\n[[Category:Australian country singer-songwriters]]\n[[Category:RCA Records Nashville artists]]\n[[Category:21st-century Australian singers]]\n[[Category:21st-century Australian women singers]]\n[[Category:Australian women singer-songwriters]]\n[[Category:21st-century Australian singer-songwriters]]"}]}}}}{"batchcomplete":"","warnings":{"main":{"*":"Subscribe to the mediawiki-api-announce mailing list at <https://lists.wikimedia.org/postorius/lists/mediawiki-api-announce.lists.wikimedia.org/> for notice of API deprecations and breaking changes. Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Troy_Cassar-Daley","to":"Troy Cassar-Daley"}],"pages":{"2443227":{"pageid":2443227,"ns":0,"title":"Troy Cassar-Daley","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|Australian musician}}\n{{Use Australian English|date=October 2016}}\n{{Use dmy dates|date=August 2014}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name             = Troy Cassar-Daley\n| image            = TroyCassar.jpg\n| image_size       = \n| landscape        = <!-- yes, if wide image, otherwise leave blank -->\n| alt              = \n| caption          = \n| background       = solo_singer\n| alias            = \n| birth_date       = {{birth date and age|1969|05|18|df=y}}\n| birth_place      = [[Surry Hills, New South Wales]], Australia\n| instruments      = Vocals, guitar, harmonica\n| genre            = [[Country music|Country]]\n| occupation       = Songwriter, singer, author\n| years_active     = 1990\u2013present\n| label            = [[Sony Music]], [[Liberation Music]]\n| website          = {{URL|http://www.troycassardaley.com.au/}}\n}}\n\n'''Troy Cassar-Daley''' (born 18 May 1969) is an Australian [[Australian country music|country music]] songwriter and entertainer.\n\nCassar-Daley has released thirteen studio albums, two live albums and five compilation albums over 30 years, including the platinum-selling ''[[The Great Country Songbook]]'' with [[Adam Harvey]]. Throughout this time he has received awards including five [[ARIA Music Awards]], forty [[Country Music Awards of Australia|Golden Guitar]]s,<ref name=\"CMAA2022\"/> nine [[Deadly Awards]] (Australian Indigenous Artist Awards), four [[Country Music Association of Australia]] Entertainer of the Year awards and two [[National Indigenous Music Awards]].<ref name=\"Sony2020\">{{cite web|url=https://themusicnetwork.com/troy-cassar-daley-sony-music/|title=Troy Cassar-Daley returns home to Sony Music under new global deal|website=The Music Network|date=24 June 2020|access-date=25 June 2020}}</ref><ref name=\"abc2021arias\">{{cite news|url=https://www.abc.net.au/news/2021-11-24/aria-awards-winners-genesis-owusu-the-kid-laroi/100647266|title=You could dub this year's awards the Hip Hop and R'n'B ARIAs|publisher=[[ABC News (Australia)|ABC News]]|date=24 November 2021|first=Mawunyo|last=Gbogbo|access-date=25 November 2021}}</ref>\n\n==Early life and career==\nCassar-Daley was born on 18 May 1969<ref name=\"allmusicbio\"/> in the Sydney suburb of [[Surry Hills, New South Wales|Surry Hills]] to a Maltese-Australian father and an [[Indigenous Australians|Aboriginal]] mother from the [[Gumbaynggirr]] and [[Bundjalung people|Bundjalung]] people.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.abc.net.au/tv/talkingheads/txt/s2554373.htm|title=Troy Cassar-Daley|work=[[Talking Heads (Australian TV series)|Talking Heads]]|publisher=[[Australian Broadcasting Corporation]]|date=4 May 2009|access-date=12 July 2011|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090524000641/http://www.abc.net.au/tv/talkingheads/txt/s2554373.htm|archive-date=24 May 2009}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://troycassardaley.com.au/about/|title=About|publisher=Troy Cassar-Daley|access-date=21 November 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20211121103946/https://troycassardaley.com.au/about/|archive-date=21 November 2021}}</ref> At a very young age, he moved with his mother to [[Grafton, New South Wales|Grafton]] in north-eastern [[New South Wales]]. At eleven, Troy went to the [[Tamworth Country Music Festival]] and returned the next year to busk on the streets.<ref>[http://au.yahoo.com/it-takes-two/couples/bio/troy-cassar-daley/ Troy Cassar-Daley \u2013 It Takes Two<!-- Bot generated title -->] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070704061433/http://au.yahoo.com/it-takes-two/couples/bio/troy-cassar-daley/ |date=4 July 2007 }}</ref> At 16, he and his band, Little Eagle, were touring the [[North Coast (New South Wales)|North Coast of New South Wales]] and he made the top 10 in [[Tamworth, New South Wales|Tamworth]]'s Toyota Star Maker Quest. He won the 1986 \"Search for a Star\" competition and then toured with Brian Young for seven months in which he began to develop his songwriting skills. After returning home he replaced [[James Blundell (singer)|James Blundell]] as leader of country music band The Blue Heeler Band.<ref name=\"allmusicbio\">{{cite web|url=https://www.allmusic.com/artist/troy-cassar-daley-mn0000393685/biography|title=Troy Cassar-Daley Biography|publisher=AllMusic|access-date=1 August 2020}}</ref>\n\n==Solo career==\nBy late 1993 Cassar-Daley had enough original songs for a debut EP. The first single \"Dream Out Loud\" was released on 24 October 1994<ref>{{cite web|url=http://i.imgur.com/T3ZokDY.png|title=New Release Summary \u2013 Product Available from: 24/10/94 (from The ARIA Report Issue No. 245)|publisher=Imgur.com|accessdate=19 September 2016}}</ref> by Sony Music and reached number-one on the Australian country music charts. His first album, ''[[Beyond the Dancing]]'', was released in January 1995 and won the [[ARIA Award for Best Country Album]] at the [[ARIA Music Awards of 1995]]. At the 1996 Country Music Awards, in Tamworth, Cassar-Daley won Best Male Vocalist. He also made a cameo appearance in the motion picture ''[[Race the Sun (film)|Race the Sun]]'' in which he performed a song in a bar scene.\n\nIn June 1996, Cassar-Daley was part of the Australian Country Music Showcase in Nashville. The Showcase included [[Lee Kernaghan]], [[Gina Jeffreys]] and [[Tommy Emmanuel]]. As a result, Cassar-Daley returned to the US to record his new album ''[[True Believer (Troy Cassar-Daley album)|True Believer]]'' (1998) with Steve Dorff.{{cn|date=November 2021}} His follow-up, ''[[Big River (album)|Big River]]'' (1999),won another best country album ARIA Award at the [[ARIA Music Awards of 2000]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.aria.com.au/awards/past-winners/2000|title=2000 ARIA Awards winners|publisher=Australian Recording Industry Association|access-date=21 November 2021}}</ref> His next four studio albums were ''[[Long Way Home (Troy Cassar-Daley album)|Long Way Home]]'' (2002), ''[[Borrowed & Blue]]'' (2004), ''[[Brighter Day (album)|Brighter Day]]'' (2005), and ''[[I Love This Place]]'' (2009), the latter two also winning best country album ARIA Awards.<ref name=\"allmusicbio\"/><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.aria.com.au/awards/past-winners/2006|title=2006 ARIA Awards winners|publisher=Australian Recording Industry Association|access-date=21 November 2021}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.aria.com.au/awards/past-winners/2010|title=2010 ARIA Awards winners|publisher=Australian Recording Industry Association|access-date=21 November 2021}}</ref>\n\nCassar-Daley performed the national anthem at the [[2003 NRL grand final]]. He partnered up with [[Kate Ritchie]] for the singing competition ''[[It Takes Two (Australian television)|It Takes Two]]'' aired on [[Seven Network]] in 2006. In May 2007 he re-appeared on the same show,<ref>[http://au.yahoo.com/it-takes-two/ It Takes Two official website] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20060615163216/http://au.yahoo.com/it-takes-two/ |date=15 June 2006 }}</ref> this time partnered with Krystal Forscutt,<ref>[http://au.yahoo.com/it-takes-two/couples/bio/krystal-forscutt/ Krystal Forscutt \u2013 It Takes Two<!-- Bot generated title -->] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070715141610/http://au.yahoo.com/it-takes-two/couples/bio/krystal-forscutt/ |date=15 July 2007 }}</ref> a former contestant on [[Network Ten]]'s [[Big Brother (Australia)|''Big Brother'' program]]. The same year, Cassar-Daley was featured in [[The Wiggles|Wiggles]] music videos for the songs \"[[Old Dan Tucker]]\" and \"[[Turkey in the Straw]]\". Cassar-Daley with [[Kasey Chambers]] and Shane Nicholson played together at the [[Melbourne Cricket Ground]] on 14 March 2009 for [[Sound Relief]] which was a multi-venue rock music concert in support of relief for the [[February 2009 Victorian bushfires|Victorian Bushfire Crisis]].<ref name=\"Brumby\">{{cite web|url=http://www.premier.vic.gov.au/premier/artists-unite-for-sound-relief-bushfire-benefit.html|title=Artists Unite For 'Sound Relief' Bushfire Benefit \u2013 Premier of Victoria, Australia|last=Brumby|first=John|authorlink=John Brumby|publisher=Premier of Victoria|date=24 February 2009|accessdate=25 February 2009}}</ref><ref name=\"Mitchell\">{{cite news|url=http://www.news.com.au/heraldsun/story/0,21985,25099180-661,00.html |title=Coldplay, Kings of Leon to headline bushfire relief concerts |last=Mitchell |first=Geraldine |work=[[Herald Sun]] |publisher=[[The Herald and Weekly Times Ltd]] |date=24 February 2009 |accessdate=25 February 2009 |url-status=dead |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20090225040650/http://www.news.com.au/heraldsun/story/0,21985,25099180-661,00.html |archivedate=25 February 2009 }}</ref> The event was held simultaneously with another concert taking place at the [[Sydney Cricket Ground]].<ref name=\"Brumby\"/> All the proceeds from the Melbourne Concert went to the [[Red Cross]] Victorian Bushfire Relief Appeal.<ref name=\"Brumby\"/><ref name=\"Mitchell\"/><ref name=\"Official\">{{cite web|url=http://www.soundrelief.com.au/melb/index.php |title=Latest News |publisher=Sound Relief |accessdate=25 February 2009 |url-status=dead |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20090227073309/http://www.soundrelief.com.au/melb/index.php |archivedate=27 February 2009 }}</ref>\n\nCassar-Daley went on to release the albums ''[[Home (Troy Cassar-Daley album)|Home]]'' (2012), ''[[The Great Country Songbook]]'' with [[Adam Harvey]] (2013), and ''[[Freedom Ride (album)|Freedom Ride]]'' (2015).<ref name=\"allmusicbio\"/> In August 2016, Cassar-Daley released his first book, an autobiography of his early life and music career titled ''[[Things I Carry Around]]'' with an accompanying album of the same title.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://australianmusician.com.au/troy-cassar-daley-new-album-book-interview/|title=Troy Cassar-Daley: New Book & Album \u2013 Interview |access-date=1 June 2016}}</ref> In 2017 Cassar-Daley was the 50th inductee into the prestigious [[Australian Roll of Renown]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.tcmf.com.au/What-s-On/Roll-of-Renown/|title=Roll of Renown |publisher=TCMF|access-date=21 August 2018}}</ref> In October 2018, Cassar-Daley released his 42-track double album [[Greatest Hits (Troy Cassar-Daley album)|Greatest Hits]], along with a new single called \"Wouldn't Change A Thing\" on the Bloodlines label, part of [[Mushroom Group]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.triplem.com.au/story/troy-cassar-daley-set-to-deliver-42-of-his-greatest-hits-109467|title=Troy Cassar-Daley Set To Deliver 42 of his Greatest Hits|publisher=TripleM|access-date=1 August 2020}}</ref> The extensive album was also released on vinyl.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.sanity.com.au/products/2393214/Greatest-Hits|title=Troy Cassar-Daley Vinyl|publisher=Sanity|access-date=1 August 2020}}</ref>\n\nIn June 2020, Cassar-Daley signed a worldwide label deal with [[Sony Music Australia|Sony Music Entertainment Australia]]; he had first signed to the label in 1995.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://themusicnetwork.com/troy-cassar-daley-sony-music/|title=Troy Cassar-Daley 'returns home' to Sony Music under new global deal|date=24 June 2020 |publisher=The Music Network|access-date=1 August 2020}}</ref> He released the albums ''[[Christmas for Cowboys]]'' in 2020 and ''[[The World Today (album)|The World Today]]'' in 2021, which won the best country album award at [[2021 ARIA Music Awards|that year's ARIA Music Awards]].<ref name=\"abc2021arias\"/><ref name=\"stack\">{{cite web|url=https://stack.com.au/music/album-review/troy-cassar-daley-christmas-for-cowboys-review/|title=Troy Cassar-Daley, ''Christmas for Cowboys'' review|website=Stack Magazine|date=25 November 2020|access-date=21 November 2021}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/music/2021/mar/19/troy-cassar-daley-i-looked-in-the-mirror-and-thought-stop-it-you-are-destroying-everything-you-love|title=Troy Cassar-Daley: 'I looked in the mirror and thought, stop it. You are destroying everything you love'|work=The Guardian|date=19 March 2021|first=Andrew|last=Stafford|access-date=21 November 2021}}</ref>\n\n==Personal life==\n[[File:TroyCassar-Daley_Family.jpg|thumb|Cassar-Daley with his wife and children]]\nCassar-Daley is married to radio and television presenter [[Laurel Edwards]] with whom he has two children.<ref>[http://www.abc.net.au/tv/enoughrope/transcripts/s1669506.htm Enough Rope with Andrew Denton \u2013 episode 109: Troy Cassar-Daley (26/06/2006)] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20060628202449/http://www.abc.net.au/tv/enoughrope/transcripts/s1669506.htm|date=28 June 2006}}</ref><ref>[http://www.laureledwards.com/bio.htm Welcome to LaurelEdwards.com]</ref> One of their children is singer-songwriter [[Jem Cassar-Daley]].<ref >{{cite web | last=Knowles | first=Rachael | title=Continuing the family legacy, Jem Cassar-Daley is making her mark with music | website=[[NITV]]| date=8 April 2022 | url=https://www.sbs.com.au/nitv/article/continuing-the-family-legacy-jem-cassar-daley-is-making-her-mark-with-music/oqbckpk7p | access-date=12 December 2022}}</ref>\n\nIn 2020, Cassar-Daley's participation in Australia's ''[[Who Do You Think You Are? (Australian TV series)|Who Do You Think You Are?]]'' was broadcast on [[SBS (Australian TV channel)|SBS]], where he traced both his ancestral roots on his father's side in [[Malta]], and his mother's [[Aboriginal Australians|Aboriginal Australian]] ancestry.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://tvtonight.com.au/2020/07/who-do-you-think-you-are-july-7.html|title= Who Do You Think You Are?: July 7|date= 6 July 2020|publisher=TV Tonight|access-date=21 November 2021}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n===Studio albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! Awards===\n[[The Deadly Awards]], (commonly known simply as The Deadlys), was an annual celebration of Australian Aboriginal and Torres Strait Islander achievement in music, sport, entertainment and community. They ran from 1996 to 2013.\n\n{{awards table}}\n|-\n| [[Deadly Awards 1997|1997]]\n| ''True Believer''\n| Album of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| [[Deadly Awards 2001|2001]]\n| himself\n| Country Artist of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| [[Deadly Awards 2003|2003]]\n| himself\n| Male Artist of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| [[Deadly Awards 2004|2004]]\n| himself\n| Male Artist of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| rowspan=\"2\"| [[Deadly Awards 2006|2006]]\n| himself\n| Male Artist of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| \"Lonesome But Free\"\n| Single of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| [[Deadly Awards 2007|2007]]\n| \"Going Back Home\"\n| Song of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| [[Deadly Awards 2012|2012]]\n| ''Home''\n| Album of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| [[Deadly Awards 2013|2013]]\n| himself\n| Male Artist of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n===Environmental Music Prize===\nThe [[Environmental Music Prize]] is a quest to find a theme song to inspire action on climate and conservation. It commenced in 2022.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://themusicnetwork.com/environmental-music-prize-search/|title=Environmental Music Prize Searches for Green Theme Song|website=The Music Network|date=May 2022|access-date=22 June 2022}}</ref>\n{{awards table}}\n! {{Abbr|Ref.|Reference}}\n|-\n| 2023\n| Back On Country\"\n| Environmental Music Prize\n| {{nom}}\n| <ref name=\"EMP 2023 noms\">{{cite web|url=https://musicfeeds.com.au/news/flume-tash-sultana-and-moju-among-finalists-for-the-2023-environmental-music-prize/|title= Environmental Music Prize 2023 Finalists|website=[[Music Feeds]]|date=26 April 2023|access-date=4 May 2023}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://musicfeeds.com.au/news/xavier-rudd-environmental-music-prize/ |title= Xavier Rudd Wins 2023's Environmental Music Prize|website=[[Music Feeds]]|date=13 June 2023|access-date=13 June 2023}}</ref>\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n===Mo Awards===\nThe Australian Entertainment Mo Awards (commonly known informally as the [[Mo Awards]]), were annual Australian entertainment industry awards. They recognise achievements in live entertainment in Australia from 1975 to 2016. Troy Cassar-Daley won six awards in that time.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.moawards.com.au/awardwinners|title=MO Award Winners|website=Mo Awards|access-date=16 March 2022}}</ref>\n{{awards table}} (wins only)\n|-\n| 1997\n| Troy Cassar-Daley\n| Male Country Entertainer of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 1998\n| Troy Cassar-Daley\n| Male Country Entertainer of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 1999\n| Troy Cassar-Daley\n| Male Country Entertainer of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 2002\n| Troy Cassar-Daley\n| Male Country Entertainer of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 2003\n| Troy Cassar-Daley\n| Male Country Entertainer of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 2008\n| Troy Cassar-Daley\n| Slim Dusty Male Country Vocal Performer of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n===National Indigenous Music Awards===\nThe [[National Indigenous Music Awards]] recognise excellence, innovation and leadership among Aboriginal and Torres Strait Islander musicians from throughout Australia. They commenced in 2004.\n\n{{awards table}}\n|-\n| rowspan=\"2\"| [[National Indigenous Music Awards 2012|2012]]\n| himself\n| Artist of the Year\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| ''Home''\n| Album of the Year\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| rowspan=\"3\"| [[National Indigenous Music Awards 2017|2017]]\n| himself\n| Artist of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| ''Things I Carry Around''\n| Album of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| \"Things I Carry Around\"\n| Song of the Year\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| rowspan=\"1\"| [[National Indigenous Music Awards 2021|2021]]\n| \"Back On Country\"\n| Film Clip of the Year\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| [[National Indigenous Music Awards 2024|2024]]\n| ''Between the Fires''\n| Album of the Year\n| {{nom}}\n| rowspan=\"1\"| <ref name=\"NIMA2024noms\">{{cite web|url= https://themusic.com.au/industry/the-kid-laroi-barkaa-lead-national-indigenous-music-awards-nominations/yHR22t3c394/19-07-24 |title= The Kid LAROI & Barkaa Lead National Indigenous Music Awards Nominations |website=[[The Music (magazine)|The Music]]|date= 19 July 2024|access-date= 19 July 2024|author= Mary Varvaris }}</ref>\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n===Queensland Music Awards===\nThe [[Queensland Music Awards]] (previously known as Q Song Awards) are annual awards celebrating [[Queensland, Australia]]'s brightest emerging artists and established legends. They commenced in 2006.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.queenslandmusicawards.com.au/about|title= About the Queensland Music Awards|website=Queensland Music Awards|access-date=21 March 2021}}</ref>\n\n{{Awards table}} <small>(wins only)</small>\n|-\n| [[Queensland_Music_Awards#2009_Q_Song_Awards|2009]]<ref>{{cite web|url= https://www.queenslandmusicawards.com.au/past-winners/2009|title=Past Winners 2009|website=Queensland Music Awards|access-date=25 March 2021}}</ref>\n| \"Big Big Love\"\n| Published Song of the Year \n| {{won}}\n|}\n\n==References==\n{{reflist}}\n\n==External links==\n* [http://www.troycassardaley.com.au Official website]\n\n{{Troy Cassar-Daley}}\n\n{{Authority control}}\n\n{{DEFAULTSORT:Cassar-Daley, Troy}}\n[[Category:1969 births]]\n[[Category:APRA Award winners]]\n[[Category:ARIA Award winners]]\n[[Category:Australian country guitarists]]\n[[Category:Australian country singers]]\n[[Category:Australian male singers]]\n[[Category:Australian people of Maltese descent]]\n[[Category:Indigenous Australian musicians]]\n[[Category:Living people]]\n[[Category:Australian male guitarists]]\n[[Category:Musicians from New South Wales]]\n[[Category:People from Grafton, New South Wales]]"}]}}}}{"batchcomplete":"","warnings":{"main":{"*":"Subscribe to the mediawiki-api-announce mailing list at <https://lists.wikimedia.org/postorius/lists/mediawiki-api-announce.lists.wikimedia.org/> for notice of API deprecations and breaking changes.
