Schneider has been nominated for two awards.<ref>{{cite web|url = https://www.ariaawards.com.au/history/search/?text=Melinda%20Schneider|title = ARIA Awards Search Results - Melinda Schneider|work = ARIA Awards|accessdate = 18 May 2020}}</ref>\n\n{{awards table}}\n|-\n| [[ARIA Music Awards of 2004|2004]]\n| ''Family Tree''\n| [[ARIA Award for Best Country Album|Best Country Album]]\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| [[ARIA Music Awards of 2008|2008]]\n| ''Be Yourself''\n| Best Country Album\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n===Country Music Awards (CMAA)===\nThe [[Country Music Awards of Australia]] (CMAA) is an annual awards night held in January during the [[Tamworth Country Music Festival]] and celebrates recording excellence in the Australian country music industry. Schneider has won six awards.<ref>{{Cite web |url=https://www.country.com.au/awards/past-award-winners|title=Past Award Winners|website=Country|accessdate=18 May 2020 }}</ref>\n\n{{awards table}}(wins only)\n|-\n| 2000 || \"Love Away the Night\" with [[Adam Brand (musician)|Adam Brand]] || Vocal Collaboration of the Year  || {{won}}\n|-\n| 2003 || \"The Story of My Life\" || Female Vocalist of the Year  || {{won}}\n|-\n| 2005 || ''Family Tree'' || Album of the Year  || {{won}}\n|-\n| 2005 || \"Real People\" || Song of the Year  || {{won}}\n|-\n| 2008 || ''Stronger'' || Top Selling Album of the Year  || {{won}}\n|-\n| 2009 || \"Still Here\" with [[Paul Kelly (Australian musician)|Paul Kelly]] || Vocal Collaboration of the Year  || {{won}}\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n===Mo Awards===\nThe Australian Entertainment Mo Awards (commonly known informally as the [[Mo Awards]]), were annual Australian entertainment industry awards. They recognise achievements in live entertainment in Australia from 1975 to 2016. Melinda Schneider won eleven awards in that time.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.moawards.com.au/awardwinners|title=MO Award Winners|website=Mo Awards|access-date=16 March 2022}}</ref>\n{{awards table}} (wins only)\n|-\n| 1994\n| Melinda Schneider\n| Johnny O'Keefe Encouragement Award\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 2000\n| Melinda Schneider\n| Female Country Entertainer of the Year \n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 2002\n| Melinda Schneider\n| Female Country Entertainer of the Year \n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 2003\n| Melinda Schneider\n| Female Country Entertainer of the Year \n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 2004\n| Melinda Schneider\n| Female Country Entertainer of the Year \n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 2006\n| Melinda Schneider\n| Slim Dusty Country Performer of the Year \n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 2007\n| Melinda Schneider\n| Female Vocal Performer of the Year \n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 2008\n| Melinda Schneider\n| Female Vocal Performer of the Year \n| {{won}}\n|-\n|rowspan=\"2\"| 2011\n| Melinda Schneider\n| Slim Dusty Country Act of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| Melinda Schneider\n| Female Vocal Performer of the Year \n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 2014\n| Melinda Schneider\n| Slim Dusty Country Act of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n==References==\n{{Reflist}}\n\n==External links==\n*[http://www.melindaschneider.com/ Official website]\n\n{{Authority control}}\n\n{{DEFAULTSORT:Schneider, Melinda}}\n[[Category:1971 births]]\n[[Category:Living people]]\n[[Category:Australian people of German descent]]\n[[Category:Australian country singers]]\n[[Category:21st-century Australian singers]]"}]}}}}{"batchcomplete":"","warnings":{"main":{"*":"Subscribe to the mediawiki-api-announce mailing list at <https://lists.wikimedia.org/postorius/lists/mediawiki-api-announce.lists.wikimedia.org/> for notice of API deprecations and breaking changes. Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Harmony_James","to":"Harmony James"}],"pages":{"37684047":{"pageid":37684047,"ns":0,"title":"Harmony James","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|Australian singer-songwriter}}\n{{Use dmy dates|date=June 2020}}\n{{Use Australian English|date=March 2019}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Harmony James\n| image           = Harmony_%26_Shane_at_Lizotte%27s.jpg\n| alt             =\n| caption         = James performing live with [[Shane Nicholson (singer)|Shane Nicholson]]\n| landscape       = yes\n| birth_name      =\n| birth_place     = [[Victoria (Australia)|Victoria]], Australia\n| genre           = [[Country music|Country]], [[alternative country]], [[folk music|folk]]\n| associated_acts =\n| occupation      = Singer, songwriter\n| years_active    = 2007\u2013present\n| label           = [[Warner Music|Warner]]\n| website         = {{URL|http://harmonyjames.com/}}\n}}\n\n'''Harmony James'''  is an Australian singer-songwriter. Although James is often classified as a country artist, her music draws on many genres, including [[folk music|folk]], pop, rock and [[blues music|blues]]. In 2006 Harmony first came to the attention of the music industry when she became the only Australian songwriter to have won the country category of the International Songwriting Competition, with her song \"Tailwind\".<ref name=\"update\" /> Her second single, \"Somebody Stole My Horse\",  became Australian radio's second most played country song in 2008.<ref>{{cite web|title=Herm Kovac Productions|url=http://www.ramrodstudio.com/Herm%20kovac.html|work=Ramrod Studio|accessdate=15 December 2012}}</ref> spawned \n\n==Early life==\nBorn in [[Victoria (Australia)|Victoria]], Australia to a [[Baptist]] preacher as one of twelve children, Harmony went to a private school and says she had \"few friends\".<ref name=\"courier\" /> She read voraciously, eventually discovering the western novels of [[Louis L'Amour]].<ref name=update>{{cite journal|title=Tailwind or Tornado?|journal=Country Update|issue=54|url=http://www.countryupdate.com.au/images/stories/cu54/01_harmony_james.pdf|accessdate=1 December 2012}}{{dead link|date=October 2017 |bot=InternetArchiveBot |fix-attempted=yes }}</ref> James discovered traditional country music after a friend returned from [[Texas]] with records by [[Dolly Parton]] and [[The Judds]].<ref name=\"courier\" /> Soon after, James taught herself enough guitar to learn a few country songs and took to the streets singing to earn money.\n\nShe later ran a stock camp in the outback of [[Queensland]] and worked with cattle on the [[Northern Territory]]'s [[Barkly Tableland]]. She left home to work as a [[Jillaroo (trainee)|jillaroo]] at some of the most remote cattle stations in southwestern Queensland,<ref name=\"update\" /> \"covered in mud and blood, roughing it with the guys, working so hard I had biceps and thinking, 'This is not what my mother pictured for me'.\" A gig at a school fete in [[Goondiwindi]] led to an offer from the local publican and Harmony's songbook started filling, even as she continued her parallel life on the land, from the Cape to [[Tennant Creek]], studying agriculture at [[The University of Queensland]] at [[Gatton, Queensland|Gatton]]<ref name=\"courier\" /> and working as a welder \"in a shed of 80 blokes.\"<ref name=capital>{{cite news|last=Jarvis|first=Susan|title=Complete Harmony|url=http://www.capitalnews.com.au/editorial.asp?editorial_id=1614&issue=117|access-date=1 December 2012|newspaper=Capital News|date=July 2009|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130427073019/http://www.capitalnews.com.au/editorial.asp?editorial_id=1614&issue=117|archive-date=27 April 2013|url-status=dead}}</ref> \"My musical exposure was mostly church music until I got a job as a checkout chick and heard the radio,\" she says. \"Now when I hang out with other musos they'll drop names and I'll just look at them blankly 'cause my music history starts in '95.\"<ref name=alberts>{{cite web|title=Harmony James|url=http://albertmusic.com/musicians/harmony-james|work=Alberts|publisher=Alberts Pty Ltd.|accessdate=1 December 2012|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150905235752/http://albertmusic.com/musicians/harmony-james|archive-date=5 September 2015|url-status=dead}}</ref>\n\n==Career==\nIn 2007, James won the country category of the International Songwriting Competition, and began working with producer Herm Kovac on her debut EP, ''[[Harmony James (EP)|Harmony James]]''.  \n\nHer debut studio album, ''[[Tailwind (album)|Tailwind]]'',  was released in 2009.  In 2009, James went on tour with [[Sara Storer]] and [[Kasey Chambers]], performing \"Tailwind\" in major festivals. Chambers later recorded her own version of one of James' songs, \"Good Enough.\"<ref>{{Citation |title=Good Enough - Kasey Chambers, Shane Nicholson {{!}} Song Info {{!}} AllMusic |url=https://www.allmusic.com/song/mt0045623522 |language=en |access-date=2022-02-26}}</ref>\n\nJames was nominated for Best Female Artist and Best Album for the CMAA Golden Guitar Awards in 2010 and won Best Female artist at the Victorian and [[Mildura]] Country Awards.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Harmony James |url=https://www.female.com.au/harmony-james.htm |access-date=2022-02-26 |website=Female.com.au |language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |last=Eliezer |first=Christie |last2= |first2= |date=2009-11-12 |title=Keith Urban Snags 4 CMAA Nominations |url=https://www.billboard.com/music/music-news/keith-urban-snags-4-cmaa-nominations-1262999/ |access-date=2022-02-26 |website=Billboard |language=en-US}}</ref>{{cn|date=April 2021}} and headlined her first [[Tamworth Country Music Festival|Tamworth]] show.<ref name=courier>{{cite news|last=Mengel|first=Noel|title=It's the sound of sweet Harmony|url=http://www.couriermail.com.au/ipad/its-the-sound-of-sweet-harmony/story-fn6ck8la-1226249629574|accessdate=1 December 2012|newspaper=The Courier-Mail|date=21 January 2012}}</ref> \n\nAustralian country music trio The [[McClymonts]] signed James in 2011 as an opening act for their first major Australian tour. James' 2011 single \"Precious Little\" became the second most played single on Australian radio.{{citation needed|date=March 2019}}\n\nIn March 2011, James returned to the studio with Herm Kovac to work on her second album, ''[[Handfuls of Sky]]''. The following November, James signed a worldwide publishing deal with [[Albert Music]]<ref>{{cite web|title=Australian Country Songwriter Harmony James Signs World-wide Deal With Alberts|url=http://albertmusic.com/news/australian-country-songwriter-harmony-james-signs-world-wide-deal-with-albe|work=Alberts|publisher=Alberts Pty Ltd|accessdate=1 December 2012|date=11 October 2011}}</ref> and a major record deal with [[Warner Music Australia]] on the same day.<ref>{{Cite web |date=17 October 2011 |title=Australian Country Music News, October 2011 |url=https://www.countrymusicbulletin.com.au/newsarchive_Oct11.html |access-date=2022-02-26 |website=Country Music Bulletin}}</ref>\n\n''[[Handfuls of Sky]]'' was released on 20 January 2012, along with the ''Harmony James Songbook'', a portfolio of sheet music, lyrics, photos and stories. In 2012, James continued performing at festivals, tours, and shows with artists including [[Troy Cassar-Daley]]<ref name=\"courier\" /> and [[Tim Freedman]]. The first single from ''Handfuls of Sky'', \"Pride\", spent six weeks at number one,<ref name=\"courier\" /> and the third single, \"Emmylou's Guitar\" spend three weeks at number one. 2012 also brought more recognition for James, as she won the country category at the Queensland Music Awards<ref>{{cite web|title=QLD Music Awards 2012|url=http://www.qmusic.com.au/qldmusicawards/2012/index.cfm?contentID=704|work=Queensland Music Awards|access-date=1 December 2012|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20141129014823/http://www.qmusic.com.au/qldmusicawards/2012/index.cfm?contentID=704|archive-date=29 November 2014|url-status=dead}}</ref> and was nominated for three 2013 Golden Guitar awards: Best Vocal Collaboration with [[Shane Nicholson (singer)|Shane Nicholson]] for \"Reach for You\", Best Female Artist, and APRA Song of the Year for \"Emmylou's Guitar\".<ref>{{cite web|title=41st Country Music Awards of Australia Finalists Announced|url=http://www.country.com.au/news/cmaa-news/856-41st-country-music-awards-of-australia-finalists-announced|work=CMAA|access-date=1 December 2012|date=12 November 2012|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121115091027/http://www.country.com.au/news/cmaa-news/856-41st-country-music-awards-of-australia-finalists-announced|archive-date=15 November 2012|df=}}</ref>\n\nIn 2014, James released her third studio album, ''[[Cautionary Tales (album)|Cautionary Tales]],'' for which James received CMAA 2015 nominations in the categories of Best Album, Best Female Artist, and Best Heritage Song for \"Coal Seam Gas\".<ref>{{Cite web |date=16 November 2014 |title=Golden Guitar Awards Unveil 2015 Finalists List |url=https://themusic.com.au/ |access-date=2022-02-26 |website=The Music |publisher=SGC Group |language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |last=Belt |first=Rebecca |date=2014-11-17 |title=Golden Guitar Awards: The finalists {{!}} SPECIAL COVERAGE |url=https://www.northerndailyleader.com.au/story/2700941/golden-guitar-awards-the-finalists-special-coverage/ |access-date=2022-02-26 |website=The Northern Daily Leader |language=en-AU}}</ref> Harmony toured extensively with Luke O'Shea and Pete Denahy and then later in the year with Lachlan Bryan.{{citation needed|date=March 2019}}<ref>{{Cite web |date=2016-12-30 |title=Lachlan Bryan & Harmony James at The Listening Room in Mobile, AL (Thur. Dec. 8, 2016) |url=https://thesouthlandmusicline.com/photos-and-music-art/photos/lachlan-bryan-harmony-james-at-the-listening-room-in-mobile-al-thur-dec-8-2016/ |access-date=2022-02-26 |website=The Southland Music Line |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nHarmony opened for and performed with Emmylou Harris and Rodney Crowell on their Australian tour in 2015. ''The Courier Mail''<nowiki/>'s Noel Mengel reviewed the show, saying about James' set, \"When someone shines while singing alongside Emmylou Harris, you know that's a truly great singer. If you love this kind of music, you really need to check her out.\"<ref>{{Cite web |last=Mengel |first=Noel |date=2 July 2015 |title=Emmylou Harris and Rodney Crowell shine at Jupiters gig |url=https://www.couriermail.com.au/entertainment/confidential/emmylou-harris-and-rodney-crowell-shine-at-jupiters-gig/news-story/0d574ce0f6d1fa5523e0da51f8e8f34a |website=The Courier Mail}}</ref> \n\nIn late 2018, James' official Facebook page announced a new independent album ''Resignation''. It was produced by Glen Hannah, music critic Bernard Zuel published a favourable review of the record, suggesting \"James might be earning the right to be counted among the likes of the more experienced Gretchen Peters and Rosanne Cash\".<ref>{{Cite web |last=Zuel |first=Bernard |date=2019-01-30 |title=Harmony James - Resignation: Review |url=https://www.bernardzuel.net/post/2019/01/31/harmony-james-resignation-review |access-date=2022-02-26 |website=Bernard Zuel |language=en}}</ref> The ''Sunburnt Country Music'' blog said \"despite its title, ''Resignation'' is not an album that sounds like defeat, retreat or weariness \u2013 it is a glorious manifestation of James's skills and talent, and it has been worth waiting for\".<ref>{{Cite web |date=2019-02-18 |title=Album review: Resignation by Harmony James |url=https://sunburntcountrymusic.com/2019/02/18/album-review-resignation-by-harmony-james/ |access-date=2022-02-26 |website=Sunburnt Country Music |language=en}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n=== Studio albums ===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\" border=\"1\"\n! This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Lee_Kernaghan","to":"Lee Kernaghan"}],"pages":{"2193612":{"pageid":2193612,"ns":0,"title":"Lee Kernaghan","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use dmy dates|date=September 2021}}\n{{Use Australian English|date=October 2016}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name                = Lee Kernaghan\n| image               = Lee Kernaghan (cropped2).jpg\n| alt                 = Man in black hat sitting on ground\n| caption             = \n| birth_name          = Lee Raymond Kernaghan\n| alias               =\n| birth_date          = {{Birth date and age|1964|4|15|df=yes}}\n| birth_place         = [[Corryong]], [[Victoria (Australia)|Victoria]], Australia\n| instrument          = Vocals, guitar\n| genre               = [[Country music|Country]], [[Country Rock]], [[Rock music|Rock]], [[Pop music|Pop]], [[Country Pop]]\n| occupation          = Singer, songwriter, musician\n| years_active        = 1977\u2013present\n| label               = [[ABC Music]]\n| associated_acts     = {{hlist|The Blue Devils|Fiona Kernaghan|[[Ray Kernaghan]]|[[Tania Kernaghan]]}}\n| website             = {{URL|leekernaghan.com.au}}\n}}\n'''Lee Kernaghan''' [[Order of Australia|OAM]] (born 15 April 1964) is an Australian [[country music]] singer, songwriter and guitarist. Kernaghan has won four [[ARIA Awards]] and three [[APRA Awards (Australia)|APRA Awards]], and has sold over two million albums, and as of 2021,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.jbhifi.com.au/products/cd-kernaghan-lee-backroad-nation-cd?queryID=1f79a7cabae927384ce0134b82f8b8e6&objectID=379435|title=Backroad Nation|website=[[JB HiFi]]|access-date=30 December 2021}}</ref> has won 38 [[Golden Guitar]]s at the Country Music Awards of Australia (second to [[Slim Dusty]]).\n\nHe was the 2008 [[Australian of the Year]], in recognition of his support for rural and regional Australia.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://nla.gov.au/nla.cs-ma-ANL%3AMA~Converted-ruth-5|title=Kernaghan. Lee|work=Music Australia|publisher=National Library of Australia|access-date=16 October 2009}}</ref><ref name=\"aoty\"/> Kernaghan was the recipient of the Outstanding Achievement Award at the 2015 ARIA Awards, for ''Spirit of the Anzacs''.<ref name=\":3\" />\n\n== Biography ==\n===1965\u20131990: Early years===\nLee Kernaghan was born on 15 April 1964 in [[Corryong]], Victoria and is the son of country music singer and truck driver [[Ray Kernaghan]]. Lee spent his formative years growing up in Albury [[New South Wales]]. His grandfather was a third generation drover of sheep and cattle.<ref name=\"abcbio\">{{cite web|url=https://www.abcmusic.com.au/lee-kernaghan|title=Lee Kernaghan|website=ABC Music|access-date=30 December 2021}}</ref>\n\nIn 1986, Kernaghan traveled to the United States to represent Australia at the [[Nashville, Tennessee|Nashville]] 'Fan Fair' country music festival.\n\n===1990s ===\nIn 1992, Kernaghan released \"Boys from the Bush\" which became his first number one on the country chart.<ref name=\"abcbio\"/> Kernaghan said \"When Garth (Porter) and I first wrote 'Boys from the Bush' I had no idea it would ever be a hit. It was just a song about me and my mates, working on the land, going to the pub and tearing around in utes. I didn't think anyone would be that interested in us... we were just kids from the bush but Garth said 'this record (''The Outback Club'') has to be about your life and where you come from so we wrote that song and several others and before long I had a band and we were out on the road performing them live.\"<ref name=\"abcbio\"/>\n\nIn May 1992, Kernaghan released ''[[The Outback Club]]''. The album debuted at number 94 on the [[ARIA Charts]].<ref name=\"AUS-Albums\"/> At the 1993 Country Music Awards of Australia (CMAA), the album won Album of the Year the [[ARIA Award for Best Country Album]].<ref name=\"CMAA\"/> The album re-entered the chart later peaking at number 58 in May 1994.<ref name=\"AUS-Albums\"/>\n\nIn August 1993, Kernaghan released his second studio album, ''[[Three Chain Road]]''. The album again won the CMAA Album of the Year and the ARIA Award for Best Country Album.<ref name=\"CMAA\"/>\n\nIn July 1995, Kernaghan released his third studio album, ''[[1959 (album)|1959]]'', which peaked at number 9 on the ARIA Chart, becoming Kernaghan's first top ten album.<ref name=\"AUS-Albums\"/> The album won Kernaghan his third Album of the Year at the CMAA of 1996.<ref name=\"CMAA\"/>\n\nIn February 1998, Kernaghan released his fourth studio album, ''[[Hat Town]]''. The album peaked at number 7 on the ARIA Chart<ref name=\"AUS-Albums\"/> and won his fourth Album of the Year at the CMAA of 1999.<ref name=\"CMAA\"/>\n\nKernaghan's fifth studio album was ''[[The Christmas Album (Lee Kernaghan album)|The Christmas Album]]'' in November 1998. The album peaked at number 31 on the ARIA chart.<ref name=\"AUS-Albums\"/>\n\n===2000s ===\nIn January 2000, Kernaghan released his sixth studio album, ''[[Rules of the Road (Lee Kernaghan album)|Rules of the Road]]''. This was followed by ''[[Electric Rodeo (Lee Kernaghan album)|Electric Rodeo]]'' in July 2002 which won Album of the Year and Top Selling Album of the Year at the 2003 CMAA.<ref name=\"CMAA\"/> ''Electric Rodeo'' peaked at number 5 on the ARIA chart.<ref name=\"AUS-Albums\"/>\n\nKernaghan was part of ''[[The Man from Snowy River: Arena Spectacular]]'' in 2002.\n\nIn October 2004, Kernaghan released his first greatest hits collection titled, ''[[The Big Ones: Greatest Hits Vol. 1]]''. The album peaked at number 16 on the ARIA charts and was certified platinum.<ref name=\"AUS-Albums\"/>\n\nIn April 2006, Kernaghan released his eighth studio album, ''[[The New Bush]]''. The album peaked at number 6 on the ARIA Charts and won Album of the Year and Top Selling Album of the Year at the 2007 CMAA.<ref name=\"CMAA\"/>\n\nIn July 2007, Kernaghan released his ninth studio album, ''[[Spirit of the Bush]]''. The album's title track peaked at number 11 on the ARIA singles chart, becoming Kernaghan's highest charting single. The song won three awards at the 2008 CMAA.<ref name=\"CMAA\"/>\n\nIn November 2009, Kernaghan released his tenth studio album, ''[[Planet Country]]''.\n\nIn 2009 Kernaghan was named the biggest hit-maker of the last twenty years on the Australian Country Tracks chart, beating musical greats from Australia and international.<ref name=\"abcbio\"/>\n\n===2010s ===\nIn September 2011, Kernaghan released his second greatest hits collection, ''[[Ultimate Hits (Lee Kernaghan album)|Ultimate Hits]]''. The album peaked at number 8 on the ARIA chart.<ref name=\"AUS-Albums\"/>\n\nIn October 2012, Kernaghan released his eleventh studio album, ''[[Beautiful Noise (Lee Kernaghan album)|Beautiful Noise]]''. The album peaked at number 9 on the ARIA chart.<ref name=\"AUS-Albums\"/>\n\nDuring a visit to the [[Australian War Memorial]] (AWM) in 2013, Kernaghan's friend and AWM Director [[Brendan Nelson|Dr. Brendan Nelson]] introduced Kernaghan to letters that were written by [[Australian Defence Force|Australian service men and women]] during various wars dating back to the landing at [[Gallipoli Campaign|Gallipoli]] during the [[World War I|First World War]]. These letters were held in the vaults at the AWM.<ref>{{Cite web|title = Lee Kernaghan \u2013 \"Outstanding Achievement Award\" for Spirit of the Anzacs {{!}} Australian War Memorial|url = https://www.awm.gov.au/blog/2015/12/10/lee-kernaghan-Spirit-of-the-Anzacs/|website = www.awm.gov.au|access-date = 14 December 2015}}</ref> The power of the letters affected Kernaghan deeply and the experience at the Australian War Memorial that day was the catalyst that saw these letters put to music in what would become the ''[[Spirit of the Anzacs (album)]]'' in March 2015. Upon release, the album peaked at number 1 on the ARIA charts, becoming Kernaghan's first chart topper. It was the highest selling Australian artist album for 2015.<ref name=\":3\">{{Cite web|title = ARIAs: Lee Kernaghan wins achievement award|url = http://www.skynews.com.au/culture/showbiz/music/2015/11/26/arias--lee-kernaghan-wins-achievement-award.html|website = www.skynews.com.au|access-date =14 December 2015}}</ref>\n\n2015 also saw the release of Kernaghan's first book, ''The Boy from the Bush, These Are My Songs, These Are My Stories''.\n\nIn March 2017, Kernaghan released his fourteenth studio album, ''[[The 25th Anniversary Album (Lee Kernaghan album)|The 25th Anniversary Album]]''. The album peaked at number 2 on the ARIA chart.<ref name=\"AUS-Albums\"/>\n\nIn 2019 Kernaghan released his fifteenth studio album, ''[[Backroad Nation]]'' with the title track staying four weeks at #1 on the country singles charts.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://countrytrackschart.com.au/index.php?chartid=273|title=Country Songs Top 40 Australian Airplay Chart|website=countrytrackschart.com.au|access-date=7 August 2019}}</ref>\n\n===2020s ===\nIn 2022 Kernaghan is set to celebrate his 30th anniversary as an artist. In January 2022, he released a 3-CD greatest hits collection titled ''[[The Very Best of Lee Kernaghan: Three Decades of Hits]]'' on 14 January 2022 which peaked at number 17 on the ARIA charts.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.jbhifi.com.au/products/cd-kernaghan-lee-very-best-of-lee-kernaghan-three-decades-of-hits-3cd?queryID=4099785a3b5dbca5b478be730a34c990&objectID=540243|title=Very Best Of Lee Kernaghan: Three Decades Of Hits|website=[[JB Hi-Fi]]|date=30 December 2021}}</ref>\n\n== Personal life ==\nDuring July 2015, Kernaghan's music was played at anti-Islam rallies in Australia, without his permission.<ref name=\"the Music\">{{cite news | url = http://themusic.com.au/news/all/2015/07/24/lee-kernaghan-sits-on-fence-over-reclaim-australia-use-of-song/ | title = Lee Kernaghan Sits on Fence Over Reclaim Australia Use of Song | last = (staff writer) | work = themusic.com.au | date = 24 July 2015 | access-date = 2 July 2016 }}</ref><ref name=\"Reclaim\">{{cite news | url = http://www.smh.com.au/entertainment/music/as-midnight-oil-demands-reclaim-australia-stop-playing-songs-lee-kernaghan-refuses-20150724-gijkuu.html | title = As Midnight Oil Demands Reclaim Australia Stop Playing Songs, Lee Kernaghan Refuses | last = Vincent | first = Peter | work = [[The Sydney Morning Herald]] | date = 24 July 2015 | access-date = 2 July 2016 }}</ref> He responded that the use of his work should be \"consistent with \u2013 and respectful of, the memory of ... [soldiers who] laid down their lives for the freedoms we have today.\"<ref name=\"Reclaim\" /> Fellow local artists, [[Jimmy Barnes]], [[John Farnham]] and [[Mark Seymour]], objected to the use of their material at those rallies.\n\nKernaghan married musician Robyn McKelvie in 1999. They have two sons, Jet and Rock.<ref name=smh2013>{{cite web|url= https://www.smh.com.au/lifestyle/what-i-know-about-women-20130528-2n9aw.html |title=What I know about women - Lee Kernaghan |website=Sydney Morning Herald |date=2 June 2013 |access-date=28 January 2023 }}</ref>\n\n=== Business ventures ===\nFor several years, Kernaghan owned the historic Great Western Hotel in [[Rockhampton, Queensland]], after buying the pub in 2003 when it was placed into receivership after a downturn in trade and public liability concerns.<ref>[http://www.abc.net.au/site-archive/rural/qld/stories/s828257.htm Kernaghan buys Great Western pub], Chris Lawson, ''[[The Country Hour|Queensland Country Hour]]'', [[ABC Rural]], 9 April 2003. Retrieved 23 March 2017.</ref><ref>[http://www.abc.net.au/site-archive/rural/news/stories/s828277.htm Boy from the bush buys QLD pub], ''National Rural News'', [[ABC Rural]], 9 April 2003. Retrieved 23 March 2017.</ref> Kernaghan has described the time during which he owned the Great Western Hotel as one of the greatest periods of his life.<ref>[https://www.themorningbulletin.com.au/news/lee-kernaghan-returns-to-second-home-country-music/2631007 Country music legend Lee Kernaghan returns to 'second home'], Michelle Gately, ''[[The Morning Bulletin]]'', 7 May 2015. Retrieved 23 March 2017.</ref>\n\n== Discography ==\n=== Studio albums ===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\" border=\"1\"\n|-\n! scope=\"col\" rowspan=\"2\" style=\"width:17em;\"| Title\n! scope=\"col\" rowspan=\"2\" style=\"width:18em;\"| Album details\n! scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\"| Peak chart positions\n! scope=\"col\" rowspan=\"2\"| [[List of music recording certifications|Certifications]]\n|-\n! scope=\"col\" style=\"width:3.7em;font-size:90%;\"| [[ARIA Charts|AUS]]<br /><ref name=\"AUS-Albums\">Peak chart positions in Australia:\n*Top 50 peaks: {{cite web|url=http://australian-charts.com/showinterpret.asp?interpret=Lee+Kernaghan|title=australian-charts.com \u2013 Discography Lee Kernaghan|publisher=Hung Medien|access-date=25 August 2021}}\n*Top 100 peaks to December 2010: {{cite book|last=Ryan|first=Gavin|title=Australia's Music Charts 1988\u20132010|year=2011|publisher=Moonlight Publishing|location=Mt. [[Shannon Noll]] and [[Megan Washington]])}}\n| 2015\n| 32\n| ''Spirit of the Anzacs''\n|}\n\n== Awards and nominations ==\nKernaghan received the [[Order of Australia]] Medal in 2004.<ref name=\"honour1\">{{cite web|url=https://honours.pmc.gov.au/honours/awards/1056303|title=KERNAGHAN, Lee Raymond OAM|work=It's an Honour|publisher=Department of the Prime Minister and Cabinet|access-date=16 October 2009}}</ref>\n\nIn 2008, he was [[Australian of the Year]],<ref name=\"australian1\">{{cite news|url=http://www.theaustralian.news.com.au/story/0,25197,23108522-5018520,00.html |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20091003235723/http://www.theaustralian.news.com.au/story/0%2C25197%2C23108522-5018520%2C00.html |url-status=dead |archive-date= 3 October 2009 |title=Lee Kernaghan named Australian of the Year |date=25 January 2008 |publisher=The Australian |access-date=16 October 2009 }}</ref> in recognition for his support of rural and regional Australia; his 'Pass the Hat Around' tours have raised more than a million dollars for rural communities during a challenging period of drought.<ref name=\"aoty\">{{Cite web|title = Australian of the Year Awards|url = https://www.australianoftheyear.org.au/recipients/lee-kernaghan/111/|archive-url = {{nom}}\n|-\n| [[ARIA Music Awards of 2019|2019]]\n| ''Backroad Nation''\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n=== APRA Awards ===\nThe [[APRA Awards (Australia)|APRA Awards]] are held in Australia and New Zealand by the [[Australasian Performing Right Association]] to recognise songwriting skills, sales and airplay performance by its members annually. Kernaghan has won four awards from nine nominations.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.apraamcos.com.au/search|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210207235410/https://www.apraamcos.com.au/search|url-status=dead|archive-date=7 February 2021|title=Nine first-time winners in 12 APRA Music Award categories|work=APRA Awards|publisher=[[Australasian Performing Right Association]] (APRA) &#124; [[Australasian Mechanical Copyright Owners Society]] (AMCOS)|date=6 March 2015}}</ref>\n\n{{awards table}}\n|-\n| [[APRA Music Awards of 1993|1993]]\n| \"Boys from the Bush\"\n| Country Song of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| [[APRA Music Awards of 1996|1996]]\n| \"1959\"\n| Most Performed Country Work\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| [[APRA Music Awards of 1999|1999]]\n| \"Hat Town\"\n| Most Performed Country Work\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| [[APRA Music Awards of 2004|2004]]\n| \"Way It Is\"\n| Most Performed Country Work\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| [[APRA Music Awards of 2007|2007]]\n| \"New Bush\"\n| Most Performed Country Work\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| [[APRA Music Awards of 2008|2008]]\n| \"Spirit of the Bush\" <small>(featuring Adam Brand and Steve Forde)</small>\n| Most Performed Country Work\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| [[APRA Music Awards of 2011|2011]]\n| \"Planet Country\"\n| Country Work of the Year\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| [[APRA Music Awards of 2014|2014]]\n| \"Flying with the King\"\n| Country Work of the Year<ref name=\"CWotYNom\">{{cite web | url = http://apraamcos.com.au/awards/2014-awards/apra-music-awards/country-work-of-the-year/ | title = Country Work of the Year | publisher = Australasian Performing Right Association (APRA) &#124; Australasian Mechanical Copyright Owners Society (AMCOS) | year = 2014 | access-date = 5 March 2016 }}</ref>\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| [[APRA Music Awards of 2020|2020]]\n| \"Backroad Nation\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.noise11.com/news/tones-and-i-leads-nominations-for-2020-virtual-apra-awards-20200407|title= Tones and I Leads Nominations for 2020 Virtual APRA Awards|website=Noise11|date=7 April 2020|access-date=11 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://apraamcos.com.au/awards/2020-awards/apra-music-awards/|title=2020 Awards|website=APRA|date=7 April 2020|access-date=11 April 2020}}</ref>\n| Most Performed Country Work of the Year\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n=== Australian Roll of Renown ===\nThe [[Australian Roll of Renown]] honours Australian and New Zealander musicians who have shaped the music industry by making a significant and lasting contribution to Country Music. It was inaugurated in 1976 and the inductee is announced at the [[Country Music Awards of Australia]] in Tamworth in January.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.tcmf.com.au/roll-of-renown |title=Roll of Renown |publisher=Tamworth Country Music Festival|access-date=29 October 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.tcmf.com.au/What-s-On/Roll-of-Renown/ |title=Roll of Renown |publisher=TCMF |access-date=21 August 2018 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180821093757/https://www.tcmf.com.au/What-s-On/Roll-of-Renown/ |archive-date=21 August 2018 |url-status=dead }}</ref>\n\n{{awards table}}\n|-\n| 2015\n| Lee Kernaghan\n| Australian Roll of Renown\n| {{yes2|inductee}}\n{{end}}\n\n=== Country Music Awards (CMAA) ===\nThe [[Country Music Awards of Australia]] (CMAA) (also known as the Golden Guitar Awards) is an annual awards night held in January during the [[Tamworth Country Music Festival]], celebrating recording excellence in the Australian country music industry. They have been held annually since 1973. Kernaghan has won thirty-eight [[Golden Guitar]] awards at the [[Tamworth, New South Wales|Tamworth]] [[Country Music Awards of Australia]].<ref name=\"CMAA\">{{Cite web Mo Awards (commonly known informally as the [[Mo Awards]]), were annual Australian entertainment industry awards. They recognise achievements in live entertainment in Australia from 1975 to 2016. Lee Kernaghan won five awards in that time.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.moawards.com.au/awardwinners|title=MO Award Winners|website=Mo Awards|access-date=16 March 2022}}</ref>\n{{awards table}} (wins only)\n|-\n|rowspan=\"2\"| 1992 \n| Lee Kernaghan\n| Country Performer of the Year \n| {{won}}\n|-\n| Lee Kernaghan\n| Male Country Entertainer of the Year \n| {{won}}\n|-\n|rowspan=\"2\"| 1993\n| Lee Kernaghan\n| Country Performer of the Year \n| {{won}}\n|-\n| Lee Kernaghan\n| Male Country Entertainer of the Year \n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 1994 \n| Lee Kernaghan\n| Male Country Entertainer of the Year \n| {{won}}\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n=== Music for a New Generation Awards===\nThe Music For A New Generation Awards are run by the [[Planet Country with Big Stu & MJ]] radio program and celebrate crossover country artist efforts each year. The awards have featured fan voting since 2016.\n{{awards table}}\n|-\n| 2015\n| Himself\n| Australian Male Artist of The Year\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| 2017\n| Himself\n| Australian Male Artist of The Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n===Tamworth Songwriters Awards===\nThe Tamworth Songwriters Association (TSA) is an annual songwriting contest for original country songs, awarded in January at the [[Tamworth Country Music Festival]]. They commenced in 1986.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.tsaonline.com.au/song-competition/|title=Tamworth Songwriters Association|website=Tamworth Songwriters Association Online|access-date=23 March 2022}}</ref> Lee Kernaghan has won three awards in that time.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.tsaonline.com.au/past-winners/|title=Tamworth Songwriters Association Past Winners|website=Tamworth Songwriters Association Online|access-date=23 March 2022}}</ref>\n{{awards table}} (wins only)\n|-\n|rowspan=\"2\"| 1993\n|rowspan=\"2\"| \"Boys from the Bush\" by Lee Kernaghan and [[Garth Porter]]\n| Contemporary Country Song of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|- \n| Country Song of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 1996\n| \"1959\" by Lee Kernaghan\n| Contemporary Country Song of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|- \n{{end}}\n\n== References ==\n{{Reflist}}\n\n== External links ==\n{{sister project links|wikt=no|b=no|q=Lee Kernaghan|s=no|commons=Category:Lee Kernaghan|n=no|v=no|species=no}}\n{{Australians of the Year}}\n{{Lee Kernaghan}}\n{{Authority control}}\n\n{{DEFAULTSORT:Kernaghan, Lee}}\n[[Category:1964 births]]\n[[Category:Living people]]\n[[Category:People from Corryong]]\n[[Category:APRA Award winners]]\n[[Category:ARIA Award winners]]\n[[Category:Australian country singer-songwriters]]\n[[Category:Australian male musical theatre actors]]\n[[Category:Australian of the Year Award winners]]\n[[Category:Recipients of the Medal of the Order of Australia]]\n[[Category:Australian country guitarists]]\n[[Category:Australian male guitarists]]\n[[Category:Australian male singer-songwriters]]\n[[Category:Australian singer-songwriters]]\n[[Category:Australian republicans]]"}]}}}}{"batchcomplete":"","warnings":{"main":{"*":"Subscribe to the mediawiki-api-announce mailing list at <https://lists.wikimedia.org/postorius/lists/mediawiki-api-announce.lists.wikimedia.org/> for notice of API deprecations and breaking changes. Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Adam_Brand_(musician)","to":"Adam Brand (musician)"}],"pages":{"13919379":{"pageid":13919379,"ns":0,"title":"Adam Brand (musician)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|Australian country musician|bot=PearBOT 5}}\n{{Use dmy dates|date=August 2020}}\n{{Use Australian English|date=January 2012}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Adam Brand\n| image           = Adam Brand in Melbourne.jpg\n| birth_name      = Adamo Alberto Brun\n| birth_date      = {{birth date and age|1970|01|27|df=yes}}\n| birth_place     = [[Perth, Western Australia]], Australia\n| death_date      =\n| genre           = [[Country music|Country]]\n| occupation      = Singer, songwriter\n| years_active    = 1997\u2013present\n| label           = {{hlist|[[ABC Music]]|[[Flying Nun Records|Flying Nun]]|Compass Brothers|[[Arista Nashville]]}}\n| associated_acts = Hodad City, [[Melinda Schneider]], [[Lee Kernaghan]]\n}}\n\n'''Adam Brand''' (born 27 January 1970) is an Australian country singer-songwriter. Brand released his debut album in 1997. He has since released 14 studio albums and has won 12 [[Country Music Awards of Australia]]. Adam Brand has been voted ''CMC Oz Artist of the Year'' five consecutive years between 2007 \u2013 2011.<ref name=McGee>{{cite web|url=https://mcgeeentertainment.com.au/adam-brand|title=Adam Brand |website=mcgeeentertainment.com.au|date=2013|access-date=8 August 2022}}</ref>\n\n==Early life==\nAdam Brand was born on 27 January 1970 in [[Perth, Western Australia]].<ref name=\":0\">{{Cite web|url=https://www.driverdb.com/drivers/adam-brand/|title=Adam Brand {{!}} Racing career profile {{!}} Driver Database|website=www.driverdb.com|access-date=2016-05-23}}</ref> Brand's first stage appearance was at age 3 singing \"[[(How Much Is) That Doggie in the Window?]]\" with his father Mick at a pub in Perth.<ref name =\"Saucer\">{{cite web|url=https://www.flyingsaucerclub.com.au/gig/adam-brand/|title=Adam Brand \u2013 Up Close & Personal |publisher=Flying Saucer|access-date=24 July 2018}}</ref>\n\nHis love for music was heavily influenced by his father who was a singer and a fan of [[Elvis Presley]].<ref name=McGee/> His mother exposed him to [[Kris Kristofferson]], [[Roy Orbison]] and [[the Everly Brothers]].<ref name=McGee/>\n\nAt age 10, Adam picked up the drum sticks. In his teens, Brand began playing the drums in church bands around [[Colac, Victoria|Colac]] and [[Geelong]] where he was introduced to gospel and developed his lifelong love of rhythm.<ref name=McGee/>\n\n==Career==\n===1997-1999: Career beginnings===\nIn January 1997, Brand began busking on Peel Street, [[Tamworth, New South Wales|Tamworth]] which led to his first record deal with [[Festival Mushroom Records]] which he signed in September 1997.<ref name =\"Saucer\"/> In July 1998, Brand released his debut [[Adam Brand (album)|self-titled studio album]], which peaked at number 44 on the Australian [[Australian Recording Industry Association|ARIA]] album charts<ref name=\"Charts\">{{cite web|url=http://australian-charts.com/search.asp?cat=a&artist=adam+brand&artist_search=starts&title=&title_search=starts| title=Adam Brand|publisher=Australian-charts.com|access-date=27 January 2010}}</ref> and was certified [[List of music recording certifications|platinum]].<ref name=\"Accred\">{{cite web|url=http://www.aria.com.au/pages/ARIACharts-Accreditations-2006Albums.htm |title=ARIA Charts \u2013 Accreditations \u2013 2006 Albums |publisher=[[Australian Recording Industry Association|ARIA]] |access-date=27 January 2010 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20100204044318/http://www.aria.com.au/pages/ARIACharts-Accreditations-2006Albums.htm |archive-date=4 February 2010 |url-status=dead}}</ref> At the 1999 [[Country Music Awards of Australia|CMAA awards]], Brand won three [[Golden Guitars]]; Song of the Year, New Talent of the Year and Video of the Year.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.country.com.au/index.cfm?page_id=1134 |title=Country Music Awards of Australia 1990\u20131999 |publisher=[[Country Music Association of Australia|CMAA]] |access-date=27 January 2010 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20091017180321/http://www.country.com.au/index.cfm?page_id=1134 |archive-date=17 October 2009 }}</ref> The album was nominated for [[ARIA Award for Best Country Album]] at the [[ARIA Music Awards of 1999|1999 ARIA Music Awards]].<ref name=\"ARIA\">{{cite web|url=http://www.ariaawards.com.au/history-by-artist.php?letter=A&artist=Adam%20Brand|title=ARIA Award History \u2013 Adam Brand|publisher=[[Australian Recording Industry Association]]|access-date=29 January 2010}}{{Dead link|date=September 2019 |bot=InternetArchiveBot |fix-attempted=yes }}</ref> Brand won the '[[Johnny O'Keefe]] Encouragement Award' at the [[Mo Awards]] in July 1999.\n\n===2000\u20132005: Career Establishment===\nIn January 2000, Brand won his fourth CMAA Award for Vocal Collaboration of the Year with [[Melinda Schneider]] for \"Love Away the Night\".<ref name=\"CMAA\">{{cite web|url=http://www.country.com.au/index.cfm?page_id=1135 |title=Country Music Awards of Australia 2000\u20132008 |publisher=[[Country Music Association of Australia|CMAA]] |access-date=27 January 2010 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20091017175108/http://www.country.com.au/index.cfm?page_id=1135 |archive-date=17 October 2009}}</ref> In March 2000, Brand released his second studio album ''[[Good Friends (Adam Brand album)|Good Friends]]'' which peaked at number 26 on the ARIA charts.<ref name=\"Charts\"/> The album was nominated for Best Country Album at the [[ARIA Music Awards of 2000|2000 ARIA Awards]].<ref name=\"ARIA\"/> In January 2001, Brand won three more CMAA Awards; Album of the Year, Male Vocalist of the Year and Song of the Year.<ref name=\"CMAA\"/> He also won a Mo Award for Male Country Performer of the Year.\n\nIn January 2002, Brand released his third studio album ''[[Built for Speed (Adam Brand album)|Built for Speed]]'' which peaked at number 24 ARIA charts<ref name=\"Charts\"/> and was certified platinum in Australia.<ref name=\"Accred\"/><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.aria.com.au/pages/httpwww.aria.com.aupagesARIACharts-Accreditations-2009Albums.htm|title=ARIA Charts \u2013 Accreditations \u2013 2009 Albums|publisher=[[Australian Recording Industry Association|ARIA]] |access-date=27 January 2010| archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20100204015724/http://aria.com.au/pages/httpwww.aria.com.aupagesARIACharts-Accreditations-2009Albums.htm| archive-date= 4 February 2010 | url-status= live}}</ref> Brand won a further Mo Award for Male Country Performer of the Year. In January 2003, \"The Anzac\" won the CMAA Award for Heritage Song of the Year, Brand's eighth CMA Award overall.<ref name =\"Saucer\"/> In 2003, Brand contributed the tracks \"Sicilian Born\" and \"Menindee\" to the compilation album ''Australian Storytellers''. Both songs received CMA Awards nominations.\n\nIn August 2004, Brand released his fourth studio album ''[[Get Loud]]'', which debuted at number 16 on the ARIA charts,<ref name=\"Charts\"/> was certified Gold and earned Brand's third ARIA Award nomination for Best Country Album.<ref name=\"ARIA\"/> In October 2005 Brand released a [[Christmas music|Christmas album]] titled ''[[Christmas in Australia (album)|Christmas in Australia]]''.\n\n===2006\u20132009: Continued Success and ''Dancing with the Stars''===\nIn July 2006, Brand released his sixth studio album ''[[What a Life (Adam Brand album)|What a Life]]'' which peaked at number 28 on the ARIA charts<ref name=\"Charts\"/> and was certified Gold.<ref name=\"Accred\"/> Brand received another ARIA nomination for 'Best Country Album' at the [[ARIA Music Awards of 2006]].<ref name=\"ARIA\"/> In January 2007 Brand is awarded the inaugural [[Country Music Channel]] Oz Artist of the Year Award.<ref name=\"auto\">{{cite web | url = https://www.countrymusicchannel.com.au/cmc-music-awards-2011 | title = CMC Music Awards 2011 | publisher = [[Country Music Channel]] (CMC) | access-date = 1 April 2018 }}</ref> In January 2008, Brand won three more CMA Awards for his song \"[[Spirit of the Bush (song)|Spirit of the Bush]]\" with [[Lee Kernaghan]] and [[Steve Forde]].<ref name=\"CMAA\"/> In January 2008, Brand released his seventh studio album ''[[Blame It on Eve]]'' which became Brand's first ARIA top ten album.<ref name=\"Charts\"/> In September 2008, Brand's first [[compilation album]] ''[[Greatest Hits 1998\u20132008]]'' was released. In January 2009 Brand wins his third consecutive CMC Oz Artist of the Year Award and his twelfth CMA Award when he won Male Artist of the Year.<ref name =\"Saucer\"/> In March 2009 Brand released his eighth studio album ''[[Hell of a Ride]]'', which peaked at number 19 on ARIA charts.<ref name=\"Charts\"/> In March 2009, Brand was the lead act at the [[Black Saturday bushfires|Victorian Bushfire Appeal]] concert in [[Traralgon]].\n\nFrom July to September 2009, Brand competed the [[Dancing with the Stars (Australian season 9)|ninth season]] of [[Dancing with the Stars (Australian TV series)|Dancing with the Stars (Australia)]] and was declared the winner on 6 September 2009.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.smh.com.au/entertainment/adam-brand-wins-dancing-with-the-stars-finale-20090907-fdcw.html|title=Adam Brand wins Dancing with the Stars finale |work=[[The Sydney Morning Herald]]|date=7 September 2009 |access-date=24 July 2018}}</ref> Brand partnered professional dancer [[Jade Hatcher]], whom he married on 31 May 2010.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.adelaidenow.com.au/entertainment/celebrity/country-singer-adam-brands-18-months-marriage-to-dancing-with-the-stars-dancer-jade-hatcher-in-break-up/story-e6fredq3-1226227888098?sv=4c98efefd65aeb0e3d13554389f60b85&nk=548c9950a8edaa17540736c41e58fa0e-1532414957|title=Country singer Adam Brand's 18-months marriage to Dancing With the Stars dancer Jade Hatcher in break-up |work=The Advertiser|location=Adelaide|date=21 December 2011 |access-date=24 July 2018}}</ref>\n\nIn September 2009 Brand signed a recording contract with Arista Records, the [[Nashville]]-based division of [[Sony Music Entertainment]] for the distribution of his recordings in the United States.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.news.com.au/entertainment/music/adam-brand-signs-us-recording-deal-will-compete-in-dancing-with-the-stars-final/news-story/3e409ccec2f2b6a38360f4d6fed98e30|title=Adam Brand signs US recording deal; will compete in Dancing with the Stars final |publisher=[[news.com.au]]|date=5 September 2009|access-date=24 July 2018}}</ref><ref name=McGee/>\n\n===2010\u2013present: Adam Brand label ===\nIn January 2010 Brand won his fourth consecutive CMC Oz Artist of the Year Award. In August 2010, Brand released his ninth studio album ''[[It's Gonna Be OK (album)|It's Gonna Be OK]]'' which peaked at number 11 on the ARIA charts.<ref name=\"Charts\"/> The Track \"Ready for Loving\" was released in the United States and reached the Top 40 in the US Country charts.<ref name =\"Saucer\"/> In January 2011, Brand won CMC Oz Artist of the Year Award for the fifth consecutive year. In May 2011, Brand released a compilation album titled ''[[You're a Revhead]]'' before supporting [[Taylor Swift]] on her North American tour.<ref name =\"Saucer\"/>\n\nIn August 2012, Brand released his tenth studio album ''[[There Will Be Love]]'' on [[Arista Nashville]]/[[Sony Music Australia]], which peaked at number 4 on the ARIA charts; Brand's highest-charting album.<ref name=\"Charts\"/> This was followed by ''[[My Acoustic Diary]]'' which was the first album recorded by Brand's own label. It was distributed by [[Australian Broadcasting Corporation|ABC Music]]. The album saw Brand re-record 13 of his own tracks in an acoustic setting. Upon release, Brand said \"I have decided to re-record some of these diary entries acoustically, the way they were first written\u2026 I've chosen songs that represent pivotal points in my life, and my growth as a songwriter and as an artist trying to find my own voice.\"<ref name=McGee/>\n\nBrand's twelfth studio album ''[[My Side of the Street]]'' was released in August 2014, became his second top 5 album. It was nominated for an ARIA Award and two CMA Awards. In January 2015, Brand won CMC Oz Artist of the Year Award for a fifth year.\n\nIn January 2016, Brand released his thirteenth studio album ''[[Adam Brand and the Outlaws]]'', featuring fellow Australian country musicians [[Travis Collins]], [[Drew McAlister]], [[Baby Animals|Matt Cornell]] and Mike Carr.<ref>{{Cite web|title = Introducing the new Aussie supergroup: Adam Brand and the Outlaws {{!}} CMC|url = http://www.countrymusicchannel.com.au/news/introducing-the-new-aussie-supergroup-adam-brand-and-the-outlaws.aspx|website = www.countrymusicchannel.com.au|access-date = 2016-01-13|archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20160122043842/http://www.countrymusicchannel.com.au/news/introducing-the-new-aussie-supergroup-adam-brand-and-the-outlaws.aspx|archive-date = 22 January 2016|url-status = dead|df = dmy-all}}</ref> The album peaked at number 6 on the ARIA charts<ref name=\"Charts\"/> and was nominated for an ARIA Award. The album won a CMC Award for Highest Selling Album. In February 2017, Brand released ''[[Get On Your Feet (album)|Get On Your Feet]]'' which peaked at number 7 on the ARIA charts.<ref name=\"Charts\"/>\n\nIn July 2018, Brand celebrated 20 years since the release of his debut album releasing a compilation album titled ''[[Milestones... 20 Years]]''. The album debuted at number 6 on the ARIA charts, becoming his highest charting compilation album.<ref name=\"Charts\"/> In September 2018 Brand joined [[Scott Darlow]], [[Sarah McLeod (musician)|Sarah McLeod]], [[Irwin Thomas|Jack Jones]] and [[Todd Hunter]] to re-record the [[Dragon (band)|Dragon]] song \"[[Rain (Dragon song)|Rain]]\" with all net proceeds from the sale to go towards to the Buy-a-bale program in support of Australian farmers suffering from the [[2018 in Australia#August|Australian drought]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.triplem.com.au/music/news/welcome-to-the-drought-breakers-australia-s-newest-band-raising-money-for-the-farmers|title=Welcome to the Drought Breakers- Australia's Newest Band Raising Money for the Farmers |publisher=Triple M|date=14 September 2018 |access-date=14 September 2018}}</ref>\n\nIn late 2019, Brand appeared in the first season of [[The Masked Singer (Australian TV series)|The Masked Singer Australia]] as the 'Dragon' and was the sixth contestant voted out.<ref>{{cite web|last=Morgan|first=Michaela|title='I Don't Believe It': Only Dannii Guessed The Dragon's Real Identity|url=https://10daily.com.au/entertainment/tv/a191008lbfwy/i-dont-believe-it-only-dannii-guessed-the-dragons-real-identity-20191008|website=10 Daily|date=8 October 2019|access-date=8 October 2019}}</ref>\n\nIn August 2019 Brand released a new single \"Life's Been Good to Me\" after taking 12 months off to start a family with the birth of his first child, a baby girl named Pepper.<ref>{{cite web |title=Adam Brand releases new single Life's Been Good to Me and talks about being a new father 30 August 2019 |url=https://www.northerndailyleader.com.au/story/6337556/adam-brand-rejigs-the-priority-list-as-he-settles-into-fatherhood/ |website=The Northern Daily Leader |date=30 August 2019 |access-date=19 October 2019}}</ref> Adam will be hitting the road with his Speed of Life Tour March 2020 when he will release his new album.<ref>{{cite web |title=The Masked Singer: Country music star Adam Brand revealed as the face behind the dragon head. The Daily Telegraph Confidential 09 October 2019 |url=https://www.dailytelegraph.com.au/entertainment/sydney-confidential/the-masked-singer-country-music-star-adam-brand-revealed-as-the-face-behind-the-dragon-head/news-story/0086d9fb3a3f764d4f3abbc9038c54dc |website=The Daily Telegraph}}</ref> Special guests on the tour will be new country duo \"Cornell & Carr\". Matt Cornell and Mike Carr were previously members of [[Adam Brand and the Outlaws]].<ref>{{cite web |title=Speed of Life Tour |url=https://www.bandsintown.com/e/101606578?affil_code=js_www.adambrandmusic.com&app_id=js_www.adambrandmusic.com&came_from=242 |website=Bandsintown |access-date=19 October 2019 |ref=\"Brand is back and he's bringing the good times with him\"}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=Kix Country Music. Country Confidential CORNELL & CARR interview\u2013 12th September 2019 |url=https://www.kixcountry.com.au/country-confidential/394-shows/luke-crossy-cross/interviews/47675-cornell-carr-12th-september-2019 |website=Kixcountry.com.au |date=13 September 2019 |access-date=19 October 2019}}</ref>\n\n==Personal life==\nBrand is a fan of motor sport.<ref name=\":0\" /> His song \"Dirt Track Cowboys\" is themed around speedway racing and features speedway commentator Wade Aunger. Brand has also raced, spending several years racing in the [[V8 Utes]] category racing Ford Falcon V8s in the early 2000s.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.v8utes.com.au/index.php?page_id=1398|title=Brand to perform V8 Ute backing track at Deni Ute Muster|last=Bain|first=Erin|website=v8utes.com.au|publisher=V8 Utes Racing Series|access-date=2011-12-26}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.fords.com.au/article/Adam-Brand-Joins-Ford-Credit-Racing |title=Adam Brand Joins Ford Credit Racing |date=1 June 2002 |publisher=Fords Online Magazine |access-date=2011-12-26 |archive-url=https://archive.today/20120731035237/http://www.fords.com.au/article/Adam-Brand-Joins-Ford-Credit-Racing |archive-date=31 July 2012 |url-status=dead}}</ref> Brand made a return to racing in 2011, competing in the [[2011 Eastern Creek Six Hour]]. Brand and his co-drivers won their class racing a Suzuki Swift.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.transtasmanmotorsport.com/#/news1-101211/4558500616 |title=Simpson shines as the stars rock the Swift field at Eastern Creek |date=10 December 2011 |work=Australian Swift Racing Series |publisher=Trans Tasman Motorsport |access-date=2011-12-26 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120426072159/http://www.transtasmanmotorsport.com/#/news1-101211/4558500616 |archive-date=26 April 2012 |url-status=dead }}</ref>\n\nHe has been married and divorced three times. At the age of 39 he met [[Jade Hatcher]], then 19, on the set of ''[[Dancing with the Stars]]'' in 2009. They went on to win the competition despite a lower score compared to their competitor, ''[[Today Tonight]]'' presenter [[Matthew White (journalist)|Matt White]]. Brand and Hatcher married in May 2010,<ref>{{cite web|title=Country singer Adam Brand's 18-months marriage to Dancing With the Stars dancer Jade Hatcher in break-up|url=http://www.dailytelegraph.com.au/entertainment/sydney-confidential/country-singer-adam-brands-18-months-marriage-to-dancing-with-the-stars-dancer-jade-hatcher-in-break-up/story-e6frewz0-1226227888098|work=The Daily Telegraph|access-date=28 December 2011}}</ref> but in late 2011 it was announced that they had separated.<ref>{{cite web|title=Adam Brand and Jade Hatcher part after two years|url=http://www.news.com.au/entertainment/television/adam-brand-and-jade-hatcher-part-after-two-years/story-e6frfmyi-1226228153701|work=Herald Sun|access-date=28 December 2011}}</ref> They later divorced.{{citation needed|date=April 2020}}\n\nIn 2019, Brand became a father for the first time, after his partner gave birth to daughter Pepper.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.nowtolove.com.au/reality-tv/the-masked-singer/the-masked-singer-adam-brand-baby-59664|title=The Masked Singer: Adam Brand fatherhood |website= Now To Love|date=October 2019|access-date=8 August 2022}}</ref>\n\nBrand's partner gave birth to a second baby in August 2022.<ref name=Iwantedtofeelfreedom>{{cite web|url=https://liveatyourlocal.com.au/2022/08/05/adam-brand-i-wanted-to-feel-freedom/|title= Adam Brand: \"I Wanted to Feel Freedom\"|website=Live at Your Local|date=5 August 2022|access-date=8 August 2022}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n{{main|Adam Brand discography}}\n\n* ''[[Adam Brand (album)|Adam Brand]]'' (1998)\n* ''[[Good Friends (Adam Brand album)|Good Friends]]'' (2000)\n* ''[[Built nominations==\n===AIR Awards===\nThe Australian Independent Record Awards (commonly known informally as [[AIR Awards]]) is an annual awards night to recognise, promote and celebrate the success of and New Zealand by the [[Australasian Performing Right Association]] to recognise songwriting skills, sales and airplay performance by its members annually. Brand has been nominated nine times.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://apraamcos.com.au/search?searchtype=site&keywords=adam+brand|title=Search Results Adam Brand|publisher=APRA AMCOS|access-date=24 July 2018}}</ref>\n\n{{awards table}}\n|-\n| 1999\n| \"Last Man Standing\" \n| rowspan=\"5\"| Most Performed Country Work \n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| 2000\n| \"Dirt Track Cowboys\" \n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| 2001\n| \"Beating Around the Bush\" \n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| [[APRA Awards of 2002|2002]]\n| \"Good Things in Life\" \n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| [[APRA Awards of 2003|2003]]\n| \"New England Highway\" \n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| [[APRA Awards of 2008|2008]]\n| \"[[Spirit of the Bush (song)|Spirit of the Bush]]\" <small>([[Lee Kernaghan]] featuring Adam Brand and [[Steve Forde]])</small> \n| rowspan=\"4\"| Country Work of the Year \n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| [[APRA Awards of 2009|2009]]\n| \"Coming From / [[Khe Sanh]]\"\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| [[APRA Awards of 2010|2010]]\n| \"Hell of a Ride\" \n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| 2015\n| \"Freedom Rebels\" \n| {{nom}}\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n===ARIA Music Awards===\nThe [[ARIA Music Awards]] is an annual awards ceremony that recognises excellence, innovation, and achievement across all genres of [[Australian music]]. Brand has been nominated seven times.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.ariaawards.com.au/search?term=adam%20brand|title= Adam Brand ARIA Awards search|publisher=ARIA Awards|access-date=24 July 2018}}</ref>\n\n{{awards table}}\n|-\n| [[ARIA Music Awards of 1999|1999]]\n| ''Adam Brand''\n| rowspan=\"7\"| [[ARIA Award for Best Country Album|Best Country Album]]\n| {{nominated}} \n|-\n| [[ARIA Music Awards of 2000|2000]]\n| ''Good Friends''\n| {{nominated}} \n|-\n| [[ARIA Music Awards of 2004|2004]]\n| ''Get Loud''\n| {{nominated}}\n|-\n| [[ARIA Music Awards of 2006|2006]]\n| ''What a Life''\n| {{nominated}} \n|-\n| [[ARIA Music Awards of 2014|2014]]\n| ''My Side of the Street''\n| {{nominated}} \n|-\n| [[ARIA Music Awards of 2016|2016]]\n| ''Adam Brand and the Outlaws''\n| {{nominated}} \n|-\n| [[2022 ARIA Music Awards|2022]]<ref name=\"2022ARIAnoms\">{{cite web|url=https://themusicnetwork.com/2022-aria-awards-nominees/|title=R\u00fcf\u00fcs Du Sol Leads 2022 ARIA Awards Nominees (Full List)|website=The Music Network|date=12 October 2022|access-date=12 October 2022|author=Lars Brandle}}</ref>\n| ''All Or Nothing''\n| {{nominated}} \n|-\n{{end}}\n\n===CMC Awards===\nThe [[Country Music Channel]] (CMC Awards) are an annual fan voted award ceremony. From 2007 to 2010, The CMC awarded only one category, The Oz Artist of the Year, which Brand won four years in a row. The CMC Awards officially commenced in 2011, with four categories in total.<ref name=\"auto\"/> Brand has won 11 awards in total.\n\n{{awards table}}\n|-\n| 2007\n| rowspan=\"6\"| Adam Brand\n| rowspan=\"6\"| Oz Artist of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 2008\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 2009\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 2010\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 2011\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| rowspan=\"2\"| 2015\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| Adam Brand \u2013 \"What Your Love Looks Like\"\n| Video of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 2016\n| Adam Brand\n| Oz Artist of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 2017\n| Adam Brand and the Outlaws \u2013 ''Adam Brand and the Outlaws''\n| ARIA Highest Selling Album\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| rowspan=\"3\"| 2018\n| rowspan=\"2\"| Adam Brand\n| Oz Artist of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| Male Artist of the Year\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| Adam Brand \u2013 \"Drunk\"\n| Video of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n===CMA Awards===\nThe [[Country Music Awards of Australia]] is an annual awards night held in January during the [[Tamworth Country Music Festival]], celebrating recording excellence in the [[Australian country music]] industry. They commenced in 2006.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.queenslandmusicawards.com.au/about/ |title=About the Queensland Music Awards |publisher=[[Queensland Music Awards]] |access-date=21 March 2021}}</ref>\n\n{{Awards table}}\n! {{Abbr|Ref.|Reference}}\n|-\n! scope=\"row\"| 2023\n| ''All Or Nothing''\n| Highest Selling Album of the Year\n| {{Won}}\n| <ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.abc.net.au/news/2023-03-29/queensland-music-awards-thelma-plum-ball-park-music/102155630|title= Thelma Plum, Ball Park Music win top gongs at 2023 Queensland Music Awards|website=[[Australian Broadcasting Corporation]]|date=29 March 2023|access-date=30 March 2023}}</ref>\n|}\n\n===Tamworth Songwriters Awards===\nThe Tamworth Songwriters Association (TSA) is an annual songwriting contest for original country songs, awarded in January at the [[Tamworth Country Music Festival]]. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"The_Sunny_Cowgirls","to":"The Sunny Cowgirls"}],"pages":{"20950298":{"pageid":20950298,"ns":0,"title":"The Sunny Cowgirls","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|Australian country music group}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name             = The Sunny Cowgirls\n| image            = \n| caption          = \n| image_size       = \n| background       = group_or_band\n| origin           = [[Hamilton, Victoria]], [[Australia]]\n| genre            = [[Country music|Country]]\n| years_active     = 2005\u2013present\n| label            = Compass Bros.<br />MSI<br />Phantom Sound and Vision\n| associated_acts  = \n| website          = www.sunnycowgirls.com.au\n| current_members  = Sophie Clabburn<br />Celeste Clabburn\n}}\n\n'''The Sunny Cowgirls''' is an Australian [[country music]] group formed in 2005. They have released a total of seven studio albums since 2005. Their debut album, ''Little Bit Rusty'', was released in 2005. Their latest album, ''Here We Go'', was released in September 2016.\n\n==Biography==\nThe Sunny Cowgirls, Sophie and Celeste Clabburn, grew up on a farm in [[Hamilton, Victoria]]. The Clabburn sisters were raised on \"Sunninghill\", the family farm at [[Dunkeld]] near Hamilton, Victoria, before the whole family moved to [[Perth]], [[Western Australia]] when they were primary school kids. Their farm was in their father's family a long while, and that's where they came up with the name \"Sunny\".<ref>[http://www.sunnycowgirls.com.au/ Sunny Cowgirls official site]</ref> After four years of working around the country and doing the occasional gig, they raised enough cash to approach well-known Perth record producer Mark Donohoe to showcase their writing and music.\n\nThe Cowgirls lives and careers changed in early 2005 when they secured places as aspiring artists in the CMAA College of Country Music, held before the [[Tamworth Country Music Festival]] each year. They then signed with Compass Bros Records and their first album, ''Little Bit Rusty'', reached No.&nbsp;4 on the [[Australian Recording Industry Association|ARIA]] country charts.\n \nThe Sunny Cowgirls have also collaborated with [[Adam Brand (musician)|Adam Brand]] on \"Someday\".{{when|date=November 2020}}\n\nOn 1 September 2012 The Sunny Cowgirls performed at the 25th [[Trundle, New South Wales|Trundle]] Bush Tucker Day.\n\n==Discography==\n===Studio albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\" \n|+ List of studio albums, with selected details chart positions\n!
