They have been held annually since 1973.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.country.com.au/awards/past-award-winners|title=Past Award Winners|accessdate=2 November 2020}}</ref>\n{{awards table}}\n|-\n| 2011\n| The Sunny Cowgirls\n| Horizon Award\n| {{won}}\n{{end}}\n* Note: wins only\n\n==References==\n{{reflist|2}}\n\n{{Authority control}}\n\n{{DEFAULTSORT:Sunny Cowgirls}}\n[[Category:Australian country music groups]]\n[[Category:Country music duos]]\n[[Category:Sibling musical duos]]\n[[Category:Musical groups established in 2005]]"}]}}}}{"batchcomplete":"","warnings":{"main":{"*":"Subscribe to the mediawiki-api-announce mailing list at <https://lists.wikimedia.org/postorius/lists/mediawiki-api-announce.lists.wikimedia.org/> for notice of API deprecations and breaking changes. Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Kasey_Chambers","to":"Kasey Chambers"}],"pages":{"709012":{"pageid":709012,"ns":0,"title":"Kasey Chambers","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|Australian rock singer-songwriter and musician (born 1976)}}\n{{Use dmy dates|date=November 2019}}\n{{Use Australian English|date=May 2011}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name             = Kasey Chambers\n| image            = Kasey Chambers at APRA Music Awards 2012 (cropped).jpg\n| image_upright    = \n| image_size       = \n| landscape        = \n| caption          = Chambers in 2012\n| background       = solo_singer\n| birth_name       = \n| alias            = \n| birth_date       = {{Birth date and age|df=y|1976|6|4}}\n| birth_place      = [[Mount Gambier, South Australia]], Australia\n| origin           = [[Adelaide]], [[South Australia]], Australia\n| death_date       = <!-- {{Death date and age|df=y|YYYY|MM|DD|YYYY|MM|DD}} (death date first) -->\n| death_place      = \n| genre            = [[Australian country music|Country]]\n| occupation       = Musician\n| instrument       = {{flatlist|\n* Vocals\n* guitar\n* banjo\n}}\n| years_active     = 1987\u2013present\n| label            = {{flatlist|\n* [[EMI Music Australia|EMI]]\n* [[Asylum Records|Asylum]]\n* Essence\n* [[Warner Bros. Records|Warner Bros.]]\n* [[Liberation Music|Liberation]]/[[Sugar Hill Records (bluegrass)|Sugar Hill]]\n}}\n| past_member_of = [[Dead Ringer Band]]\n| website          = {{URL|kaseychambers.com/}}\n}}\n\n'''Kasey Chambers''' (born 4 June 1976) is an [[Australian country music|Australian country singer-songwriter and musician]] born in [[Mount Gambier, South Australia|Mount Gambier]] to fellow musicians Diane and [[Bill Chambers (musician)|Bill Chambers]]. Her older brother is musician and producer [[Nash Chambers]]. All four were members of family country-music group [[Dead Ringer Band]] in Bowral, New South Wales from 1992 to 1998; Chambers launched her solo career thereafter. Five of her twelve studio albums have reached No.&nbsp;1 on the [[ARIA Charts|ARIA Albums Chart]], ''[[Barricades & Brickwalls]]'' (September 2001), ''[[Wayward Angel]]'' (May 2004), ''[[Carnival (Kasey Chambers album)|Carnival]]'' (August 2006) ''[[Rattlin' Bones]]'' (April 2008), and ''[[Dragonfly (Kasey Chambers album)|Dragonfly]]'' (January 2017). In November [[ARIA Music Awards of 2018|2018]] she was inducted into the [[ARIA Hall of Fame]] and has won an additional 14 [[ARIA Music Awards]] with nine for [[ARIA Award for Best Country Album|Best Country Album]]. Her autobiography, ''A Little Bird Told Me...'', co-authored with music journalist Jeff Apter, was released in 2011.\n\n==Dead Ringer Band==\n{{main|Dead Ringer Band}}\nKasey Chambers was born in 1976 in Mount Gambier, South Australia to Diane and Bill Chambers.<ref name=\"McFarlane\"/><ref name=\"SMH 2009\"/><ref name=\"Kasey Hands\"/> Her older brother, Nash Chambers, was born in 1974.<ref name=\"Nimmervoll\"/> From July 1976 the Chambers family travelled around the [[Nullarbor Plain]], where the parents hunted foxes and rabbits for pelts during seven or eight months a year, spanning nine years.<ref name=\"Hands 98\"/><ref name=\"AMG Ringer\"/> During the \"hot months\" (generally from November to March) they returned to [[Southend, South Australia]],<ref name=\"Nimmervoll\"/><ref name=\"Hands 98\"/> where her family owned a [[fish and chips|fish and chip]] shop for a time.\n\nFrom 1986 Bill and Diane returned to performing as a country-music duo while their children attended school in Southend.<ref name=\"Nimmervoll\"/> In the following year their parents added first Chambers and then Nash to their act, which became the [[Dead Ringer Band]] \u2013 named for the children looking like their parents.<ref name=\"McFarlane\"/><ref name=\"AMG Ringer\"/><ref name=\"abcnews\"/> Chambers was recorded on vocals for two albums released under Bill's name, ''Sea Eagle'' (1987) and ''Kindred Spirit'' (1991). From 1992 Dead Ringer Band released an extended play and four albums.<ref name=\"McFarlane\"/><ref name=\"AMG\"/> For their first album, ''Red Desert Sky'' (November 1993), she was named as Kasey Jo Chambers, provided vocals and wrote four of its tracks.<ref name=\"NLA Red\"/><ref name=\"AMG RedDesert\"/> It was co-produced by the group with Eddie Sikorski at John Reynolds Recording Studio, [[Adelaide]].<ref name=\"NLA Red\"/><ref name=\"AMG RedDesert\"/>\n\nChambers met fellow country singer-songwriter [[Beccy Cole]] in mid-1989 in Adelaide, and she joined Dead Ringer Band on a tour through New South Wales before going solo.<ref name=\"AusStory Jul12\"/> Chambers later recalled, \"I never really met anyone at this point in my life that was of the same generation as me \u2013 a young girl who liked country music. And funnily enough the first song that I ever wrote in my life was called 'Beccy', about Beccy. It's the worst song you've ever heard in your whole life.\"<ref name=\"AusStory Jul12\"/> She cited [[Emmylou Harris]] as one of her primary influences, recalling that her parents had frequently Harris' music throughout her childhood.<ref name=\"Ryan\"/> The group ended when Chambers' parents divorced in the late 1990s, Diane moved to [[Norfolk Island]], and Bill moved to Sydney.<ref name=\"AMG\"/><ref name=\"Age Oct02\"/>\n\n==Solo career==\n===1998\u20132002: ''The Captain'' to ''Barricades & Brickwalls''===\nChambers recorded her debut solo album, ''[[The Captain (album)|The Captain]]'', on Norfolk Island during July and August 1998 with her brother Nash producing and father Bill on guitar.<ref name=\"McFarlane\"/><ref name=\"Nimmervoll\"/> United States country musicians, [[Buddy Miller|Buddy]] and [[Julie Miller]] added guitars and vocals to four tracks. ''The Captain'' was released in May 1999 via [[EMI Music Australia]] and in June 2000 in the US by [[Asylum Records]]. It peaked at No.&nbsp;11 on the [[ARIA Charts|ARIA Albums Chart]] and No.&nbsp;1 on the related ARIA Country Albums chart.<ref name=\"AUS\"/> At the [[ARIA Music Awards of 1999]] she won [[ARIA Award for Best Country Album|Best Country Album]] and in the [[ARIA Music Awards of 2000|following year]] she won [[ARIA Award for Best Female Artist|Best Female Artist]] for its [[The Captain (Kasey Chambers song)|title track]], which was issued in 2000.<ref name=\"ARIA list\"/>\n\n''The Captain'' was certified double platinum for shipment of 140,000 copies by [[Australian Recording Industry Association]] (ARIA) in 2001.<ref name=\"ARIA Cert01 Albs\"/> It reached the top&nbsp;50 of the ''Billboard'' Top Country Albums in 2001.<ref name=\"Billb CountryA\"/> She toured the US as a support act to [[Lucinda Williams]] and later supported Emmylou Harris on the Australian leg of that artist's tour. \"The Captain\" was played in episode 8 (\"[[He Is Risen (The Sopranos)|He Is Risen]]\") of the third season of ''[[The Sopranos (season 3)|The Sopranos]]'', in April 2001.\n\nChambers' second studio album, ''[[Barricades & Brickwalls]]'', was released in September 2001 via EMI Music, which was also produced by Nash.<ref name=\"NLA Barricades\"/> It debuted at No.&nbsp;4 in the ARIA Albums Chart and peaked at No.&nbsp;1 in February of the following year.<ref name=\"McFarlane\"/><ref name=\"AUS\"/> Its third single, \"[[Not Pretty Enough]]\" (January 2002), also peaked at No.&nbsp;1 on the related ARIA Singles Chart in the same month.<ref name=\"McFarlane\"/><ref name=\"AUS\"/> The track was written by Chambers and according to Australian musicologist, [[Ian McFarlane]], \"[it's] about being ignored by commercial radio.\"<ref name=\"McFarlane\"/> He cited her autobiography, ''A Little Bird Told Me'' (2011), \"'I wrote [it] as a song about feeling invisible... it was obvious that out in the music industry there was only one path for most young women \u2013 over-sexualised and over made up. To succeed you needed to look like Britney or Shakira.\"<ref name=\"McFarlane\"/>\n\nShe is the first Australian country music artist to have simultaneous No.&nbsp;1 single and album. Subsequent singles \"[[Million Tears]]\" (June 2002) and \"[[If I Were You (Kasey Chambers song)|If I Were You]]\" (October) also made the top&nbsp;40.<ref name=\"AUS\"/> At the [[ARIA Music Awards of 2002]] she won three categories, [[ARIA Award for Album of the Year|Album of the Year]], Best Female Artist and Best Country Album, for ''Barricades & Brickwalls''.<ref name=\"ARIA list\"/> It was certified seven times platinum in 2003 for shipment of at least 490,000 copies.<ref name=\"ARIA Creds03A\"/> In February 2002 it was released in the US, which peaked at No.&nbsp;104 on the [[Billboard 200|''Billboard'' 200]], topping the related Heatseeker Chart and reaching the top&nbsp;20 of their country music chart. It received \"generally favorable reviews\" according to aggregate site, [[Metacritic]], with a rating of 74% from 12 critics.<ref name=\"Metacritic\"/>\n\nAustralian music journalist [[Ed Nimmervoll]] compared it to her first album, \"The musical cast remains essentially the same as ''The Captain'' with the addition of a 'rock' component via drummer Peter Luscombe and rhythm guitarist Dave Steel, and a guest appearance from 'punkabilly' band the Living End. The album also features appearances from Paul Kelly and American country's Lucinda Williams.\"<ref name=\"Nimmervoll\"/> Nimmervoll cited Chambers' observation, \"The last album showed my life story. That was Introducing Kasey Chambers. This one's The Many Moods of Kasey Chambers.\"<ref name=\"Nimmervoll\"/>\n\n===2003\u20132007: ''Wayward Angel'' to ''Carnival''===\nChambers recorded a cover version of Cyndi Lauper's \"[[True Colors (Cyndi Lauper song)|True Colours]]\" (April 2003), which peaked at No.&nbsp;4 on the ARIA Singles Chart <ref name=\"McFarlane\"/><ref name=\"AUS\"/> and was used as the theme song for the [[Rugby Union World Cup|Rugby World Cup]] in that year.<ref name=\"McFarlane\"/> Her rendition reached No.&nbsp;76 on the End of Year Top&nbsp;100 Singles for 2003,<ref name=\"EoY 03S\"/> and was certified as a gold record for shipment of 35,000.<ref name=\"ARIA Creds03S\"/> At the [[APRA Music Awards of 2003]] Chambers won three categories with \"Not Pretty Enough\" named as Song of the Year, Most Performed Australian Work and Most Performed Country Work.<ref name=\"APRA List\"/>\n[[File:Chambers, Canberra, Nov 2006.jpg|thumb|160px|Chambers at the Royal Theatre, Canberra, November 2006|alt=She is shown in upper-body shot and left profile. She has her eyes closed as she sings into a microphone and plays her guitar.]]\nShe released her third solo album, ''[[Wayward Angel]]'', in May 2004, which debuted at No.&nbsp;1 on the ARIA Albums Chart and remained at the top position for five&nbsp;weeks.<ref name=\"McFarlane\"/><ref name=\"AUS\"/> It was accredited triple platinum for shipment of 210,000 copies by the end of the following year.<ref name=\"ARIA Cred05A\"/> [[AllMusic]]'s Mark Deming felt, \"[it] is perhaps a bit less striking than her first two sets, ''The Captain'' and ''Barricades & Brickwalls'', if only because she staked out her style on those sessions, and here she's harvesting from the ground she broke earlier on. But this also sounds like her most accomplished effort to date.\"<ref name=\"Deming 2\"/>\n\nSingles from the album include \"[[Hollywood (Kasey Chambers song)|Hollywood]]\" (August 2004), \"Pony\" (January 2005), and \"Saturated\" (May).<ref name=\"McFarlane\"/> Following the [[2004 Indian Ocean earthquake and tsunami|Boxing Day Tsunami]] (26 December 2004), Chambers appeared at the [[Wave Aid]] charity concert in Sydney in January 2005, to help raise funds for organisations in disaster affected areas.<ref name=\"NME Wave\"/> At the [[ARIA Music Awards of 2004]] she won both Best Female Artist and Best Country Album for ''Wayward Angel''.<ref name=\"ARIA list\"/>\n\nChambers's fourth studio album, ''[[Carnival (Kasey Chambers album)|Carnival]]'' (August 2006), also debuted at No.&nbsp;1.<ref name=\"McFarlane\"/><ref name=\"AUS\"/> Deming found, \"[it] is roots-friendly enough that it isn't likely to seriously alienate most of her fans, this album does represent a clear and decisive break from the country-influenced approach of her earlier music; most of these 12 songs are easygoing but satisfying roots rock with a bluesy undertone... As a songwriter, she keeps getting better at writing about the stuff of everyday lives (love, lust, disappointment, getting on with life) with an uncommon degree of horse sense and attention to detail, and if anything, the new musical backdrops have added to the depth of her emotional landscapes.\"<ref name=\"Deming 3\"/> Its lead single, \"[[Nothing at All (Kasey Chambers song)|Nothing at All]]\" (July), reached the top&nbsp;ten.<ref name=\"AUS\"/>\n\n===2008\u20132010: ''Rattlin' Bones'' to ''Little Bird''===\n[[File:Kasey Chambers.jpg|Chambers at the ARIA Hall of Fame, July 2008|thumb|160px|alt=The 32-year-old Chambers wears a white dress with bare shoulders. She has numerous brown necklaces and a silver one. She has a chin stud below her lower lip and is looking to her right with a smile as she speaks.]]\nIn April 2008 Chambers issued her first collaboration album, ''[[Rattlin' Bones]]'', with her then-husband [[Shane Nicholson (singer)|Shane Nicholson]], which was co-produced by Nash and Nicholson.<ref name=\"McFarlane\"/><ref name=\"Gutch\"/> It debuted at No.&nbsp;1 and was certified platinum for 70,000 shipments by that year's end.<ref name=\"AUS\"/><ref name=\"ARIA Creds08\"/> Frank Gutch Jnr of ''[[No Depression (magazine)|No Depression]]'' felt, \"[it] could be the soundtrack of the Old West, or themes from the old mountain lifestyle. They have it down, from the sparing use of mandolin and the at times Everly Brothers harmonies to the dirt-beneath-the-fingernails aura. This music is American. Except that it's Australian. It's a conundrum.\"<ref name=\"Gutch\"/>\n\nChambers and Nicholson were joined by fellow country musician, [[Troy Cassar-Daley]], to perform at [[Sound Relief]], in March 2009, which was a benefit concert in support of survivors of the [[February 2009 Victorian bushfires]].<ref name=\"Brumby\"/><ref name=\"Mitchell\"/> It was held at the [[Melbourne Cricket Ground]], simultaneously with another concert at the [[Sydney Cricket Ground]].<ref name=\"Brumby\"/> All the proceeds from the Melbourne concert went to the [[Red Cross]] Victorian Bushfire relief.<ref name=\"Brumby\"/><ref name=\"Mitchell\"/> Appearing with Chambers in Melbourne were [[Augie March]], Bliss N Eso with Paris Wells, [[Gabriella Cilmi]], [[Hunters & Collectors]], [[Jack Johnson (musician)|Jack Johnson]], [[Jet (band)|Jet]], [[Kings of Leon]], [[Liam Finn]], [[Midnight Oil]], [[Paul Kelly (Australian musician)|Paul Kelly]], [[Split Enz]], and [[Wolfmother]].<ref name=\"Official\"/>\n\nDuring 2009 Chambers collaborated with Bill, Nash and family members to release a children's music album, ''[[Kasey Chambers, Poppa Bill and the Little Hillbillies]]'' (November 2009).<ref name=\"NLA Hillbillies\"/> In 2010 it won the [[Australian Independent Record Labels Association|Australian Independent Record (AIR) Award]] for Best Independent Country Album.<ref name=\"AutoRI-1\"/> As part of that project she also co-wrote a children's story, ''Little Kasey Chambers and the Lost Music'' (2009), with Bernadette Werchon.<ref name=\"NLA Little Kasey\"/>\n\nChambers' seventh studio album, ''[[Little Bird (Kasey Chambers album)|Little Bird]]'', appeared in September 2010 via [[Liberation Music]], which peaked at No.&nbsp;3.<ref name=\"McFarlane\"/><ref name=\"AUS\"/> ''[[Slant Magazine]]''{{'}}s Jonathan Keefe rated it as four-out-of-five stars and explained, \"[it] is a polished, studio-slick record of pop-country whose songs are catchy as all hell... It's the economy of [her] songwriting that has been the source of the comparisons between her work and that of [Lucinda] Williams, and Chambers's deep understanding of song structure allows her to create real emotional complexity from just a few turns of phrase.\"<ref name=\"Keefe\"/> It won Best Country Album at the ARIA Awards in [[ARIA Music Awards of 2011|2011]].<ref name=\"ARIA list\"/>\n\n===2011\u20132013: ''Storybook'' to ''Wreck & Ruin''===\n''[[Storybook (Kasey Chambers album)|Storybook]]'', Chambers next studio album, was released in September 2011 and consists of cover versions of other artists material, which peaked at No.&nbsp;21.<ref name=\"McFarlane\"/><ref name=\"AUS\"/> ''No Surf Music''{{'}}s Jason D Hamad described how, \"because of its very nature I can't say that this album breaks any new ground. Still, it does justice to Chambers' sometimes-eclectic influences and adds an additional layer of understanding for her fans.\"<ref name=\"Hamad\"/>\n\nHer single from the album, \"[[Luka (song)|Luka]]\" (2011), is a rendition of Susan Vega's original from 1987. Hamad discussed how, \"[she] strips away the 80's synth-pop, replacing it with more traditional instrumentation including a prominent, bouncing bass, but keeps the airy musical feel meant to contrast with the dark tone of the lyrics.\"<ref name=\"Hamad\"/> Her autobiography, ''A Little Bird Told Me...'', was co-authored with music journalist, Jeff Apter, and was issued later that year.<ref name=\"NLA Autobio\"/><ref name=\"Hente\"/>\n\nHer second collaboration with Nicholson, ''[[Wreck & Ruin]]'' (September 2012), reached No.&nbsp;6 and provided another ARIA Award for Best Country Album in the [[ARIA Music Awards of 2013|next year]].<ref name=\"McFarlane\"/><ref name=\"AUS\"/><ref name=\"ARIA list\"/> Keefe found the album has, \"the married couple layering intricate vocal harmonies over some casual, mostly acoustic country-rock... Though [it] impresses for its thematic focus and gallows humor, the economy of language in the songwriting occasionally scans as a bit pedestrian.\"<ref name=\"Keefe 2\"/>\n\nOn 23 April 2013, it was announced that Nicholson and Kasey Chambers had separated, their split forced by the collision of work and family life.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.news.com.au/entertainment/music/shane-nicholson-and-kasey-chambers-separate-after-eight-years-of-marriage/news-story/240f7c7dc6fa67ac7c78b6ba8a508cbb?sv=7674704dcfb1d17ffd9293047dec897a|title=Shane Nicholson and Kasey Chambers separate after eight years of marriage |website=[[news.com.au]]|date= 23 April 2013|access-date=30 April 2020}}</ref>\n\n===2014\u20132018: ''Bittersweet'' to ''Campfire''===\n[[File:Kasey and Bernard.jpg|thumb|right|With [[Bernard Fanning]] in 2017]]\nChambers' tenth studio album, ''[[Bittersweet (Kasey Chambers album)|Bittersweet]]'', appeared in August 2014, which peaked at No.&nbsp;2.<ref name=\"McFarlane\"/><ref name=\"AUS\"/><ref name=\"Deming 4\"/> It was produced by [[Nick DiDia]] \u2013 her first album which was not produced by her brother, Nash.<ref name=\"Deming 4\"/> Deming felt, \"[she] has written a set of songs that are unpretentiously intelligent but deal with matters of the heart and soul with unrelenting honesty, and her rough, sweet vocals never deliver anything short of the ring of truth. [It] is a strong, satisfying album from one of the best and most distinctive singer/songwriters of her day, and this confirms she can move in any number of different directions and still offer her listeners something remarkable.\"<ref name=\"Deming 4\"/>\n\nIt was also recorded after her marital split from Nicholson the previous year.<ref name=\"Familton\"/> ''[[The Music (magazine)|The Music]]''{{'}}s Chris Familton observed, \"It finds her canvassing a range of styles and moods, often with religious/biblical references, without sacrificing her heart-on-sleeve emotiveness, innate sense of melody and country heart.\"<ref name=\"Familton\"/> The title track is a duet with [[Bernard Fanning]] (ex-[[Powderfinger]]), which Familton found, \"sways with a Neil Young looseness that works surprisingly well.\"<ref name=\"Familton\"/> It won Best Country Album at the [[ARIA Music Awards of 2014]].<ref name=\"ARIA list\"/>\n\nIn late 2015 she covered the track, \"Cold and Bitter Tears\", on a [[tribute album]] for US soul blues musician, [[Ted Hawkins]], ''Cold and Bitter Tears: The Songs of Ted Hawkins'', which was released on Eight 30 Records in [[Austin, Texas]].<ref name=\"Begrand\"/> She was joined on the track by Bill and explained, \"My dad called me up one day and told me about the project... We recorded it at my dad's house, sitting around jamming around a mike. It was a really special thing. I play with my dad all the time, but the novelty never wears off. I love the combination that we create together.\"<ref name=\"Begrand\"/>\n\n''[[Dragonfly (Kasey Chambers album)|Dragonfly]]'', her eleventh studio album, appeared in January 2017 and reached No.&nbsp;1.<ref name=\"AUS\"/> It is a double album with Nash producing one session at his Foggy Mountain studio and Australian singer-songwriter Paul Kelly producing another session at Sing Sing Studios, Melbourne.<ref name=\"Hipwell\"/><ref name=\"Bernstein\"/> She followed with a US tour in mid-year.<ref name=\"Sacks Dragon\"/> Besides duetting on a track with Kelly, she also sings on a track each with [[Ed Sheeran]], [[Keith Urban]] and [[Foy Vance]].<ref name=\"Hipwell\"/><ref name=\"Bernstein\"/>\n\n[[Rolling Stone Australia|''Rolling Stone'' Australia]]'s Gareth Hipwell observed, \"[she] has always tended to eschew the more reticent course of songwriting from a point of abstraction, consistently wearing her profoundest truths and uncertainties on her sleeve. It's an artistic penchant given full flight on free-ranging double-LP ''Dragonfly'': 'Talkin' Baby Blues', a shot of Woody Guthriesque spoken-word acoustica, is itself a stunningly candid retelling of Chambers' storied life to date.\"<ref name=\"Hipwell\"/> Jonathan Bernstein of ''[[American Songwriter]]'' rated it at three-and-a-half stars out-of five and explained, \"[it] serves as a summation of sorts of the singer's entire career, a comprehensive, double-album opus that effortlessly switches between Appalachian mountain music, slow-burning folk-rock, melodic radio-pop, Woody Guthrie talking blues, and celebratory country-gospel.\"<ref name=\"Bernstein\"/> At the [[ARIA Music Awards of 2017]] she won her eighth Best Country Album trophy, for ''Dragonfly''.<ref name=\"ARIA list\"/>\n\nChambers twelfth studio album, ''[[Campfire (Kasey Chambers album)|Campfire]]'' (April 2018), is a collaboration with the Fireside Disciples, an \"ad hoc acoustic ensemble\", comprising Bill on [[dobro]], Brandon Dodd on acoustic guitar, and Alan Pigram on [[mandolin]] (and vocals on the album's lead track).<ref name=\"Deming 5\"/> It peaked at No.&nbsp;6 and was co-produced by Chambers, Bill, Dodd, Pigram, and Jordan Power.<ref name=\"AUS\"/><ref name=\"Deming 5\"/> At the [[ARIA Music Awards of 2018]] Chambers became the youngest solo female artist to be inducted into the [[ARIA Hall of Fame]], as well as winning the Best Country Album category for a record ninth time.<ref name=\"ARIA list\"/><ref name=hof/> At the Australian Country Music Awards of 2019, ''Campfire'' won Traditional Country Album of the Year.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.abc.net.au/news/2019-01-27/golden-guitars-wolfe-brothers-win-top-country-music-awards/10753724|title= Wolfe Brothers, Andrew Swift, Beccy Cole and Travis Collins win Golden Guitars|publisher=ABC|date=27 January 2019|access-date=27 January 2019 }}</ref>\n\n===2024: ''Backbone''===\nIn July 2024, Chambers announce the release of her new album ''Backbone'' and book ''Just Don't Be a D*ckhead''.<ref name=\"backbone\">{{cite web|url=https://countrytown.com/news/kasey-chambers-announces-new-album-backbone-book-just-don-t-be-a-d-ckhead/xHh61tnY29o/30-07-24|title= Kasey Chambers Announces New Album 'Backbone'|website=Country Town|date=30 July 2024|access-date=30 July 2024}}</ref>\n\n==Personal life==\nFrom 2000 Kasey Chambers' domestic partner was Cori Hopper, a [[Perth]]-born actor, film and music video maker, later based in Sydney.<ref name=\"Tamworth 1\"/><ref name=\"SMH Feb06\"/> Their son Talon was born in 2002;<ref name=\"Tamworth 1\"/><ref name=\"Kasey Official Bio\"/> they separated in November 2004.<ref name=\"SMH Feb06\"/> Hopper was a presenter on ''[[Australia's Funniest Home Videos]]'' from January to December of that year and was a regular cast member on ''[[The Wedge (Australian TV series)|The Wedge]]'' during 2006.<ref name=\"SMH Feb06\"/>\n\nOn 17 December 2005, Chambers married fellow country music singer-songwriter [[Shane Nicholson (singer)|Shane Nicholson]].<ref name=\"SMH Feb06\"/> Chambers had sung a duet, \"Designed to Fade\", with Nicholson on his debut solo album, ''It's a Movie'' (2002), which was produced by Nash Chambers.<ref name=\"SMH Dec02\"/> Subsequently, they co-released two albums, ''Rattlin' Bones'' (2008) and ''Wreck & Ruin'' (2012). Their son Arlo Ray was born in 2007, followed by daughter Poet Poppin in 2011. In April 2013 the couple announced their separation.<ref name=\"AutoRI-2\"/>\n\n[[File:Kasey Chambers & Shane Nicholson.jpg|thumb|160px|Chambers and Shane Nicholson, at the ARIA Hall of Fame, July 2008]]\nAt age 30 Chambers was diagnosed with an eating disorder, a combination of [[bulimia nervosa|bulimia]] and [[anorexia nervosa]].<ref name=\"Stephens\"/><ref name=\"News.com Jan17\"/> She explained, \"I just didn't feel myself and I knew that something wasn't right [...] It wasn't an image thing for me ... It wasn't 'Oh I look fat in photos'. It was more about the control thing.\"<ref name=\"News.com Jan17\"/> She was treated by a psychologist and ''MammaMia''{{'}}s Jessie Stephens, observed, \"she recognises the importance of accepting that it might be a bad day, or a bad week, and negativity is a vital part of living a balanced life. Pushing it away can lead to anxieties manifesting in a different, more debilitating way.\"<ref name=\"Stephens\"/>\n\nIn her autobiography, ''A Little Bird Told Me...'' (2011), Chambers provided, \"a disarmingly honest account of a remarkable talent.\"<ref name=\"Hente\"/> ''[[The Herald Sun]]''{{'}}s Corinna Hente observed, \"Despite all the success, tragedy struck through a miscarriage, a broken relationship, anorexia and a breakdown. She rebuilt her life with music, playing covers with her family in a band called the Lost Dogs at the local pub.\"<ref name=\"Hente\"/> She described one of their gigs from July 2007, \"it's not the best idea to get up and sing with a band when you're nine months pregnant, 10 days overdue and bigger than a barn, but there was something about my gigs with the Lost Dogs band that I found impossible to resist. They were a reminder of why I'd fallen in love with music in the first place.\"<ref name=\"Chambers 1\"/>\n\nChambers was raised in the [[Seventh-day Adventist Church]] by her parents.<ref name=\"Age Oct02\"/><ref name=\"Chambers 1\"/><ref name=\"Tele Apr15\"/> After releasing her single, \"Is God Real?\" (April 2015), she described her beliefs, \"It is a very personal thing, which is probably why we don't talk about it, but I don't think that means we shouldn't... For me, I certainly believe in a higher power. I don't have a yes or no answer. I have some sort of belief there, but it has changed a lot over the years.\"<ref name=\"Tele Apr15\"/> As of November 2018 she lives in [[Copacabana, New South Wales|Copacabana]], New South Wales Central Coast.<ref name=\"AutoRI-3\"/><ref name=\"Coast Nov18\"/>\n\n==Bibliography==\n* {{citation | author1 = Chambers, Kasey | author2 = Werchon, Bernadette | others = Harrold, Emma, (illustrator) the Fireside Disciples)</small> (2018)\n* ''[[Backbone (Kasey Chambers album)|Backbone]]'' (2024)\n\n==Awards and nominations==\n{{Main|List of awards and nominations received by Kasey Chambers}}\nChambers has won and been nominated for numerous music awards. They include fourteen [[ARIA Awards|Australian Recording Industry Association (ARIA) Awards]] and ten [[APRA Awards (Australia)|Australasian Performing Right Association (APRA) Awards]]. She was inducted into the [[ARIA Hall of Fame]] in [[ARIA Music Awards of 2018|2018]].<ref name=\"ARIA HoF\"/><ref name=hof/> This induction recognised her achievement of a \"significant body of recorded work\" and that she \"has had a cultural impact within Australia\".<ref name=hof/> Chambers has also won awards in the country music field with nine from the [[Country Music Association of Australia]] (CMAA).{{citation needed|date=April 2022}}\n\n==References==\n{{reflist|refs=\n\n<ref name=\"McFarlane\">{{cite book | author1 = McFarlane, Ian | author-link1 = Ian McFarlane | others = current_members  =\n| website          = <!-- {{URL|website.com}} -->\n}}\n\n'''Roger Knox''' (born 1948) is an Australian [[Australian country music|country singer]], nicknamed \"the Black Elvis\" and \"Koori King of Country\".\n\n== Early life and education==\nKnox was born in 1948<ref name=ChiTrib-Stranger-2013>{{cite news|last1=Dickinson|first1=Chrissie|title=To Roger Knox, the whole world is country|url=https://www.chicagotribune.com/2013/02/19/to-roger-knox-the-whole-world-is-country/|access-date=20 December 2014|work=[[Chicago Tribune]] |date=19 February 2013}}</ref><ref name=Australian-Survivor-2013>{{cite news |last1=Guilliatt |first1=Richard |title=Songlines of a survivor: Roger Knox|url=http://www.theaustralian.com.au/news/features/songlines-of-a-survivor-roger-knox/story-e6frg8h6-1226658460268?nk=99ea51c9b54ba94d692634e3e6f404d8|accessdate=20 December 2014|work=[[The Australian]]|date=8 June 2013}}</ref> in [[Moree, New South Wales]]. He is of the [[Gamilaroi]] nation, an [[Aboriginal Australian]] people. Knox grew up in the [[Toomelah Station|Toomelah Aboriginal Mission]] near [[Boggabilla]], which is near the border between [[New South Wales]] and [[Queensland]].<ref name=ABCRadio-AWAYE!-2003>{{cite web |last1=Browning|first1=Daniel|title=Roger Knox \u2013 Koori King of Country|url=http://www.abc.net.au/rn/awaye/stories/2003/858423.htm |website=AWAYE!|publisher=[[ABC Radio National]]|accessdate=20 December 2014| archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20080531225401/http://abc.net.au/rn/awaye/stories/2003/858423.htm |archivedate=31 May 2008|date=23 May 2003}}</ref><ref name=GreenLeaf-WarriorinChains-Review-1993>{{cite news |last1=Kim |first1=Ignatius|title=Singing with something to say|url=http://www.greenleft.org.au/1993/103/6031 |accessdate=20 December 2014|work=[[Green Left Online]]|issue=103|date=9 June 1993 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20080228232704/http://www.greenleft.org.au/1993/103/6031|archivedate=28 February 2008}}</ref> Knox comes from a family with 11 children.<ref name=Australian-Survivor-2013 /> His mother was a [[Stolen Generations|stolen child]], who was taken from her parents as a baby and raised in a children's home in [[Bomaderry]].<ref name=Australian-Survivor-2013 /> \n\nKnox was not allowed to attend the high school in [[Goondiwindi]], but instead was sent by the mission to work without pay at one of their properties.<ref name=Australian-Survivor-2013 /> Knox has said that the first music he heard growing up was [[gospel music]], which his grandmother, who taught [[Sunday school]], played.<ref name=ABC-MessageStick-2010 /><ref name=ABC-RNDrive-Stranger-2013>{{cite news|last1=Morrow|first1=Julian|title=Roger Knox: Stranger in my Land (video)|url=http://www.abc.net.au/radionational/programs/drive/roger-knox3a-stranger-in-my-land/4626386|accessdate=20 December 2014|work=[[Australian Broadcasting Corporation|ABC]] RN (Radio National) Drive|date=12 April 2013|format=video performance and interview}}</ref>\n\n== Career ==\nKnox left the mission at 17 and moved to [[Tamworth, New South Wales|Tamworth]], where he became a singer.<ref name=ChiTrib-Stranger-2013 /> He started out in the 1980s as a gospel singer.<ref name=ABC-MessageStick-2010 /> He acquired the nickname \"The Black Elvis\" (for his hairstyle and manner of dress) at the [[Toyota Star Maker Quest|Star Maker]] talent contest when he was 31.<ref name=Australian-Survivor-2013 /> He was also later dubbed  \"Koori King of Country\".<ref name=AllMusic-Knox>{{cite web|last=Leggett |first=Steve |url=http://www.allmusic.com/artist/roger-knox-mn0001624726 |title=Roger Knox \u2013 Biography |publisher=[[AllMusic]] |date=12 February 2013 |accessdate=21 March 2013}}</ref>\n\nIn 2007, Knox went public with claims that he couldn't get booked at Tamworth's annual festival, [[Tamworth Country Music Festival]], \"because he attracted the wrong crowd\".<ref name=SBS-Tamworth-2007>{{cite news |last1=Grant |first1=Karla |author-link= Karla Grant|title=Living Black: Series 7, Episode 4|url=http://news.sbs.com.au/livingblack/series_7_episode_4_131666|accessdate=20 December 2014|work=[[Special Broadcasting Service]]|date=28 March 2007 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20090108122722/http://news.sbs.com.au/livingblack/series_7_episode_4_131666 |archivedate=8 January 2009|format=transcript}}</ref>\n\n=== Jon Langford and the Pine Valley Cosmonauts/''Buried Country'' ===\nOn 12 February 2013, Knox along with the [[Pine Valley Cosmonauts]], released his first album in nine years, ''Stranger in My Land'' on [[Bloodshot Records]].<ref name=AllMusic-Stranger>{{cite web|last=Leggett |first=Steve |url=http://www.allmusic.com/album/stranger-in-my-land-mw0002471493 |title=Stranger in My Land \u2013 Roger Knox, The Pine Valley Cosmonauts |publisher=[[AllMusic]] |date=12 February 2013 |accessdate=21 March 2013}}</ref> The album was produced by [[Jon Langford]] and included guest contributions from [[Bonnie \"Prince\" Billy]], [[Charlie Louvin]], [[Dave Alvin]] ([[X (American band)|X]], [[The Blasters]]), [[Kelly Hogan]], Jon Langford, [[Andre Williams (musician)|Andre Williams]], the [[Sadies]], [[Sally Timms]] ([[Mekons]]), and [[Tawny Newsome]].<ref name=PRITheWorld-Stranger-2013>{{cite web|url=http://www.theworld.org/2013/02/aboriginal-roger-knox/ |title=Aboriginal Country Music from Roger Knox |last=Werman|first=Marco|work=[[PRI's The World]]|publisher=[[Public Radio International]]|format=audio interview |date=12 February 2013 |accessdate=21 March 2013}}</ref><ref name=NoDep-Spotlight-2013>{{cite news|title=Spotlighting Roger Knox: A week's worth of previews|url=http://nodepression.com/article/spotlighting-roger-knox-weeks-worth-previews|accessdate=20 December 2014|work=[[No Depression (magazine)|No Depression]]|date=31 January 2013}}</ref> The title of the record comes from a [[Vic Simms]] song.<ref name=DeadlyVibe-Studio-2013>{{cite news|title=In The Studio With Roger Knox|url=http://www.deadlyvibe.com.au/2013/05/in-the-studio-with-roger-knox/|accessdate=20 December 2014|work=Deadly Vibe|date=23 May 2013}}</ref> Jon Langford illustrated the booklet that accompanies the CD.<ref name=ChiTrib-Stranger-2013 />\n\nThe material features covers of traditional and Aboriginal country songs.<ref name=ChiTrib-Stranger-2013 /> The record came about after Langford read about Knox in Australian author [[Clinton Walker]]'s book, ''[[Buried Country]],'' which chronicled Aboriginal country artists.<ref name=VerseChorusPress-BuriedCountry-2000>{{cite web|last1=Walker|first1=Clinton|title=The Man Who Would be King: Roger Knox|url=http://www.versechorus.com/buried-country_roger-knox.html|website=Verse Chorus Press|accessdate=20 December 2014|url-status=dead|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141107175624/http://versechorus.com/buried-country_roger-knox.html|archivedate=7 November 2014|df=dmy-all}}</ref> When Langford visited Australia, he heard many of the recordings, then went to see Knox play at Tamworth's annual country music festival.<ref name=ChiTrib-Stranger-2013 />\n\nIn 2009, Knox was scheduled to perform at the [[Old Town School of Folk Music]] (OTSFM) in [[Chicago, Illinois]], on 10 October 2009 with [[Jon Langford]] and the [[Pine Valley Cosmonauts]]. However, his US visa was denied a week before the show because the US immigration office stated he lacked cultural significance.<ref name=Australian-Survivor-2013 /> The Knox-Langford tour finally occurred in 2012, including performances at OTSFM and the [[Hardly Strictly Bluegrass]] festival in [[San Francisco, California]].<ref name=Australian-Survivor-2013/>\n\nIn 2016, Knox joined the cast of the stage show adaptation of ''[[Buried Country]]'' itself, which played its premiere performance in Newcastle in August.{{citation needed|date=March 2019}}\n\n=== Musical style ===\nDescribing his music, Knox says: \"My music is basically country with an influence of aboriginal spirituality... I use all these (Aboriginal instruments such as [[didgeridoo]]s) but I still play country music. I may not sing about trains and sheep and cattle, but I still play country music\".<ref name=ChiTrib-Stranger-2013 /> It has been described as \"frequently upbeat and the lyrics often sharply political in tone. The lyrics are sprinkled with references to kangaroos and pelicans and detail the struggles of Australia's Indigenous Aboriginal population\".<ref name=ChiTrib-Stranger-2013 />\n\n==Honours and awards==\nIn 1993, Knox was named [[NAIDOC]] Artist of The Year.{{citation needed|date=March 2019}}\n\nIn 2004, he was inducted into the Australian Country Music Foundation's Country Music Hands of Fame.<ref name=DeadlyVibe-AbsentFriends-2007>{{cite web|title=Absent Friends-Roger Knox|url=http://www.deadlyvibe.com.au/2007/11/roger-knox/|website=Deadly Vibe|accessdate=20 December 2014|date=30 November 2007}}</ref>\n\nIn 2006, Knox was given the [[Jimmy Little]] Award for Lifetime Achievement in Aboriginal and Torres Strait Music at the 2006 [[The Deadlys|Deadlys]].{{citation needed|date=March 2019}}\n\n== Activism ==\nKnox is well known in Australia and is loved for his regular tours of the New South Wales and Queensland prison systems, where many Aboriginal men and women are incarcerated.<ref name=ABC-MessageStick-2010>{{cite news|last1=Corowa|first1=Miriam|title=Message Sick \u2013 Summer Series: Warrior in Chains|url=http://www.abc.net.au/tv/messagestick/stories/s2774829.htm|accessdate=20 December 2014|work=[[Australian Broadcasting Corporation|ABC]] Indigenous|date=10 January 2010}}</ref> Knox has also performed at many Canadian prisons for Native American prisoners.<ref name=ABC-RNDrive-Stranger-2013 />\n\nKnox participated in the Voices United for Harmony project, jointly managed by the Queensland Aboriginal and Islander Health Council and [[Griffith University]].<ref name=KooriMail-VoicesUnite-2010>{{cite news|last1=Strohfeldt|first1=Mahala|title=Indigenous voices unite for harmony|url=http://www.aiatsis.gov.au/koorimail/issues/pdf/488.pdf|accessdate=20 December 2014|work=The Koori Mail|date=3 November 2010|page=32|format=PDF}}</ref>\n\n== Personal life ==\n===Buddy Knox===\n<!---redirect \"Buddy Knox (guitarist)\" targets this section until new articles is created--->\nKnox's son Buddy is also a musician, starting to play guitar at the age of 10. In 2006, he formed the Buddy Knox Blues Band, which won Best New Blues Talent at the Australian Blues Music CHAIN Awards at Goulburn in February 2009. He was a finalist for Male Artist of the Year in the 2009 [[Deadly Awards|DeadlyAward]], and won numerous awards further awards. His debut album was ''got da blues'' (January 2008), which won the Newcastle Blues Awards Album of the Year.This was followed by ''Buddy's Blues'' in 2010, which comprises his own compositions as well as cover versions, including the National Musicoz Awards 2010 finalist \"Squeaky Chair Blues\". In 2011, he was nominated for a [[The Deadlys|Deadlys]] award. He has toured with the [[Warumpi Band]], [[Troy Cassar-Daley]], [[Paul Kelly (Australian musician)|Paul Kelly]], and [[Kev Carmody]].<ref name=DeadlyAwards-Buddy-2011>{{cite web|title=2011 Deadly Awards \u2013 Nominations: Male Artist of the Year \u2013 Buddy Knox|url=http://www.vibe.com.au/images/pdfs/deadly-awards-2011-mediakit.pdf |website=Deadly Vibe|accessdate=20 December 2014|page=10|format=PDF|date=15 July 2011}}</ref> \n\nBuddy married Sarina Andrew, daughter of famed Aboriginal country music singer [[Auriel Andrew]], but they later divorced.<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.noise11.com/news/r-i-p-auriel-andrew-1947-2017-20170102 |title=R.I.P. Auriel Andrew 1947\u20132017 |first=Paul| last=Cashmere |website=Noise11|date=2 January 2017 |access-date=5 January 2017| quote=  Buried Country producer Mary Mihelakos has provided the following obituary by Clinton Walker| first2=Clinton| last2=Walker}}</ref> Their sons, Gene, John, and Ruben, played in Buddy's band at some point.<ref name=VerseChorusPress-BuriedCountry-2000 />\n\n===Plane crashes===\nKnox survived two consecutive aircraft crashes.<!---only one mentioned here?---> In 1981, early in his career, Knox joined the roadshow of Brian Young, who had a band that criss-crossed Australia by light plane, which crashed due to engine failure.<ref name=Australian-Survivor-2013 /> The musicians and equipment had to be airlifted from the crash site. The plane carrying Knox, drummer Ken Ramsay, and singer Stephen Bunz from the scene also crashed. Ramsay was killed and the others were injured (including the pilot).<ref name=Australian-Survivor-2013 /><ref name=DeadlyVibe-Studio-2013 /> Knox suffered third-degree burns over more than 90 percent of his body<ref name=DeadlyVibe-Studio-2013 /> and became addicted to painkillers. One of his [[Australian Aboriginal elder|elders]] prescribed a traditional [[bush medicine|bush remedy]] in the form of a natural bath oil made from the [[Eura bush]]. That bush and the settlement on which his father was born were inspiration for the name of his band, the Euraba Band.<ref name=DeadlyVibe-Studio-2013 />\n\n== Discography ==\n===Albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\" border=\"1\"\n! scope=\"col\" style=\"width:11em;\"| Title\n! scope=\"col\" style=\"width:17em;\"| Details\n|-\n! scope=\"row\"| ''Give It a Go''\n|\n* Released: 1984\n* Label: Enrec Records (ENL 001)\n|-\n! scope=\"row\"| ''The Gospel Album''\n|\n* Released: 1986\n* Label: Enrec Records\n|-\n! scope=\"row\"| ''Warrior in Chains \u2013 The Best of Roger Knox''\n|\n* Released: 1998\n* Label: Enrec Records\n|-\n! scope=\"row\"| ''Goin' On, Still Strong''\n|\n* Released: 2004\n* Label: Trailblazer Records\n|-\n! scope=\"row\"| ''Stranger in My Land'' <br/> (with The Pine Valley Cosmonauts)\n|\n* Released: 2013\n* Label: [[Bloodshot Records]]\n|}\n\n\n=== Singles ===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\" border=\"1\" \n!
