Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Tommy_Emmanuel","to":"Tommy Emmanuel"}],"pages":{"1900005":{"pageid":1900005,"ns":0,"title":"Tommy Emmanuel","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|Australian guitarist (born 1955)}}\n{{Use Australian English|date=July 2013}}\n{{Use dmy dates|date=April 2021}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n| name               = Tommy Emmanuel \n| image              = 2024-09-18 Concert of Tommy Emmanuel and Mike Dawes at UdK Berlin Konzertsaal (Martin Rulsch) 096.jpg\n| caption            = Emmanuel in Berlin, September 2024\n| background         = non_vocal_instrumentalist\n| birth_name         = William Thomas Emmanuel\n| birth_date         = {{birth date and age|df=yes|1955|05|31}}\n| birth_place        = [[Muswellbrook, New South Wales]], Australia\n| genre              = [[Jazz]], [[Pop music|pop]], [[Rock music|rock]], [[Country music|country]]\n| occupation         = Musician\n| instrument         = Guitar, vocals\n| years_active       = 1962\u2013present\n| label              = [[Sony Music|Sony]], [[Columbia Records|Columbia]], [[Favored Nations Records|Favored Nations]]\n| associated_acts = Southern Star Band, [[John Farnham]], [[Dragon (band)|Dragon]], [[Jerry Reed]], [[Chet Atkins]], [[Martin Taylor (guitarist)|Martin Taylor]], [[Hank Marvin]], [[Gabriella Quevedo]]\n| website            = {{URL|tommyemmanuel.com}}\n{{Infobox person|embed=yes\n| signature          = Tommy Emmanuel signature 2013.svg\n}}\n}}\n\n'''William Thomas Emmanuel''' {{post-nominals|country=AUS|AM}} (born 31 May 1955) is an Australian guitarist. Originally a session player in many bands, he has released many award-winning recordings as a solo artist. In June 2010, Emmanuel was appointed a Member of the [[Order of Australia]] (AM);<ref name=\"It's an Honour: AM\">{{cite web|url=https://honours.pmc.gov.au/honours/awards/1142663 |title=It's an Honour \u2013 Honours \u2013 Search Australian Honours |publisher=Itsanhonour.gov.au |date=14 June 2010 |access-date=17 March 2013}}</ref> in 2011, he was inducted into the [[Australian Roll of Renown]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.tcmf.com.au/What-s-On/Roll-of-Renown/ |title=Roll of Renown|publisher=TCMF |access-date=21 August 2018}}</ref> In 2019, he was listed by MusicRadar as the best [[acoustic guitar]]ist in the world.<ref>{{Cite web|date=12 December 2019|first=Matt |last=Parker |title=The 10 best acoustic guitarists in the world today|url=https://www.musicradar.com/news/the-10-best-acoustic-guitarists-in-the-world-today|access-date=2021-08-03|website=MusicRadar|language=en}}</ref>\n\n==Life and career==\nOne of six children, Emmanuel was born in [[Muswellbrook, New South Wales]], Australia, in 1955. He received his first guitar in 1959 at age four and was taught by his mother to accompany her playing [[lap steel guitar]]. In 1961, at the age of six, he heard [[Chet Atkins]] playing on the radio. He vividly remembers that moment and said it greatly inspired him as a musician.<ref name=\"pritcher\">{{cite web |url=http://users.adam.com.au/donald/markinter.htm |title=The Official Tommy Emmanuel Web Site \u2013 Interview |publisher=Users.adam.com.au |date=19 April 1997 |access-date=17 March 2013 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20131010192609/http://users.adam.com.au/donald/markinter.htm |archive-date=10 October 2013 }}</ref>\n\nBy the age of six, he was a working professional musician. Recognizing the musical talents of Emmanuel and his older brother, [[Phil Emmanuel|Phil]], their father created a family band, sold their home, and took his family on the road. With the family living in two station wagons, much of Emmanuel's childhood was spent touring Australia, playing rhythm guitar, and rarely going to school. After their father died in 1966, Australian Country Music star [[Buddy Williams (country musician)|Buddy Williams]] approached the family and asked permission to take the Emmanuel brothers on the road with his touring show travelling around Australia. Tommy Emmanuel would go on to record a number of Buddy Williams albums in the early 1970s. The family settled in Parkes after the [[New South Wales Department of Education]] insisted that the Emmanuel children had to go to school regularly. <ref name=\"cmonline\">{{cite web|url=http://www.countrymusiconline.net/tommyemmanuel.html |title=Tommy Emmanuel: c.g.p |publisher=Countrymusiconline.net|access-date=17 March 2013}}</ref>\n\nIn his teen years, Tommy Emmanuel moved to Sydney, and was noticed nationally when he won a string of talent contests. <ref name=\"pritcher\" /><ref name=\"musicfrisk\">{{cite web|url=http://www.musicfrisk.com/picture/interview/tommy.emmanuel.fingerstyle.02.14.2003.php |title=Tommy Emmanuel Interview |publisher=Music Frisk |date=14 February 2003 |access-date=17 March 2013}}</ref> By the late 1970s, he was playing drums with his brother Phil in the group Goldrush as well as doing session work on numerous albums and jingles. He gained further prominence in the late 1970s as the lead guitarist in the Southern Star Band, the backing group for vocalist [[Doug Parkinson]]. During 1986\u20131988 and 1995, he joined the lineup of the leading New Zealand/Australian 1970s rock group [[Dragon (band)|Dragon]] that had reformed in 1982, touring widely with them, including a 1987 tour with [[Tina Turner]]; he left the group to embark on a solo career.\n\nIn 1994, Australian music veteran [[John Farnham]] invited him to play the guitar next to Stuart Fraser from [[Noiseworks]] for the ''Concert for Rwanda''. Emmanuel had previously been a member of Farnham's band during the early 1980s and featured on the album ''[[Uncovered (John Farnham album)|Uncovered]]'' and rejoined after the 1994 concert.\n\nIn July 1999, [[Chet Atkins]] commented that Emmanuel was a \"fearless\" [[fingerpicking]] guitar player and awarded Tommy and four others ([[John Knowles (guitarist)|John Knowles]], [[Marcel Dadi]], [[Jerry Reed]], and [[Steve Wariner]]) the \"Certified Guitar Player\" title.<ref name=Certified>{{cite news|last1=St. James|first1=Adam|title=Tommy Emmanuel: Certified Guitar Player|url=https://www.guitar.com/articles/tommy-emmanuel-certified-guitar-player|access-date=3 June 2019|publisher=Guitar.com|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160111083823/https://guitar.com/articles/tommy-emmanuel-certified-guitar-player|archive-date=11 January 2016}}</ref><ref name=\"Certified Wariner\">{{cite magazine|last1=Thompson|first1=Art|title=Steve Wariner|url=http://www.guitarplayer.com/artists/1013/steve-wariner/11636|magazine=[[Guitar Player]]|access-date=25 October 2015|date=1 September 2009}}</ref>\n\nEmmanuel and his brother Phil performed live in Sydney at the closing ceremony of the [[Summer Olympics]] in 2000. The event was televised worldwide with an estimated 2.85&nbsp;billion viewers.<ref name=\"musicfrisk\" />\n\nIn December 2007, he was diagnosed with heart problems<ref>{{cite web |url=http://break-hollywood.blogspot.com/2007/12/oz-music-legend-tommy-emmanuel-falls.html |title= Oz music legend Tommy Emmanuel falls ill|website=break-hollywood.blogspot.com |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20100316231641/http://break-hollywood.blogspot.com/2007/12/oz-music-legend-tommy-emmanuel-falls.html |archive-date=16 March 2010}}</ref> and was forced to take a break from his hectic touring schedule due to exhaustion but returned to full-time touring in early 2008.\n\nIn June 2010, Emmanuel was appointed a Member of the [[Order of Australia]] (AM).<ref name=\"It's an Honour: AM\"/>\n\nAt the 2011 \u2018TommyFest\u2019, Tommy took the chance to talk to the audience about his strong Christian faith.\n\u201cThe Lord is my shepherd, so I lack nothing\u2014it\u2019s true!\u201d he told the gathered crowds.\n<ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.warcry.org.au/single-post/2018/02/10/Tommy-Emmanuel-Guitar-star-takes-his-cue-from-God | title=Salvos Magazine &#124; the Salvation Army Australia }}</ref>\n\nIn 2012, Governor [[Steve Beshear]] awarded Emmanuel the state of Kentucky's honorific title of [[Kentucky Colonel]].<ref name=\"BroadwayWorld.com Kentucky Colonel\">{{cite web|author1=Music News Desk|title=Tommy Emmanuel to Tour United States Alongside Martin Taylor in Early 2014|url=http://www.broadwayworld.com/bwwmusic/article/Tommy-Emmanuel-to-Tour-United-States-Alongside-Martin-Taylor-in-Early-2014-20140114|access-date=25 October 2015|website=BroadwayWorld.com|date=14 January 2014}}</ref>\n\nIn 2009 he worked with fellow local artists [[Ray Burgess]], [[Marty Rhone]], [[John St Peeters]] and [[Swanee (singer)|John \"Swanee\" Swan]] to release a single, \"Legends of the Southern Land\".<ref name=\"Pascuzzi\">{{cite news | archive-url = https://webarchive.nla.gov.au/awa/20131018132000/http://pandora.nla.gov.au/pan/63544/20131019-0020/www.mediasearch.com.au/music/wrap/legendsofthesouthernland.html | url = http://www.mediasearch.com.au/music/wrap/legendsofthesouthernland.html | title = 'Legends of the Southern Land' \u2013 a new Australian anthem | last = Pascuzzi | first = Carmine | work = MediaSearch | archive-date = 18 October 2013 | access-date = 13 May 2017 }}{{cbignore|bot=medic}}</ref>\n\nDuring a July 2019 concert he mentioned recently receiving American citizenship.<ref>{{Cite web |url=https://www.theday.com/article/20190719/ENT10/190719396 |title=Review: Acoustic guitarists Tommy Emmanuel, Mike Dawes dazzle Garde crowd |date=19 July 2019 |website=The Day |language=en-US |access-date=26 July 2019}}</ref>\n\n==Guitar style==\n[[File:Tommy Emmanuel flickr.jpg|thumb|220px|right|Emmanuel's fingerstyle technique was featured at a June 2006 performance at [[City Stages]] in Birmingham, Alabama]]\nEmmanuel had said that even at a young age he was fascinated by [[Chet Atkins|Chet Atkins's]] musical style (sometimes referred to as [[Travis picking]]) of playing bass lines, chords, melodies, and harmonies simultaneously using the thumb and fingers of the right hand, achieving a dynamic range of sound from the instrument. Although Emmanuel's playing incorporates a multitude of musical influences and styles, including [[jazz]], [[blues]], [[bluegrass music|bluegrass]], [[folk music|folk]] and rock, this type of [[country music|country]] finger-style playing is at the core of his technique. While Emmanuel has never had formal music training and does not read or write music, his natural musical ability, intrinsic sense of rhythm, and charisma gained him fans from all over the world. As a solo performer, he never plays to a setlist and uses a minimum of effects onstage.<ref name=\"musicfrisk\" /> He usually completes studio recordings in one take.\n\n[[File:2024-09-18 Concert of Tommy Emmanuel and Mike Dawes at UdK Berlin Konzertsaal (Martin Rulsch) 163.jpg|thumb|Emmanuel uses a snare-drum brush to emulate the sound of a percussion kit]]\nIn his solo shows, he mainly plays guitars made by [[Maton]], an Australian guitar manufacturer. He usually travels with two custom Maton EBG808 TE models and one TE1 model, both of which are Tommy Emmanuel artist signature models.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://maton.com.au/product/te-series|title=The Maton TE Series - Maton Guitars Australia|access-date=19 September 2016}}</ref> He has played Maton guitars for most of his career and is somewhat of an ambassador for the company due to his long-standing association with the brand.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.maton.com.au/artists/tommy-emmanuel|title=Tommy Emmanuel - Maton Guitars Australia|access-date=19 September 2016}}</ref> Emmanuel is known for the battered and worn-down appearances of his guitars; a result of his dynamic, energetic playing and percussive techniques. One of his signature performances, for example, involves striking the whole body of the guitar in various places with his hands or a drummer's [[Drum brush#Brushes|snare-drum brush]] to emulate the sound of a percussion kit.\n\nEmmanuel usually keeps one Maton EBG808 in standard guitar tuning (E-A-D-G-B-E), while he tunes his second Maton EBG808 to D-G-D-G-B-E (G6 tuning) and his TE1 to C{{music|sharp}}-F{{music|sharp}}-B-E-G{{music|sharp}}-C{{music|sharp}}. He generally uses 0.12 gauge (light) strings on one EBG808 and 0.13 gauge (medium) strings on the second Maton EBG808 and on the TE1. This allows him to quickly change tuning by swapping between guitars during a show if needed, rather than spending time onstage re-tuning one guitar.{{Cn|date=December 2023}}\n\nEmmanuel often curls his left thumb around the neck of the guitar onto the [[fretboard]] to play some notes, rather than using only his fingers to play \u2014 contrary to how classical guitarists play, but not unusual for jazz and country guitarists. He frequently plays common three-finger chord shapes with just two fingers. He commonly uses a [[thumbpick]], a flat pick ([[plectrum]]), his fingers, or a combination of these in his playing, a style known as [[hybrid picking]]. Amongst his trademark rapid virtuoso licks and cascading harmonic progressions, he often uses a technique that imitated an electric guitar's tremolo system on acoustic guitar \u2014 by pressing the palm of his right hand against the [[Sound board (music)|sound board]] of the guitar near the neck joint, while maintaining forward pressure with his left hand on the top of the [[headstock]]. The guitar neck slightly bends away from the body and consequently affects the pitch of the strings to achieve the desired sound.{{Cn|date=December 2023}}\n\n==Influences==\nAs a young man in Australia, Emmanuel wrote to his hero [[Chet Atkins]] in [[Nashville, Tennessee]]. Eventually, Atkins replied with words of encouragement and a long-standing invitation to drop by to visit.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://justjazzguitar.com/index.php?option=com_content&task=view&id=329&Itemid=52 |title=Just Jazz Guitar Online \u2013 Tommy Emmanuel Interview |publisher=Justjazzguitar.com |access-date=17 March 2013}}</ref>\n\nIn 1997, Emmanuel and Atkins recorded as a duo, releasing the album ''[[The Day Finger Pickers Took Over the World]]''. It would be Atkins's last album, with the exception of \"Solo Sessions\" which Atkins' estate released posthumously.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Chet Atkins: Solo Sessions|url=https://www.misterguitar.us/news/solorelease.html|access-date=2021-04-25|website=www.misterguitar.us}}</ref> Emmanuel and Atkins appeared together on [[The Nashville Network]]'s 'Country Christmas' in late 1997, and on that occasion, Atkins stated about him: \"He is one of the greatest guitar players I've ever seen.\" Atkins gave Emmanuel the guitar on which [[Arthur \"Guitar Boogie\" Smith]] recorded \"Guitar Boogie\", one of the foundation performances of the blues guitar world and a regular feature of Emmanuel's shows.\n\nIn July 1999, at the 15th Annual Chet Atkins Appreciation Society Convention,<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.misterguitar.com/caas/index.html |title=The Chet Atkins Appreciation Society |publisher=Misterguitar.com |date=21 December 1997 |access-date=17 March 2013}}</ref> Atkins presented Emmanuel with a Certified Guitar Player award, an honour Chet personally bestowed to only four guitarists.<ref name=\"pritcher\" /> This award gains its fame from being bestowed by Atkins himself, a widely recognised leader in guitar music. The award states: \"In Recognition of His Contributions to the Art of Fingerpicking.\" Tommy performed at the Chet Atkins Appreciation Society (CAAS) in July each year in Nashville.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.modernguitars.com/archives/002881.html |title= Tommy Emmanuel Interview|website=www.modernguitars.com |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080509135648/http://www.modernguitars.com/archives/002881.html |archive-date=9 May 2008}}</ref>\n\nIn addition to being influenced by Chet Atkins, Emmanuel has stated that he and his brother [[Phil Emmanuel]] were inspired by and modelled themselves on [[Hank Marvin]] and [[Bruce Welch]] of [[the Shadows]].<ref>{{cite news |last1=Zollo |first1=Paul |title=Tommy Emmanuel: On Becoming \"The World's Greatest Living Guitarist\" |url=https://americansongwriter.com/tommy-emmanuel-on-becoming-the-worlds-greatest-living-guitarist/ |access-date=17 February 2022 |work=American Songwriter |date=20 August 2020}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n{{Main|Tommy Emmanuel discography}}\n\n{{Div col|colwidth=20em}}\n* ''[[From Out of Nowhere (Tommy Emmanuel (2023)\n{{Div col end}}\n\n==Awards==\n===APRA Awards===\nThe [[APRA Awards (Australia)]] are annual awards to recognise composing and songwriting skills, sales, and airplay performance by its members annually.\n\n{|class=\"wikitable\"\n|- style=\"background:#ccc;\"\n!Year\n!Category\n!Nominated work\n!Result\n|-\n||[[APRA Music Awards of 1992|1992]]\n|Jazz Composition of the Year\n||\"[[Stevie's Blues]]\"\n|{{won}}\n|}\n\n===ARIA Awards===\nThe Australian Recording Industry Association Music Awards, commonly known as [[ARIA Music Awards]], are held to recognise excellence and innovation and achievement across all genres of Australian music. Award nominees and winners, excluding for sales and public voted categories, are selected by the ARIA Academy comprising \"judges from all sectors of the music industry\u2013retail, radio and tv, journalists and critics, television presenters, concert promoters, agents, ARIA member record companies and past ARIA winners\".<ref>[https://web.archive.org/web/20120126003459/http://www.ariaawards.com.au/faqs/ ARIA Awards - FAQs]. ARIA Awards. Archived from [http://www.ariaawards.com.au/faqs/ the original] on 25 January 2012.</ref> The inaugural ARIA Awards took place in 1987.<ref>[https://web.archive.org/web/20120126020142/http://www.ariaawards.com.au/about/ Aria Awards overview]. Australian Recording Industry Association. Archived from [http://www.ariaawards.com.au/about/ the original] on 24 January 2012.</ref>\n\n{|class=\"wikitable\"\n|- style=\"background:#ccc;\"\n!Year\n!Category\n!Nominated work\n!Result\n|-\n||[[ARIA Music Awards of 1989|1989]]\n|[[ARIA Award for Best Cover Art|Best Cover Art]]\n||\"[[Up from Down Under]]\"\n|{{nom}}\n|-\n||[[ARIA Music Awards of 1991|1991]]\n|[[ARIA Award for Best Adult Contemporary Album|Best Adult Contemporary Album]]\n|''[[Dare to Be Different (album)|Dare to Be Different]]''\n|{{nom}}\n|-\n|rowspan=\"2\"|[[ARIA Music Awards of 1992|1992]]\n|Best Adult Contemporary Album\n|rowspan=\"2\"|''[[Determination (Tommy Emmanuel album)|Determination]]''\n|{{won}}\n|-\n|[[ARIA Award for Best Male Artist|Best Male Artist]]\n|{{nom}}\n|-\n||[[ARIA Music Awards of 1994|1994]]\n|Best Adult Contemporary Album\n|''[[The Journey (Tommy Emmanuel album)|The Journey]]''\n|{{won}}\n|-\n||[[ARIA Music Awards of 1995|1995]]\n|Best Adult Contemporary Album\n|''[[Terra Firma (Tommy Emmanuel album)|Terra Firma]]''\n|{{nom}}\n|-\n||[[ARIA Music Awards of 1996|1996]]\n|Best Adult Contemporary Album\n|''[[Classical Gas (Tommy Emmanuel album)|Classical Gas]]''\n|{{nom}}\n|-\n||[[ARIA Music Awards of 1997|1997]]\n|Best Adult Contemporary Album\n|''[[Can't Get Enough (Tommy Emmanuel album)|Can't Get Enough]]''\n|{{nom}}\n|-\n||[[ARIA Music Awards of 2013|2013]]\n|Best Jazz Album\n|''The Colonel & The Governor''\n|{{nom}}\n|}\n\n===Australian Roll of Renown===\nThe [[Australian Roll of Renown]] honours Australian and New Zealand musicians who have shaped the music industry by making a significant and lasting contribution to Country Music. It was inaugurated in 1976 and the inductee is announced at the [[Country Music Awards of Australia]] in Tamworth in January.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.tcmf.com.au/roll-of-renown |title=Roll of Renown |publisher=Tamworth Country Music Festival|access-date=29 October 2020}}</ref>\n\n{{awards table}}\n|-\n| 2011\n| Tommy Emmanuel\n| Australian Country Music Roll of Renown\n| {{yes2|inductee}}\n{{end}}\n\n===Country Music Awards of Australia===\nThe [[Country Music Awards of Australia]] (CMAA) (also known as the Golden Guitar Awards) is an annual awards night held in January during the [[Tamworth Country Music Festival]], celebrating recording excellence in the Australian country music industry. They have been held annually since 1973.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.country.com.au/awards/past-award-winners|title=Past Award Winners|access-date=2 November 2020}}</ref><ref despite cancelled Tamworth Country Music Festival|website=ABC|date=23 January 2021|access-date=24 January 2021}}</ref>\n\n{|class=\"wikitable\"\n|- industry]].<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.grammy.com/grammys/artists/tommy-emmanuel|title=Grammy Awards Artist Tommy Emmanuel|publisher=Grammy|access-date=22 January annual Australian entertainment industry awards. They recognise achievements in live entertainment in Australia from 1975 to 2016. Tommy Emmanuel won two awards in that time.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.moawards.com.au/awardwinners|title=MO Award Winners|website=Mo Awards|access-date=16 March 2022}}</ref>\n{{awards table}} (wins only)\n|-\n| 1994\n| Tommy Emmanuel\n| Australian Performer of the Year \n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 1996\n| Tommy Emmanuel\n| Australian Performer of the Year \n| {{won}}\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n===National Live Music Awards===\nThe [[National Live Music Awards]] (NLMAs) are a broad recognition of Australia's diverse live industry, celebrating the success of the Australian live scene. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Dianna_Corcoran","to":"Dianna Corcoran"}],"pages":{"30939848":{"pageid":30939848,"ns":0,"title":"Dianna Corcoran","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use Australian English|date=October 2016}}\n{{Use dmy dates|date=August 2014}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name         = Dianna Corcoran\n| image        = Dianna Corcoran.jpg\n| alt          =\n| caption      = Corcoran performing in 2010\n| image_size   =\n| birth_name   = Dianna Elizabeth Corcoran\n| birth_date   = {{Birth date and age|df=yes|1979|6|20}}\n| birth_place  = [[Parkes, New South Wales]], Australia\n| instrument   = Vocals, guitar\n| genre        = Country music\n| occupation   = Singer-songwriter\n| years_active = 2003\u2013present\n| label        =\n| website      = [http://diannacorcoran.com/ diannacorcoran.com]\n}}\n\n'''Dianna Elizabeth Corcoran''' (born 20 June 1979 in [[Parkes, New South Wales]])<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.flickr.com/photos/diannacorcoran/4171288376/|title=Mum (Jann) and baby Dianna in Hospital|date=8 December 2009|work=flickr.com|accessdate=20 May 2011}}</ref> is an Australian country music singer-songwriter. Among numerous awards, she is a three-time [[Country Music Awards of Australia|Golden Guitar]] winner\n\n==History==\nCorcoran's initial interest in country music involved [[yodelling]]. After finishing high school, Corcoran moved to Adelaide where she worked in three jobs (recruitment, dog food factory and car parts plant)<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.country.com.au/links-contacts/country-contacts/127-corcoran-dianna|title=Dianna Corcoran|date=6 July 2010|work=country.com.au|accessdate=21 February 2011|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110315165722/http://country.com.au/links-contacts/country-contacts/127-corcoran-dianna|archive-date=15 March 2011|url-status=dead}}</ref> to save enough money to make her first record (''Little Bit Crazy''). She became a professional musician in 2004.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.abc.net.au/tv/programs/landline/old-site/content/2004/s1189932.htm|title=Gympie Muster goes from strength to strength|last=Lee|first=Tim|date=5 September 2004|work=abc.net.au|accessdate=28 December 2018}}</ref> In that year, she toured with [[Adam Brand (musician)|Adam Brand]] as an [[opening act]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.abc.net.au/tasmania/stories/s1202879.htm|title=Adam Brand gets louder|last=Cox|first=Tim|date=20 September 2004|work=abc.net.au|accessdate=19 February 2011}}</ref> It was also in that year that she won her first Golden Guitar Award for New Talent of the Year.\n\nCorcoran has been deployed on three occasions to perform for Australian troops on active duty in war zones around the world, including a tour of Afghanistan with [[Jenny Morris (musician)|Jenny Morris]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.jennymorris.com/?p=353|title=The FACE tour: Images|last=Morris|first=Jenny|date=29 September 2009|work=jennymorris.com|accessdate=20 February 2011|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110713101857/http://www.jennymorris.com/?p=353|archive-date=13 July 2011|url-status=dead}}</ref> During one such tour to the [[Solomon Islands]] in March 2007 she met Tom Hinds, an Australian soldier. Corcoran wrote the song \"Come Back Home\" on the album ''Keep Breathing'' for him. She has written other songs about family and childhood experiences, including her father (\"If You Hear Angels\"), her mother (\"You'll Always Love Me More\") and her hometown Parkes (\"Rocky Hill\").<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.capitalnews.com.au/editorial.asp?editorial_id=1747|title=Twists and Turns|last=Jarvis|first=Susan|year=2011|work=capitalnews.com.au|accessdate=20 February 2011|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110706102524/http://www.capitalnews.com.au/editorial.asp?editorial_id=1747|archive-date=6 July 2011|url-status=dead}}</ref>\n\nIn 2008, Corcoran won Female Artist of the Year.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.northerndailyleader.com.au/news/local/news/general/awards-ceremony-a-singing-spectacular/287367.aspx|title=Awards ceremony a singing spectacular|last=Belt|first=Rebecca|date=28 January 2008|work=northerndailyleader.com.au|accessdate=20 February 2011|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110706110607/http://www.northerndailyleader.com.au/news/local/news/general/awards-ceremony-a-singing-spectacular/287367.aspx|archive-date=6 July 2011|url-status=dead}}</ref> In August, Corcoran was invited by [[Deborah Conway]] to take part in the Broad Festival project, which toured major Australian cities including performing at the Sydney Opera House.<ref name=\"Elliott\">{{Cite news | url = http://www.smh.com.au/news/music/ladys-night-at-the-beckoning-microphone/2008/08/18/1218911561072.html?page=fullpage#contentSwap1 | title = Lady's Night at the Beckoning Microphone | last = Elliott | first = Tim | newspaper = The Sydney Morning Herald | publisher = Fairfax Media | date = 19 August 2008 | accessdate = 5 June 2011 }}</ref> With Corcoran and Conway were [[Laura Jean]], [[Liz Stringer]] and [[Elana Stone]] \u2013 they performed their own and each other's songs.<ref name=\"Broad2008\">{{Cite web | url = http://www.broadfestival.com/ | title = Broad 2008 | publisher = Broad Festival | accessdate = 5 June 2011 | url-status = usurped | archiveurl = https://web.archive.org/web/20110511080719/http://www.broadfestival.com/ | archivedate = 11 May 2011 | df = dmy-all }}</ref>\n\n==Discography ==\n===Albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"James_Blundell_(singer)","to":"James Blundell (singer)"}],"pages":{"4442088":{"pageid":4442088,"ns":0,"title":"James Blundell (singer)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|Australian country singer}}\n{{Use Australian English|date=August 2013}}\n{{Use dmy dates|date=November 2023}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n|name                = James Blundell\n|image               = James Blundell autographing.jpg\n|alt                 = Man signing autograph\n|caption             = Blundell in 2009\n|background          = solo_singer\n|birth_name          = \n|birth_date          = {{Birth date and age|1964|12|08|df=yes}}\n|death_date          = \n|origin              = [[Stanthorpe, Queensland]], Australia\n|instrument          = Vocals, guitar\n|genre               = [[Country music|Country]], [[country rock]]\n|occupation          = Singer-songwriter\n|years_active        = 1987\u2013present \n|label               = [[EMI Records|EMI]], ABC, Compass Brothers, Revenge, Red Rebel\n|website             = {{URL|jamesblundell.com.au}}\n}}\n\n'''James Blundell''' (born 8 December 1964) is an Australian [[country music]] singer. Born in [[Stanthorpe, Queensland]], Blundell first rose to prominence after being named \"best new talent\" at the 1987 [[Country Music Awards of Australia]]. Blundell has since released several albums in both Australia and the United States, with his most successful album ''[[This Road (album)|This Road]]'' (released in 1992) selling more than 145,000 copies in Australia. Blundell was an unsuccessful candidate for the [[Australian Senate|Senate]] in Queensland at the [[2013 Australian federal election|2013 federal election]], running for [[Katter's Australian Party]]. At the 2019 [[Country Music Awards of Australia]], Blundell was inducted into the Hall of Fame.\n\n==Early life==\nBlundell was born in [[Queensland]] town of [[Stanthorpe, Queensland|Stanthorpe]], and was brought up on a sheep and cattle station near the town. As an adult he worked as a station hand across various locations in northern Australia. After a back injury sustained while working on a farm in [[Papua New Guinea]] he turned to music.<ref name=\"countrystyle1\">{{cite web|url=http://countrystyle-cndsrc.texterity.com/countrystyle/200904/?pg=14|title=My Country Childhood - James Blundell Singer|last=Sweeney|first=Barbara|date=April 2009|publisher=Country Style|pages=32\u201334|access-date=1 February 2010|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110716212940/http://countrystyle-cndsrc.texterity.com/countrystyle/200904/?pg=14|archive-date=16 July 2011|url-status=dead}}</ref><ref name=dictionaryperformingarts1>{{cite book|last=Atkinson|first=Ann|author2=Linsay Knight|author3=Margaret McPhee|title=The Dictionary of Performing Arts in Australia|publisher=Allen & Unwin|year=1996|location=[[St Leonards, New South Wales|St Leonards]]|page=34|isbn=1-86373-898-3}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.canberratimes.com.au/act-news/the-boys-from-the-bush-are-back-in-town--james-blundell-plays-with-lee-kernaghan-in-canberra-on-may-5-20170426-gvsvbe.html|title=The boys from the bush are back in town - James Blundell plays with Lee Kernaghan in Canberra |work=The Canberra Times|date= 28 April 2017|access-date=21 February 2018}}</ref>\n\n==Music career==\n===1987\u20131991: Career beginnings===\n{{Main|James Blundell (album)|Hand It Down}}\nIn 1987, Blundell won the Australia's Starker Quest at the [[Country Music Awards of Australia]] (CMAA) and won a recording contract with RCA Victor Australia where he released \"Gidgee Bug Pub Song\".<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.discogs.com/James-Blundell-The-Gidgee-Bug-Pub-Song/release/10851998|title=The Gidgee Bug Pub Song |publisher=Discogs|access-date=22 February 2018}}</ref> In 1988, Blundell won the [[Country Music Awards of Australia|Golden Guitar Award]] for the \"Best New Talent\".<ref name=\"age1\">{{cite news|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=wmYRAAAAIBAJ&pg=4678,334073&dq=james-blundell+country&hl=en|title=What's on Music - Singles|last=Mangan|first=John|date=21 April 1989|work=The Age|pages=10|access-date=1 February 2010}}</ref><ref name=smh1>{{cite news|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=WDsRAAAAIBAJ&pg=4880,8136322&dq=james-blundell+country&hl=en|archive-url=https://archive.today/20130124132450/http://news.google.com/newspapers?id=WDsRAAAAIBAJ&sjid=aucDAAAAIBAJ&pg=4880,8136322&dq=james-blundell+country&hl=en|url-status=dead|archive-date=24 January 2013|title=Two golden guitars for singer|last=Jarvis|first=Sue|date=29 January 1989|work=The Sydney Morning Herald|access-date=1 February 2010}}</ref> Blundell signed with [[EMI]] released his [[eponymous]] debut studio album in 1989. The album spawned the singles \"Cloncurry Cattle Song\" and \"Kimberley Moon\"; both of which won him Male Vocalist of the Year awards at the CMAA in 1989 and 1990. In 1990, Blundell contributed \"Until the Next Big Dry\" for the 1990 compilation album ''[[Breaking Ground - New Directions in Country Music]]''. Late in 1990, Blundell released his second studio album ''[[Hand It Down]]'' which peaked at number 50 on the ARIA charts in 1991 and won him his first [[ARIA Award]] in [[ARIA Music Awards of 1991|1991]] for [[ARIA Award for Best Country Album|Best Country Album]]. The single \"Age of Grace\" won Blundell his third consecutive Male Vocalist of the Year awards at the CMAA in 1991.\n\n===1992\u20132002: Commercial Success with EMI===\n{{Main|This Road (album)|Touch of Water|Earth & Sea|I Shall Be Released: The Best of James Blundell}}\nIn March 1992, Blundell released a cover of [[The Dingoes]]' song \"[[Way Out West (The Dingoes song)|Way Out West]]\" with [[James Reyne]]. The song was a commercial success peaking at number 2 on the [[ARIA Charts]] and was certified gold.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.ariacharts.com.au/annual-charts/1992/singles-chart|title=1992 ARIA SINGLES CHART|publisher=ARIA Charts|access-date=21 February 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20171006163157/https://www.ariacharts.com.au/annual-charts/1992/singles-chart|archive-date=6 October 2017|url-status=dead}}</ref> It won Blundell his first [[APRA Awards (Australia)|APRA Award]] for Country Song of the Year. In April, Blundell released his third studio album ''[[This Road (album)|This Road]]'' which peaked at number 4 on the ARIA Charts, was certified platinum and has sold more than 145,000 copies in Australia.<ref name=PerthNow>{{cite web|url=https://www.perthnow.com.au/news/wa/bankrupt-james-blundell-back-with-his-folks-ng-d2f72398ac83efd21e265d879918c439|title= Bankrupt James Blundell back with his folks|publisher=Perth Now|date=30 May 2010 |access-date= 21 February 2018}}</ref> Additional singles \"This Road\" and \"Down on the Farm\" were released in 1992 and Blundell won two more Golden Guitar awards at the 1993 CMAA, including Top Selling album of the Year. In August 1993, Blundell released ''[[Touch of Water]]'' which peaked at number 11 on the ARIA Charts. Blundell continued to play regularly at folk and country music festivals around Australia. In April 1995, Blundell released his fifth studio album ''[[Earth & Sea]]'' which peaked at number 31. In 1996, disillusioned with the music industry, around Europe in a van, earning money by busking.<ref name=PerthNow/>\nIn 1997, Blundell featured in a [[Qantas]] commercial, singing \"[[I Still Call Australia Home]]\", and in the lead-up to the [[1999 Australian republic referendum]], Blundell recorded the official song for the \"No\" campaign, despite being in favour of a republic.<ref name=guardian1>{{cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/1999/nov/03/australia.monarchy1|title=Digger's final push to keep the Queen|last=Campbell|first=Duncan|date=3 November 1999|work=The Guardian|access-date=1 February 2010}}</ref><ref name=abc1>{{cite news|url=http://www.abc.net.au/am/stories/s58288.htm|title=Ad campaigns won't make referendum voting easier|date=11 October 1999|work=AM|publisher=ABC Radio|access-date=1 February 2010}}</ref><ref name=\"abc2\">{{cite news|url=http://www.abc.net.au/worldtoday/stories/s58363.htm|title='No' campaign accused of sexist advert |date=11 October 1999|work=The World Today|publisher=ABC Radio|access-date=1 February 2010}}</ref> In 1999, Blundell released his sixth studio album ''Amsterdam Breakfast'' which sold 8,000 copies.<ref name=PerthNow/> In August 2001, EMI released his first greatest hits album, ''[[I Shall Be Released: The Best of James Blundell]]'', which concluded his record deal.\n\n===2003\u20132012: Independent Artist, CMAA Hands of Fame and CMC Hall of Fame===\nAs an independent artist, Blundell garnered media attention for his 2003 song \"[[Postcards from Saigon]]\", speaking out against the [[war in Iraq]].<ref name=\"capitalnews1\">{{cite news|url=http://www.capitalnews.com.au/editorial.asp?editorial_id=696&issue=63|title=WEATHERING THE STORM|last=Jarvis|first=Susan|date=February 2005|publisher=Capital News|access-date=1 February 2010|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20091007043702/http://www.capitalnews.com.au/editorial.asp?editorial_id=696&issue=63|archive-date=7 October 2009|url-status=dead}}</ref><ref name=PerthNow/> In 2005, the song won Australian Independent Country Music Single of the Year and Independent Country Music Male Vocalist of the Year. In 2005, Blundell released ''Deluge'', followed by ''Ring Around the Moon'' in 2007 and ''Portrait of a Man'' in 2008.\n\nIn 2007, Blundell was inducted into the Australia Country Music Hands of Fame.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.countrymusichalloffame.com.au/Hands/1-Hands%20of%20F.htm |publisher=Country Music Hall of Fame|title= The Country Music Hands of Fame|access-date=21 February 2018}}</ref> In October 2010 Blundell was the narrator for [[Network Ten]]'s television show, [[Keeping up with the Joneses (TV series)|Keeping up with the Joneses]] and for four months from November 2010, Blundell performed in a musical theatre show, ''The Ultimate Rock 'n' Roll Jam Session'', with [[Nick Barker (Australian musician)|Nick Barker]], Dave Larkin, [[Ezra Lee (musician)|Ezra Lee]] and [[Doug Parkinson (entertainer)|Doug Parkinson]].<ref name=\"Fox Photo\">{{cite web|url=http://www.foxmediamarketing.com.au/gallery_385493.html|title=''The Ultimate Rock 'n' Roll Jam Session''|publisher=Fox Media Marketing (Clive Fox Photography)|access-date=16 June 2015}}</ref><ref name=\"Ultimate Rock\">{{cite web|url=http://www.abc.net.au/local/stories/2010/10/26/3048379.htm|title=Win Tweet Seats to the ''Ultimate Rock 'n' Roll Jam Sessions''|publisher=774 ABC Melbourne (Australian Broadcasting Corporation (ABC))|date=29 October 2010|access-date=16 June 2015}}</ref><ref name=\"Kary\">{{cite news|url=http://www.sydneyartsguide.com.au/the-ultimate-rock-n-roll-jam-session/|title=''The Ultimate Rock 'n' Roll Jam Session''|last=Kary|first=David|work=Sydney Arts Guide|date=22 February 2011|access-date=16 June 2015}}</ref> Blundell released his tenth studio album ''Woolshed Creek'' in April 2011. In March 2012, Blundell was the inaugural inductee into the [[Country Music Channel]]'s Hall of Fame.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.countrymusicchannel.com.au/the-cmc-awards-winners|title=THE CMC Award Winners |publisher=Country Music Channel|date=March 2012 |access-date=21 February 2018}}</ref>\n\n===2013\u2013present: politics and music===\n{{Main|Campfire (James Blundell album)}}\nIn June 2013, Blundell became a candidate in the [[2013 Australian federal election]]. In August 2015, Blundell released ''Come on In'' and in February 2017, his twelfth studio album ''[[Campfire (James Blundell album)|Campfire]]'' which became his first charting album in over 20 years, peaking at number 58. In February 2018, a tribute album ''30 Years of Pride: A Tribute to James Blundell'' was released.\n\n==Politics==\nIn June 2013, Blundell was selected as [[Katter's Australian Party]]'s lead [[Australian Senate|Senate]] candidate<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.abc.net.au/news/federal-election-2013/guide/sqld/|title=Federal Election 2013|publisher=ABC|date=30 August 2013|access-date=4 December 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.kattersaustralianparty.com.au/our-people/james-blundell|title=Katter's Australia Party James Blundell|publisher=Katter's Australia Party|date=17 July 2013|access-date=30 August 2013|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130819072825/http://www.kattersaustralianparty.com.au/our-people/james-blundell|archive-date=19 August 2013|url-status=dead}}</ref> for Queensland in the [[2013 Australian federal election|2013 federal election]].<ref name=signsup>{{cite web|url=http://www.couriermail.com.au/news/queensland/country-music-star-james-blundell-signs-up-for-bob-katters-party/story-e6freoof-1226655052412|archive-url=https://archive.today/20130830203805/http://www.couriermail.com.au/news/queensland/country-music-star-james-blundell-signs-up-for-bob-katters-party/story-e6freoof-1226655052412|url-status=dead|archive-date=30 August 2013|title= Country music star James Blundell signs up for Bob Katter's party|publisher= [[The Courier-Mail]]|date= 2 June 2013|access-date= 30 August 2013}}</ref> This was largely at the urging of [[Bob Katter]], the party's founder and only federal member of parliament. Blundell had previously been approached to stand in elections by the [[Liberal National Party of Queensland|Liberal National Party]] (LNP), but declined.<ref name=\"somethingtosingabout\">Jamie Walker (2013). [http://www.theaustralian.com.au/national-affairs/election-2013/country-star-gives-katter-something-to-sing-about/story-fn9qr68y-1226690482518 \"Country star gives Katter something to sing about\"] {{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130804094342/http://www.theaustralian.com.au/national-affairs/election-2013/country-star-gives-katter-something-to-sing-about/story-fn9qr68y-1226690482518 |date=4 August 2013 }} \u2013 ''The Australian''. Published 3 August 2013. Retrieved 30 August 2013.</ref> His selection was controversial within the party, in part because he had not been a party member before his candidacy was announced, and contributed to a former vice-president, Kevin Brown, resigning his membership.<ref>Jason Tin (2013). [http://www.news.com.au/national-news/queensland/katters-australian-party-members-slam-senate-preselection-of-country-star-james-blundell/story-fnii5v6w-1226655436169 \"Katter's Australian Party members slam Senate preselection of country star James Blundell\"] {{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20131020145227/http://www.news.com.au/national-news/queensland/katters-australian-party-members-slam-senate-preselection-of-country-star-james-blundell/story-fnii5v6w-1226655436169 |date=20 October 2013 }} \u2013 ''The Courier-Mail''. Published 3 June 2013. Retrieved 30 August 2013.</ref> Some of Blundell's political positions have been controversial within the party, notably his support for [[Same-sex marriage in Australia|same-sex marriage]] and the abolition of [[Overtime|penalty rates]].<ref>[http://www.theaustralian.com.au/national-affairs/election-2013/clive-palmer-bob-katter-discuss-all-things-great-and-small/story-fn9qr68y-1226704378810 \"Clive Palmer, Bob Katter discuss all things great and small\"] {{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130826220941/http://www.theaustralian.com.au/national-affairs/election-2013/clive-palmer-bob-katter-discuss-all-things-great-and-small/story-fn9qr68y-1226704378810 |date=26 August 2013 }} \u2013 ''[[The Australian]]''. Published 10 August 2013. Retrieved 30 August 2013.</ref>\n\n==Personal life==\nBlundell has been married twice\u2014first to Louise, a former manager, and second to Lidia, with whom he had two sons.<ref name=\"telegraph2\">{{cite news|url=http://www.news.com.au/adelaidenow/story/0,22606,22311096-5012985,00.html|title=Ex's pals hit back at James Blundell over Idol Jesse Curran|date=26 August 2007|work=The Daily Telegraph|location=Sydney|access-date=1 February 2010}}</ref> He left his second wife in August 2007 for Jesse Curran, a singer who he had met at one of his concerts and while she was a contestant on Australian Idol. He and Curran have since had two children together, Fian Blundell and Ria Blundell.<ref name=\"telegraph1\">{{cite news|url=http://www.news.com.au/blundell-leaves-wife-for-idol-star/story-e6frfo60-1111114268538|title=James Blundell leaves wife for Jesse Curran |last=Reines|first=Ros|date=26 August 2007|work=The Daily Telegraph|location=Sydney|access-date=1 February 2010}}</ref><ref name=\"somethingtosingabout\"/>\n\nBlundell was engaged to Kristal Padget in 2017.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.canberratimes.com.au/story/6033676/the-boys-from-the-bush-are-back-in-town-james-blundell-plays-with-lee-kernaghan-in-canberra-on-may-5/|title = The boys from the bush are back in town - James Blundell plays with Lee Kernaghan in Canberra on May 5|date = 27 April 2017}}</ref> In March 2020 he announced his engagement to Rebecca Williams, 28 years after she inspired his 1992 hit \"Down on the Farm\".<ref>{{Cite web|title=James Blundell will marry \"Rebecca\" from his 1992 hit 'Down On The Farm'|url=https://tonedeaf.thebrag.com/country/james-blundell-will-marry-rebecca-from-his-1992-hit-down-on-the-farm/|access-date=2021-07-16|website=Tone Deaf|language=en-AU}}</ref>\n\nIn May 2010, Blundell filed for [[Bankruptcy#Australia|bankruptcy]], having gone into debt attempting to finance his albums, as well as having lost money on the sale of an investment property the previous year.<ref>[https://archive.today/20130830203825/http://www.news.com.au/breaking-news/james-blundell-caught-out-in-investment-property-slump/story-e6frfkp9-1225690988423 \"James Blundell caught out in investment property slump\"] \u2013 ''The Daily Telegraph''. Published 24 March 2009. Retrieved 30 August 2013.</ref> The bankruptcy was discharged in April 2013\u2014had it not been, he would have ineligible to stand as a candidate for election.<ref name=\"signsup\" />\n\nBlundell's brother, [[Peter Blundell (mayor)|Peter Blundell]], died on 24 December 2021. He was a former mayor of the [[Shire of Stanthorpe|Stanthorpe Shire]] and the [[Southern Downs Region]] as well as the [[Liberal National Party of Queensland|LNP]] candidate for [[Electoral district of Keppel|Keppel]] in the [[2017 Queensland state election]].<ref>{{cite news |last=Bowman|first=Trish|date=19 July 2017|title=LNP reveals shock candidate to take on Brittany Lauga|url=https://www.couriermail.com.au/news/queensland/rockhampton/lnp-reveals-shock-candidate-to-take-on-brittany-lauga/news-story/d181fc40a4aa017c1ac4ed1cfafc03db|work=The Morning Bulletin|access-date=26 December 2021}}</ref><ref>[https://archive.today/20130830203810/http://www.afr.com/p/national/with_senate_in_sight_katter_man_Y8yJzToBCKw7tHgQZJCLgL \"With Senate in sight, Katter's man sings to small business\"] \u2013 ''[[The Australian Financial Review]]''. Published 17 June 2013. Retrieved 30 August 2013.</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n{{Further|James Blundell discography}}\n*''[[James Blundell (album)|James Blundell]]'', 1989 \n*''[[Hand It Down]]'', 1990 \n*''[[This Road (album)|This Road]]'', 1992 \n*''[[Touch of Water]]'', 1993 \n*''[[Earth & Sea]]'', 1995 \n*''Amsterdam Breakfast'', 1999\n*''Deluge'', 2005\n*''Ring Around the Moon'', 2007<ref name=jamesblundell>{{cite web|url=http://www.jamesblundell.com.au/music.html|title=discography - albums |publisher=James Blundell Official Website|access-date=1 February 2010}}</ref>\n*''Portrait of a Man'', 2008<ref name=\"compass1\">{{cite web|url=http://www.compassbrothers.com.au/node/5|title=James Blundell|date=20 July 2008|publisher=Compass Brothers Records|access-date=1 February 2010|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110227123659/http://www.compassbrothers.com.au/node/5|archive-date=27 February 2011|url-status=dead}}</ref>\n*''Woolshed Creek'', 2011<ref name=jamesblundell/>\n*''Come on In'', 2015<ref name=jamesblundell/>\n*''[[Campfire (James Blundell album)|Campfire]]'', 2017<ref name=jamesblundell/>\n*''World Don't Stop'', 2023\n\n==Awards==\n===AIR Awards===\nThe Australian Independent Record Awards (commonly known informally as [[AIR Awards]]) is an annual awards night to recognise, promote and celebrate the success of Australia's Independent Music sector.\n{{awards table}}\n|-\n| [[AIR Awards of 2009|2009]]<ref name=\"09noms\">{{cite web|url=https://www.auspop.com.au/2009/10/air-nominees/|title=AIR Nominees|date=19 October 2009|access-date=19 August 2020}}</ref><ref name=\"AIRwins\">{{cite web|url=https://www.air.org.au/awards/history|title=History Wins|website=[[Australian Independent Record Labels Association]]|access-date=18 August 2020}}</ref>\n|''Portrait of a Man'' \n| Best Independent Country Album\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n===ARIA Music Awards===\nThe [[ARIA Music Awards]] are a set of annual ceremonies presented by [[Australian Recording Industry Association]] (ARIA), which recognise excellence, innovation, and achievement across all genres of the [[music of Australia]]. They commenced in 1987. Blundell had been nominated for five [[ARIA Music Awards]] and has won one.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.ariaawards.com.au/search?term=James%20Blundell|title = Search - ARIA}}</ref><ref name=\"CountryAlbum\">ARIA Award previous winners. {{cite web|url=http://www.ariaawards.com.au/history/award/Best-Country-Album|title=ARIA Awards Best Country Album|publisher=Australian Recording Industry Association (ARIA)|access-date=9 April 2022}}</ref>\n{{awards table}}\n|-\n| [[ARIA Music Awards of 1991|1991]] || ''Hand it Down'' || [[ARIA Award for Best Country Album|Best Country Album]] || {{won}} \n|-\n| [[ARIA Music Awards of 1992|1992]] || \"Time on His Hands\" || Best Country Album || {{nominated}} \n|-\n| [[ARIA Music Awards of 1993|1993]] || ''This Road'' || Best Country Album || {{nominated}} \n|-\n| [[ARIA Music Awards of 1994|1994]] || ''Touch of Water'' || [[ARIA Award for Best Adult Contemporary Album|Best Adult Contemporary Album]] || {{nominated}}\n|-\n| [[ARIA Music Awards of 2007|2007]] || Ring Around the Moon || Best Country Album || {{nominated}} \n|-\n{{end}}\n\n===APRA Awards===\nThe [[APRA Awards (Australia)|APRA Awards]] are held in Australia and New Zealand by the [[Australasian Performing Right Association]] to recognise songwriting skills, sales and airplay performance by its members annually. Blundell has been nominated for three awards and has won one.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.apraamcos.com.au/search |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210207235410/https://www.apraamcos.com.au/search |url-status=dead |archive-date=7 February 2021 |title=APRA search - James Blundell |work=APRA Awards |publisher=apraamcos.com.au |date=26 March 2015 }}</ref>\n{{awards table}}\n|-\n| 1992\n| \"Way Out West\" <small> (with [[James Reyne]]) </small>\n| Country Song of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 1999\n| Work of the Year\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n===Country Music Awards (CMAA)===\nBlundell has won ten [[Golden Guitar|Golden guitar]] awards at the [[Tamworth, New South Wales|Tamworth]] [[Country Music Awards of Australia]].<ref>{{Cite web |url=http://country.com.au/golden-guitars/award-winners/1990s |title=1990\u2032s :: Country Music Australia |access-date=21 February 2018 inducted into the [[Australian Roll of Renown]], which honours Australian and New Zealander musicians who have shaped the music industry by making a significant and lasting contribution to Country Music.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.tcmf.com.au/roll-of-renown |title=Roll of Renown |publisher=Tamworth Country Music Festival |access-date=29 October 2020 }}{{Dead link|date=February 2023 {{yes2|imprint}}\n|-\n| 2019 || himself || [[Australian Roll of Renown]] || {{yes2|inducted}}\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n===Mo Awards===\nThe Australian Entertainment Mo Awards (commonly known informally as the [[Mo Awards]]), were annual Australian entertainment industry awards. They recognise achievements in live entertainment in Australia from 1975 to 2016. James Blundell won one award in that time.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.moawards.com.au/awardwinners|title=MO Award Winners|website=Mo Awards|access-date=16 March 2022}}</ref>\n{{awards table}} (wins only)\n|-\n| 1989\n| James Blundell\n| Male Country Entertainer of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n===Queensland Music Awards===\nThe [[Queensland Music Awards]] (previously known as Q Song Awards) are annual awards celebrating [[Queensland, Australia]]'s brightest emerging artists and established legends. They commenced in 2006.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.queenslandmusicawards.com.au/about|title= About the Queensland Music Awards|website=Queensland Music Awards|access-date=21 March 2021}}</ref>\n\n{{Awards table}} <small>(wins only)</small>\n|-\n| [[Queensland Music Awards#2011 Queensland Music Awards|2011]]<ref>{{cite web|url= https://www.queenslandmusicawards.com.au/past-winners/2011|title=Past Winners 2011|website=Queensland Music Awards|access-date=25 March 2021}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://musicfeeds.com.au/news/photos-queesland-music-awards-2011-winners/#/slide/1|title= Photos Queensland Music Awards 2011 Winners|website=Music Feeds|date=August 2011|access-date=25 March 2021}}</ref>\n| \"Move into the City\"\n| Country Song of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| 2024<ref>{{cite web|url=https://themusic.com.au/industry/cub-sport-jem-cassar-daley-joff-bush-win-big-at-2024-queensland-music-awards/WYznTUxPTnE/17-04-24|title= Cub Sport, Jem Cassar-Daley & Joff Bush Win Big At 2024 Queensland Music Awards|website=[[The Music (magazine)|The Music]]|date=17 April 2024|access-date=18 April 2024}}</ref>\n| James Blundell\n| Grant McLennan Lifetime Achievement Award\n| {{yes2|awarded}}\n|-\n|}\n\n===Tamworth Songwriters Awards===\nThe Tamworth Songwriters Association (TSA) is an annual songwriting contest for original country songs, awarded in January at the [[Tamworth Country Music Festival]]. They commenced in 1986.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.tsaonline.com.au/song-competition/|title=Tamworth Songwriters Association|website=Tamworth Songwriters Association Online|access-date=23 March 2022}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.tsaonline.com.au/past-winners/|title=Tamworth Songwriters Association Past Winners|website=Tamworth Songwriters Association Online|access-date=23 March 2022}}</ref>\n{{awards table}} (wins only)\n|-\n| 1988\n| \"Gidgee Pub Song\" by James Blundell \n| Comedy/Novelty Song of the Year\n| {{won}}\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n==References==\n{{Reflist}}\n{{James Blundell (singer)}}\n{{Authority control}}\n\n{{DEFAULTSORT:Blundell, James}}\n[[Category:1964 births]]\n[[Category:ARIA Award winners]]\n[[Category:Australian country singer-songwriters]]\n[[Category:Australian republicans]]\n[[Category:Katter's Australian Party politicians]]\n[[Category:Living people]]\n[[Category:People from Stanthorpe, Queensland]]\n[[Category:People educated at the Southport School]]"}]}}}}{"batchcomplete":"","warnings":{"main":{"*":"Subscribe to the mediawiki-api-announce mailing list at <https://lists.wikimedia.org/postorius/lists/mediawiki-api-announce.lists.wikimedia.org/> for notice of API deprecations and breaking changes. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Gina_Jeffreys","to":"Gina Jeffreys"}],"pages":{"4144048":{"pageid":4144048,"ns":0,"title":"Gina Jeffreys","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|Australian country singer-songwriter (born 1968)}}\n{{Use dmy dates|date=May 2015}}\n{{Use Australian English|date=May 2015}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n|name         = Gina Jeffreys\n|image        = Gina_Jeffreys.jpg\n|caption      = Jeffreys at Broadway Melodies Theatre, ''[[Rhapsody Of The Seas]]'', October 2013\n|image_size   =\n|background   = solo_singer\n|birth_name   = Gina Hillenberg <ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.ginajeffreys.com.au/pressclippings/06/Dec17_Sunday_Mail_Brisbane.pdf |title=Archived copy |access-date=2014-01-28 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140204093341/http://ginajeffreys.com.au/pressclippings/06/Dec17_Sunday_Mail_Brisbane.pdf |archive-date=4 February 2014 |df=dmy-all }}</ref>\n|birth_date   = {{Birth date and age|df=yes|1968|4|1}}\n|birth_place  = [[Toowoomba]], [[Queensland]], Australia\n|genre        = [[Country music|Country]]\n|occupation   = Singer-songwriter\n|instrument   = Vocals\n|years_active = 1991\u2212present \n|label        = [[Australian Broadcasting Corporation|ABC Music]], Ocean Road Music/MGM\n|associated_acts = [[Rod McCormack]], [[Garth Porter]]\n|website      = {{URL|http://ginajeffreys.com.au }}\n}}\n'''Gina Jeffreys''' (born 1 April 1968), also known as '''Gina Jeffries''', '''Gina Hillenberg''' and '''Gina McCormack''', is an Australian [[country music|country]] singer-songwriter and radio presenter.\n\n==Career==\nIn 1991, Jeffreys competed in the Toyota Star Maker Quest at the [[Tamworth Country Music Festival]]. After releasing her first single, \"[[Slipping Away (Max Merritt & The Meteors song)|Slipping Away]]\" (a cover of the 1975 song by [[Max Merritt]]), through [[BMG Music]] and \"Radio Santa\" in 1992, she signed a record deal with [[Australian Broadcasting Corporation|ABC Music]] and released \"Two Stars Fell\" in 1993. The song went straight to No. 1 on the Australian country charts.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://ginajeffreys.com.au/bio/|title=Gina Jeffreys Bio|publisher=ginajeffreys.com.au|access-date=26 March 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150402161723/http://ginajeffreys.com.au/bio/|archive-date=2 April 2015|url-status=dead}}</ref>\n\n\"Two Stars Fell\" won Jeffreys her first [[Golden Guitar]] award at the 1994 [[Tamworth, New South Wales|Tamworth]] [[Country Music Awards of Australia]] for Best Female Vocal Award. Later that year, she supported [[Johnny Cash]] and [[Kris Kristofferson]] on their Australian tours and positive reviews had her the subject of a ''[[60 Minutes (Australian TV program)|Sixty Minutes]]'' story and an ''[[A Current Affair (Australian TV series)|A Current Affair]]', segment. Her debut album, ''[[The Flame (Gina Jeffreys album)|The Flame]]'', was released in August 1994 and went platinum in 1997. Further hits followed, including \"Girls' Night Out\" which won Jeffreys her second Golden Guitar award for Best Female Vocal in 1995.\n\nIn July 1996, Jeffreys released her second album, ''[[Up Close (Gina Jeffreys album)|Up Close]]''. This was to be the album that broke the crossover barrier between country and mainstream. The album debuted straight into the national [[ARIA Charts]] at No. 9 while taking the No. 1 position of the national country charts. ''Up Close'' achieved Gold status during the same year as its release. Jeffreys toured nationally throughout 1996, appeared as a guest host of ''[[Sale of the Century]]'' and co-hosted the [[ARIA Music Awards of 1997|1997]] [[ARIA Music Awards]]. In 1997, she was inducted into the Tamworth Hands of Fame.\n\nIn June 1998, Jeffreys released her third album ''[[Somebody's Daughter (album)|Somebody's Daughter]]'', which peaked at No. 13 on the ARIA Charts. The album was certified Gold in 1999 and produced the hit song \"Dancin' With Elvis\" which won the Country Music Television's Video of the Year award in 1999. Jeffreys released a Christmas album in 1999, titled ''[[Christmas Wish (Gina Jeffreys album)|Christmas Wish]]''.\n\nIn December 1999, Jeffrey's performed at the [[Tour of Duty \u2013 Concert for the Troops]] in [[Dili]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.noise11.com/news/historic-1999-tour-of-duty-concert-featuring-john-farnham-kylie-minogue-and-the-living-end-to-be-released-for-anzac-day-20240420|title=Historic 1999 Tour of Duty Concert Featuring John Farnham, Kylie Minogue and The Living End To Be Released For ANZAC Day |website=Noise11|date=20 April 2024|access-date=22 April 2024}}</ref>\n\nThroughout 2000, Jeffreys relocated to Nashville to record her next album, ''[[Angel (Gina Jeffreys album)|Angel]]'', which was released in April 2001. The title track, \"[[Angel (Gina Jeffreys song)|Angel]]\", won numerous awards; including the 2002 Golden Guitar Award for Video Clip of the Year, the 2002 APRA Award for Most Performed Country Work and was named a finalist in the Australian Animation Awards in 2001. It charted at No. 57 on the ARIA singles chart.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.aria.com.au/issue577.PDF|title=ARIA Charts/ Week Commencing 19th March 2001|publisher=www.aria.com.au|date=19 March 2001|access-date=19 April 2015|url-status=bot: unknown|archive-url=https://webarchive.nla.gov.au/awa/20020220130000/http://pandora.nla.gov.au/pan/23790/20020221-0000/www.aria.com.au/issue577.PDF|archive-date=20 February 2002|df=dmy-all}}{{cbignore|bot=medic}}</ref>\n\nIn 2002, the ''[[Best of Gina Jeffreys... So Far]]'' was released. It includes her version of [[Radiohead]]'s \"[[Creep (Radiohead song)|Creep]]\", which she had performed on ''[[Andrew Denton's Musical Challenge]]''. This concluded her contract with ABC Music.\n\nJeffreys gave birth to her son Jackson in January 2003 and took some time out of the spotlight.\n\nIn 2006, Jeffreys signed a deal with Ocean Road Music and returned with the release of her album ''[[Walks of Life]]''. In 2007, she was awarded Best Independent Country Release at the [[AIR Charts|Australian Independent Record (AIR) Awards]],<ref>[http://ausindies.com.au/awards.html Australian Independent Record Labels Association Ltd (AIR) 2012] {{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110220134456/http://ausindies.com.au/awards.html |date=20 February 2011 }}</ref> for her album ''Walks of Life''. At the Tamworth Country Music Festival of 2007, Jeffreys initiated a now annual \"Walk of Life\" where country music artists and fans walk around the streets of Tamworth to help create awareness and raise money for the Leukaemia Foundation.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://caama.com.au/walk-of-life-with-gina-jeffreys|title=Walk of Life with Gina Jeffreys|publisher=www.caama.com.au|date=22 January 2011|access-date=6 April 2015|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150412092907/http://caama.com.au/walk-of-life-with-gina-jeffreys|archive-date=12 April 2015|df=dmy-all}}</ref>\nIn April 2007, Jeffreys joined [[Beccy Cole]] and [[Sara Storer]] to form [[Songbirds (group)|Songbirds]]; a successful multi-artist show in Australia that continued for some years. A live DVD was released of the Songbirds in 2009.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.jbhifi.com.au/music/Whats-Hot/emi/songbirds-youve-got-a-friend-live-in-concert/250500/|title= Songbirds - You've Got A Friend: Live In Concert|publisher=JBHiFi|access-date=26 March 2015}}</ref>\n\nIn 2009, Jeffreys performed a sell-out concert at Tamworth with [[Guy Sebastian]] and [[Wendy Matthews]], followed by the release of ''[[Old Paint]]'' in 2010, a laid-back acoustic album of her all- time favourite songs.\n\nIn August 2019, Jeffreys released her eighth studio album, ''[[Beautiful Tangle]]''. The first single, \"Cash\", was released in June 2019. It is her first new album in nine years.<ref name=\"BT\">{{cite web|url=https://www.nsw.gov.au/news-and-events/events/gina-jeffreys-beautiful-tangle-central-coast-album-launch/|title=Gina Jeffreys Beautiful Tangle Central Coast Album Launch|publisher=NSW Government|date=June 2019|access-date=14 July 2019|archive-date=14 July 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190714032543/https://www.nsw.gov.au/news-and-events/events/gina-jeffreys-beautiful-tangle-central-coast-album-launch/|url-status=dead}}</ref>\n\nFrom January 2022, Jeffreys replaced Sarah Forster as the co-host of the breakfast show on [[Star 104.5]] on the New South Wales [[Central Coast, New South Wales|Central Coast]], alongside Dave Rabbetts.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.radiotoday.com.au/gina-jeffreys-joins-star-fm-central-coast-breakfast-show/|title=Gina Jeffreys joins Star FM Central Coast breakfast show |publisher=Radio Today |date=December 2021|access-date=4 January 2022}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n===Albums===\n{|class=\"wikitable\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n!rowspan=\"2\"| Year\n!rowspan=\"2\"| Album details\n!colspan=\"2\"| Peak chart positions\n!rowspan=\"2\" width=\"150\"| [[Music recording sales certifications|Certifications]]<br><small>[[List of music recording sales certifications|(sales thresholds)]]</small>\n|-\n!style=\"width:3em;font-size:75%\"|[[ARIA Charts|AUS]]<br><ref name=\"auscharts\">{{cite web|url=http://www.australian-charts.com/search.asp?cat=a&search=gina+jeffreys |title=Australian Album Chart > Gina Jeffreys |publisher=australian-charts.com Hung Medien |access-date=2014-01-29 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140202224703/http://www.australian-charts.com/search.asp?cat=a&search=gina+jeffreys |archive-date=2 February 2014 |df=dmy }}\n*Top 100 (ARIA) peaks from January 1990 to December 2010: {{cite book|last=Ryan|first=Gavin|title=Australia's Music Charts 1988\u20132010|year=2011|edition=pdf|publisher=Moonlight Publishing|location=Mt. [[Songbirds (group)|Songbirds]]\n\n==Awards and nominations==\n===ARIA Awards===\nThe [[ARIA Music Awards]] is an annual awards ceremony that recognises excellence, innovation, and achievement across all genres of [[Australian music]]. Jeffreys had been nominated for four [[ARIA Music Awards]]<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.ariaawards.com.au/history/search?q=Gina+Jeffreys|title = ARIA Awards Winners}}</ref>\n{{awards table}}\n|-\n| [[ARIA Music Awards of 1995|1995]] || ''The Flame'' || [[ARIA Award for Best Country Album|Best Country Album]] || {{nominated}} \n|-\n| [[ARIA Music Awards of 1998|1998]] || ''Somebody's Daughter'' ||Best Country Album || {{nominated}} \n|-\n| [[ARIA Music Awards of 2001|2001]] || ''Angel'' ||Best Country Album || {{nominated}} \n|-\n| [[ARIA Music Awards of 2007|2007]] || ''Walks Of Life'' || Best Country Album || {{nominated}} \n|-\n{{end}}\n\n===APRA Awards===\nThe [[APRA Awards (Australia)|APRA Awards]] are held in Australia and New Zealand by the [[Australasian Performing Right Association]] to recognise songwriting skills, sales and airplay performance by its members annually. Jeffreys has won two awards.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.apraamcos.com.au/search |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210207235410/https://www.apraamcos.com.au/search |url-status=dead |archive-date=7 February 2021 |title=APRA search - Gina Jeffreys |work=APRA Awards |publisher=www.apraamcos.com.au |date=26 March 2015 }}</ref>\n{{awards table}}\n|-\n| [[APRA Music Awards of 1998|1998]]\n| \"I Haven't Got a Heart\"\n| Most Performed Country Work\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| [[APRA Music Awards of 2002|2002]]\n| \"[[Angel (Gina Jeffreys song)|Angel]]\"\n| Most Performed Country Work\n| {{won}}\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n===Australian Independent Record Label Association Awards===\nJeffreys has won one [[AIR Awards|AIR Award]]<ref name=\"wins\">{{cite web|url=https://www.air.org.au/awards/history|title=History Wins|website=[[Australian Independent Record Labels Association]]|access-date=18 August 2020|archive-date=10 March 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160310102536/https://www.air.org.au/awards/history|url-status=dead}}</ref>\n{{awards table}}\n|-\n| [[AIR Awards of 2007|2007]] || ''Walks Of Life'' || Best Independent Country Release || {{won}}\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n===Country Music Awards (CMAA)===\nThe [[Country Music Awards of Australia]] (CMAA) (also known as the Golden Guitar Awards) is an annual awards night held in January during the [[Tamworth Country Music Festival]], celebrating recording excellence in the Australian country music industry. They have been held annually since 1973. Jeffreys has won five awards.<ref>{{Cite web |url=http://country.com.au/golden-guitars/award-winners/1990s |title=1990\u2032s :: Country Music Australia |access-date=28 January 2014 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140125225402/http://country.com.au/golden-guitars/award-winners/1990s/ |archive-date=25 January 2014 |url-status=dead }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.historyofcountrymusic.com.au/cmhands.html|title=Australian Country Music Hands of Fame |website=historyofcountrymusic|access-date=14 October 2020}}</ref>\n\n{{awards table}} <small>(wins only)</small>\n|-\n| 1994 || \"Two Stars Fell\" || Female Vocalist of the Year || {{won}}\n|-\n| 1995 || \"Girls Night Out\" || Female Vocalist of the Year || {{won}}\n|-\n| 1996 || \"Didn't we Shine\" || Female Vocalist of the Year || {{won}}\n|-\n| 1999 || \"Dancin' With Elvis\" || Female Vocalist of the Year || {{won}}\n|-\n| 2002 || \"[[Angel (Gina Jeffreys song)|Angel]]\" [Gina Jeffreys (directed by Dylan Perry)] || Video Clip of the Year || {{won}}\n|-\n| 2007 || herself || Hands of Fame || {{yes2|imprinted}}\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n===Mo Awards===\nThe [[Mo Awards]] are annual Australian entertainment industry awards. They recognise achievements in live entertainment in Australia. Jeffreys has won four awards.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.moawards.com.au/awardwinners|title=Award Winners|access-date=14 October 2020|archive-date=11 August 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200811130738/https://www.moawards.com.au/awardwinners|url-status=dead}}</ref>\n\n{{awards table}}\n|-\n| 1993 || herself|| Female Country Entertainer of the Year|| {{won}}\n|-\n| 1994 || herself|| Female Country Entertainer of the Year|| {{won}}\n|-\n| 1996 || herself|| Female Country Entertainer of the Year|| {{won}}\n|-\n| 1998 || herself|| Female Country Entertainer of the Year|| {{won}}\n|-\n{{end}}\n\n==References==\n{{reflist}}\n\n==External links==\n* [http://www.ginajeffreys.com.au/ Official website]\n{{Gina Jeffreys}}\n{{Authority control}}\n\n{{DEFAULTSORT:Jeffreys, Gina}}\n[[Category:1968 births]]\n[[Category:Living people]]\n[[Category:APRA Award winners]]\n[[Category:Australian country singers]]\n[[Category:Australian women singers]]\n[[Category:Songbirds (group) members]]\n[[Category:Musicians from Queensland]]"}]}}}}
